## Copilot

Here are some common Python interview questions, grouped by topic:

## Basics
1. What are the key features of Python?
2. What is the difference between `list`, `tuple`, `set`, and `dict`?
3. What is the difference between `==` and `is`?
4. What is Python’s `*args` and `**kwargs`?
5. What are mutable and immutable types?
6. What is the difference between shallow copy and deep copy?

## Data Structures
7. How does a Python list work internally?
8. What is the difference between a list and a tuple?
9. When would you use a set?
10. How do dictionaries work in Python?
11. What is a generator?
12. What is the difference between an iterator and an iterable?

## Functions and Scope
13. What is the LEGB rule?
14. What are default argument pitfalls?
15. What is a lambda function?
16. What is a closure?
17. What are decorators?

## OOP
18. What is inheritance in Python?
19. What is polymorphism?
20. What is encapsulation?
21. What is method overriding?
22. What is the difference between `@staticmethod`, `@classmethod`, and instance methods?
23. What is multiple inheritance?

## Advanced Python
24. What is the Global Interpreter Lock (GIL)?
25. What is garbage collection in Python?
26. What are context managers?
27. What is the `with` statement used for?
28. What is monkey patching?
29. What are metaclasses?

## Concurrency
30. What is the difference between threading and multiprocessing?
31. When would you use async/await?
32. What is an event loop?

## Practical / Coding
33. How would you reverse a string in Python?
34. How do you remove duplicates from a list?
35. How do you find the most common element in a list?
36. How do you flatten a nested list?
37. How do you merge two dictionaries?

If you want, I can also provide:
- **answers** to these questions
- **beginner / intermediate / advanced** Python interview questions
- **Python coding interview questions with solutions**
- a **mock interview** format

Absolutely — for this Optum role, interviewers will likely focus on **Python + AI/LLM usage + practical data engineering** rather than pure ML theory.

## What they may ask on Python + LLM + AI

### Python basics they may still test
1. What are Python’s main features?
2. Difference between list, tuple, set, and dict?
3. What is the difference between `is` and `==`?
4. What are `*args` and `**kwargs`?
5. Explain mutable vs immutable types.
6. What is a generator?
7. What is the difference between an iterator and iterable?
8. What are decorators?
9. What is the difference between shallow copy and deep copy?
10. How do exception handling and logging work in Python?

### Python for data/automation
11. How do you read and process large flat files in Python efficiently?
12. How do you parse CSV/JSON files?
13. How do you handle missing or bad data in a file?
14. How do you use Python for ETL pipelines?
15. How do you connect Python to Snowflake?
16. How do you optimize Python code for performance?
17. How do you write reusable and maintainable Python modules?
18. How do you write unit tests in Python?
19. How do you manage dependencies and environments?

### LLM / AI-focused questions
20. What is an LLM?
21. How does a transformer work at a high level?
22. What is prompt engineering?
23. What is the difference between zero-shot, one-shot, and few-shot prompting?
24. How do you reduce hallucinations in LLM outputs?
25. What is RAG (Retrieval-Augmented Generation)?
26. When would you use RAG instead of fine-tuning?
27. What is the difference between fine-tuning and prompting?
28. What are embeddings?
29. What is a vector database?
30. How do you evaluate LLM responses?
31. What are temperature, top-p, and max tokens?
32. How do you handle sensitive or PHI data when using LLMs?
33. How do you make LLM outputs more reliable for enterprise use?
34. How do you monitor LLM quality in production?
35. How would you build a Python app that uses an LLM API?

### Practical AI + Python questions
36. Write Python code to call an LLM API and process the response.
37. How would you build a chatbot for internal support?
38. How would you summarize large documents using Python and an LLM?
39. How would you chunk large text before sending it to an LLM?
40. How would you store embeddings and retrieve relevant chunks?
41. How would you design a pipeline for document ingestion + RAG?
42. How would you secure API keys and secrets in Python apps?
43. How would you log LLM prompts and responses safely?
44. How would you validate JSON output from an LLM?
45. How do you handle prompt injection attacks?

### Enterprise / healthcare angle
46. How would you ensure compliance when using AI in healthcare?
47. How would you avoid exposing PHI to external models?
48. What controls would you add before sending data to an LLM?
49. How would you make AI outputs explainable to business users?
50. How would you use AI to improve data engineering productivity?

## Questions they may ask specifically for this job
Because this role mentions Snowflake, Airflow, CI/CD, and data engineering, they may combine Python with those topics:

- How have you used Python in ETL or orchestration?
- Have you used Python with Snowflake connectors or Snowpark?
- How would you automate a Snowflake data load using Python?
- How do you validate data after ingestion?
- How would you use Python to profile source data?
- How do you use AI tools safely to speed up coding or debugging?
- Have you used Python to build wrappers around APIs, Kafka, or CDC feeds?
- How would you implement an LLM-based data quality assistant?

## Strong answers they may expect
You should be ready to speak about:
- writing Python scripts for data processing
- handling files, APIs, and JSON
- using pandas for profiling
- building reusable functions and classes
- error handling and logging
- calling LLM APIs
- prompt design and output validation
- RAG basics
- AI safety, privacy, and governance
- using AI to improve productivity without compromising compliance

Sure — here are **Python interview questions from basic to beginner to advanced**, tailored a bit toward **data engineering + AI/LLM** roles.

## 1) Basic Python Questions
1. What is Python?
2. What are the key features of Python?
3. What is the difference between `list`, `tuple`, `set`, and `dict`?
4. What is the difference between `==` and `is`?
5. What are mutable and immutable objects?
6. What are `*args` and `**kwargs`?
7. What is indentation in Python, and why is it important?
8. What are Python’s built-in data types?
9. What is the difference between local and global variables?
10. What is the use of `if __name__ == "__main__"`?

## 2) Beginner Python Questions
1. What is a function in Python?
2. How do you write a loop in Python?
3. What is the difference between `for` and `while` loops?
4. What is a list comprehension?
5. What is the difference between `append()` and `extend()`?
6. How do you handle exceptions in Python?
7. What is the purpose of `try`, `except`, and `finally`?
8. What is a module in Python?
9. What is the difference between a module and a package?
10. How do you read and write files in Python?
11. What is slicing in Python?
12. How do you remove duplicates from a list?
13. What is a lambda function?
14. What is the difference between `copy()` and assignment?
15. What is a generator?

## 3) Intermediate / Beginner-Advanced Questions
1. What is the difference between an iterator and an iterable?
2. What is the LEGB rule?
3. What is a decorator?
4. What is a closure?
5. What are default arguments in Python, and what are the pitfalls?
6. What is shallow copy vs deep copy?
7. How does Python manage memory?
8. What is garbage collection?
9. What is the Global Interpreter Lock (GIL)?
10. How do you optimize Python code for performance?
11. What are comprehensions for list, dict, and set?
12. What is the difference between `map()`, `filter()`, and `reduce()`?
13. What is object-oriented programming in Python?
14. What are classes and objects?
15. What is inheritance?
16. What is polymorphism?
17. What is encapsulation?
18. What is method overriding?
19. What is the difference between instance, class, and static methods?
20. How do you use error handling in a production script?

## 4) Advanced Python Questions
1. What are metaclasses?
2. What is monkey patching?
3. How does Python’s memory management work internally?
4. What is the difference between threading and multiprocessing?
5. When would you use asyncio?
6. What is an event loop?
7. How do context managers work?
8. What happens behind the scenes when you use `with`?
9. How do you implement a custom iterator?
10. How do you implement a custom decorator?
11. How do you manage concurrency in Python?
12. What are coroutines?
13. How would you profile Python code?
14. How do you handle large files efficiently in Python?
15. How do you make Python code production-ready?
16. How do you structure a large Python project?
17. How do you write unit tests in Python?
18. What is mocking in tests?
19. How do you handle secrets and environment variables securely?
20. How do you ensure code quality in Python?

## 5) Python + Data Engineering Questions
1. How do you use Python in ETL pipelines?
2. How do you parse JSON and CSV files in Python?
3. How do you process large flat files efficiently?
4. How do you validate source data in Python?
5. How do you use pandas for profiling data?
6. How do you connect Python to Snowflake?
7. How do you load data into Snowflake using Python?
8. How do you handle bad records in a pipeline?
9. How do you log and monitor Python jobs?
10. How do you write idempotent ETL code?

## 6) Python + AI/LLM Questions

2. How do you call an LLM API in Python?

## Copilot

Here’s a practical **interview roadmap** for this Optum role, focused on **Python + Snowflake + AI/LLM + data engineering**.

## 1) Understand the role first
This job is mainly about:
- **Data engineering / support / operations**
- **Snowflake development**
- **Python scripting**
- **SQL-heavy problem solving**
- **Some AI/LLM exposure**
- **Process discipline**: incident management, batch monitoring, SLA, production support

So your prep should not be only Python theory — it should be:
- Python basics + scripting
- SQL
- Snowflake
- ETL/data pipelines
- LLM basics and practical usage
- Production support mindset

---

## 2) Roadmap by priority

### Phase 1: Core basics
Focus on these first:

#### Python
- data types
- lists, tuples, dicts, sets
- loops, conditionals
- functions
- file handling
- exception handling
- modules/packages
- OOP basics
- list comprehensions
- generators
- decorators basics

#### SQL
- SELECT, WHERE, GROUP BY, HAVING
- JOINs
- subqueries
- CTEs
- window functions
- aggregations
- case statements
- query optimization basics

#### Snowflake basics
- Snowflake architecture
- virtual warehouse
- stages
- SnowSQL
- Snowpipe
- tables/views
- file formats
- loading/unloading data
- streams/tasks basics
- credits and warehouse sizing

---

### Phase 2: Job-relevant Python
Learn Python specifically for data work:

- read CSV/JSON/flat files
- parse and validate records
- handle bad rows
- use pandas for profiling
- logging
- retry logic
- build scripts for data movement
- API calling using `requests`
- JSON normalization
- writing reusable utilities
- basic unit testing

---

### Phase 3: Snowflake + ETL
This is very important for this role.

- loading data into Snowflake
- handling semi-structured data
- using Snowpipe
- stored procedures
- JavaScript UDFs
- task scheduling
- debugging failed loads
- performance tuning
- query cost/credit awareness
- data migration patterns
- incremental vs full load

---

### Phase 4: AI / LLM basics
Since the job mentions AI usage, be ready for practical questions:

#### Learn:
- what is an LLM
- prompt engineering
- zero-shot / few-shot prompting
- embeddings
- RAG
- vector databases
- hallucinations
- evaluation of outputs
- token limits
- temperature / top-p
- safety and privacy

#### Be able to explain:
- how to use an LLM in Python
- how to summarize text
- how to classify or extract structured data
- how to validate LLM output
- how to avoid sending sensitive data
- how AI can improve productivity in data engineering

---

### Phase 5: Production support / operations
Because this role includes monitoring and war rooms, prepare for:

- batch job monitoring
- incident handling
- root cause analysis
- SLA compliance
- release/change management
- production debugging
- stakeholder communication
- prioritization under pressure

---

## 3) Suggested preparation order
If you have limited time, study in this order:

1. **SQL**
2. **Python basics**
3. **Snowflake**
4. **ETL/data pipelines**
5. **Python for file/API processing**
6. **LLM / AI basics**
7. **Production support scenarios**
8. **Mock interviews**

---

## 4) What interviewers may test
They may check if you can:
- write Python scripts for ETL/data processing
- debug data issues
- write SQL for complex business logic
- explain Snowflake concepts clearly
- talk about production support and monitoring
- explain how you would use AI safely and efficiently
- communicate well with stakeholders

---

## 5) Best way to answer in interview
Use this structure:

### For theory questions:
- define the concept
- give a simple example
- explain where you used it

### For scenario questions:
- clarify the problem
- explain your approach
- mention edge cases
- mention logging/testing/validation
- mention impact on production

### For AI/LLM questions:
- explain business use case
- explain how Python integrates
- explain safety/privacy controls
- explain validation of output
- explain performance/cost considerations

---

## 6) 7-day fast-track roadmap
If your interview is near, use this:

### Day 1
- Python basics
- data structures
- functions

### Day 2
- file handling
- exceptions
- generators
- decorators

### Day 3
- SQL basics
- joins
- window functions
- CTEs

### Day 4
- Snowflake basics
- loading/unloading
- Snowpipe
- warehouse/credits

### Day 5
- ETL with Python
- pandas
- APIs
- logging

### Day 6
- LLM basics
- prompt engineering
- RAG
- embeddings
- AI safety

### Day 7
- mock interview
- resume/project explanation
- production support scenarios

---

## 7) What to prepare from your experience
Have 2–3 project stories ready for:
- Python data processing
- Snowflake / ETL work
- a production issue you resolved
- a time you improved a process
- any AI/LLM tool or automation you used

Use the **STAR format**:
- Situation
- Task
- Action
- Result

---

## @brehman_uhg

with answer in easy language i can revise quickly 

## Copilot

Absolutely — here are **basic Python interview questions with easy, quick revision answers**.

## Basic Python Interview Questions with Answers

1. **What is Python?**  
   Python is a simple, high-level programming language used for web development, data analysis, automation, AI, and more.

2. **What are the key features of Python?**  
   Python is easy to read, simple to learn, open-source, portable, and supports many libraries.

3. **Is Python case-sensitive?**  
   Yes. `name` and `Name` are treated as different variables.

4. **What are the different data types in Python?**  
   Common types are `int`, `float`, `str`, `bool`, `list`, `tuple`, `set`, and `dict`.

5. **What is the difference between a list and a tuple?**  
   A list can be changed, but a tuple cannot be changed after creation.

6. **What is the difference between `==` and `is`?**  
   `==` checks value. `is` checks whether two variables point to the same object.

7. **What are mutable and immutable objects?**  
   Mutable objects can be changed, like lists. Immutable objects cannot be changed, like strings and tuples.

8. **What is indentation in Python?**  
   Indentation means spaces at the beginning of a line. Python uses it to define blocks of code.

9. **What are Python keywords?**  
   Keywords are reserved words like `if`, `else`, `for`, `while`, `def`, and `class`.

10. **What is the purpose of comments in Python?**  
    Comments explain code and are ignored by Python.

11. **How do you declare a variable in Python?**  
    You just assign a value, like `x = 10`.

12. **What is type casting in Python?**  
    It means converting one data type into another, like `int("5")`.

13. **What is the difference between `int()`, `float()`, and `str()`?**  
    `int()` converts to integer, `float()` converts to decimal, and `str()` converts to text.

14. **What is the use of `print()`?**  
    It displays output on the screen.

15. **What is the use of `input()`?**  
    It takes input from the user.

16. **What are operators in Python?**  
    Operators are symbols used for calculations or comparisons.

17. **What are arithmetic operators?**  
    They are `+`, `-`, `*`, `/`, `%`, `//`, and `**`.

18. **What are comparison operators?**  
    They compare values, like `==`, `!=`, `>`, `<`, `>=`, and `<=`.

19. **What are logical operators?**  
    They are `and`, `or`, and `not`.

20. **What are assignment operators?**  
    They assign values, like `=`, `+=`, `-=`, `*=`, etc.

21. **What are membership operators?**  
    They check if a value exists in a sequence. Examples: `in`, `not in`.

22. **What are identity operators?**  
    They check whether two variables refer to the same object. Examples: `is`, `is not`.

23. **What is the difference between `and` and `or`?**  
    `and` returns true only if both conditions are true. `or` returns true if at least one condition is true.

24. **What is the use of `if`, `elif`, and `else`?**  
    They are used for decision-making in code.

25. **What are loops in Python?**  
    Loops repeat a block of code again and again.

26. **What is the difference between `for` and `while` loops?**  
    `for` is used when you know how many times to repeat. `while` runs until a condition becomes false.

27. **What is the use of `break`, `continue`, and `pass`?**  
    `break` stops the loop. `continue` skips the current step. `pass` does nothing.

28. **What is a string in Python?**  
    A string is a sequence of characters written inside quotes.

29. **How do you access characters in a string?**  
    By using indexing, like `name[0]`.

30. **What is string slicing?**  
    It means getting part of a string, like `name[1:4]`.

31. **What are some common string methods?**  
    `lower()`, `upper()`, `strip()`, `replace()`, `split()`, and `join()`.

32. **What is a list in Python?**  
    A list is an ordered collection that can change.

33. **How do you add or remove elements from a list?**  
    Use `append()` to add, `remove()` or `pop()` to delete.

34. **What is a tuple?**  
    A tuple is an ordered collection that cannot be changed.

35. **What is a set?**  
    A set is an unordered collection of unique values.

36. **What is a dictionary?**  
    A dictionary stores data in key-value pairs.

37. **How do you access values in a dictionary?**  
    Use the key, like `student["name"]`.

38. **What is a function in Python?**  
    A function is a reusable block of code that performs a task.

39. **What are parameters and arguments?**  
    Parameters are variables in the function definition. Arguments are values passed when calling the function.

40. **What are `*args` and `**kwargs`?**  
    `*args` is used for multiple positional arguments. `**kwargs` is used for multiple keyword arguments.

41. **What is a module?**  
    A module is a Python file with functions, classes, or variables.

42. **What is a package?**  
    A package is a collection of modules.

43. **How do you import a module?**  
    Use the `import` keyword.

44. **What is exception handling?**  
    It is a way to handle errors without stopping the program.

45. **What are `try`, `except`, `else`, and `finally`?**  
    `try` contains risky code, `except` handles errors, `else` runs if no error happens, and `finally` runs always.

46. **What is a class in Python?**  
    A class is a blueprint for creating objects.

47. **What is an object?**  
    An object is an instance of a class.

48. **What is inheritance?**  
    Inheritance allows one class to use features of another class.

49. **What is a constructor?**  
    A constructor is a special method used when an object is created.

50. **What is the use of `self`?**  
    `self` refers to the current object inside a class.

## Copilot

Sure — here are the **basic Python interview questions with slightly bigger, easy-to-revise answers**.

## Basic Python Interview Questions with Answers

1. **What is Python?**  
   Python is a popular high-level programming language used for web development, automation, data analysis, machine learning, AI, and scripting. It is known for being simple, readable, and easy to learn.

2. **What are the key features of Python?**  
   Python has simple syntax, easy readability, large community support, many libraries, and works on different platforms. It is also interpreted and supports both procedural and object-oriented programming.

3. **Is Python case-sensitive?**  
   Yes, Python is case-sensitive. This means `name`, `Name`, and `NAME` are all treated as different variables.

4. **What are the different data types in Python?**  
   Python has several data types such as `int` for integers, `float` for decimal numbers, `str` for text, `bool` for true/false values, `list`, `tuple`, `set`, and `dict`. These are used depending on the kind of data you want to store.

5. **What is the difference between a list and a tuple?**  
   A list can be modified after creation, while a tuple cannot be changed. Lists are mutable, and tuples are immutable. Lists are usually used when data may change, and tuples when data should remain fixed.

6. **What is the difference between `==` and `is`?**  
   `==` checks whether two values are equal. `is` checks whether two variables point to the same object in memory. So `==` is about value, and `is` is about identity.

7. **What are mutable and immutable objects?**  
   Mutable objects can be changed after they are created, such as lists, dictionaries, and sets. Immutable objects cannot be changed, such as strings, tuples, and integers.

8. **What is indentation in Python?**  
   Indentation means spaces at the beginning of a line. In Python, indentation is very important because it defines code blocks like loops, conditions, and functions.

9. **What are Python keywords?**  
   Python keywords are reserved words with special meaning, like `if`, `else`, `for`, `while`, `def`, `class`, `return`, and `break`. We cannot use them as variable names.

10. **What is the purpose of comments in Python?**  
    Comments are used to explain the code. They make code easier to read and understand. Python ignores comments when running the program.

11. **How do you declare a variable in Python?**  
    In Python, you do not need to declare variable type separately. You simply assign a value, like `x = 10` or `name = "John"`.

12. **What is type casting in Python?**  
    Type casting means converting one data type into another. For example, `int("5")` converts a string into an integer, and `str(100)` converts a number into text.

13. **What is the difference between `int()`, `float()`, and `str()`?**  
    `int()` converts a value into an integer, `float()` converts it into a decimal number, and `str()` converts it into a string. These are commonly used when converting input or output values.

14. **What is the use of `print()`?**  
    `print()` is used to display output on the screen. It is one of the most common functions in Python and is often used for debugging and showing results.

15. **What is the use of `input()`?**  
    `input()` is used to take data from the user during program execution. The input is always taken as a string unless converted to another type.

16. **What are operators in Python?**  
    Operators are symbols used to perform operations on values or variables. They include arithmetic, comparison, logical, assignment, membership, and identity operators.

17. **What are arithmetic operators?**  
    Arithmetic operators are used for mathematical calculations. Examples are `+` for addition, `-` for subtraction, `*` for multiplication, `/` for division, `%` for remainder, `//` for floor division, and `**` for power.

18. **What are comparison operators?**  
    Comparison operators compare two values and return `True` or `False`. Examples include `==`, `!=`, `>`, `<`, `>=`, and `<=`.

19. **What are logical operators?**  
    Logical operators are used to combine conditions. `and` returns `True` only if both conditions are true, `or` returns `True` if one condition is true, and `not` reverses the result.

20. **What are assignment operators?**  
    Assignment operators are used to assign values to variables. The basic one is `=`, and others like `+=`, `-=`, `*=`, and `/=` are used for shortcut operations.

21. **What are membership operators?**  
    Membership operators check whether a value is present in a sequence like a list, string, or tuple. `in` checks presence, and `not in` checks absence.

22. **What are identity operators?**  
    Identity operators check whether two variables refer to the same memory location. `is` means same object, and `is not` means different object.

23. **What is the difference between `and` and `or`?**  
    `and` gives `True` only when both conditions are true. `or` gives `True` if at least one condition is true. They are used in decision-making.

24. **What is the use of `if`, `elif`, and `else`?**  
    These are used for conditional statements. `if` checks the first condition, `elif` checks another condition if the first one is false, and `else` runs when none of the conditions are true.

25. **What are loops in Python?**  
    Loops are used to repeat a block of code multiple times. Python mainly uses `for` and `while` loops.

26. **What is the difference between `for` and `while` loops?**  
    A `for` loop is used when the number of iterations is known or when iterating over items. A `while` loop keeps running until a condition becomes false.

27. **What is the use of `break`, `continue`, and `pass`?**  
    `break` stops the loop completely, `continue` skips the current iteration and moves to the next one, and `pass` is used when no action is needed but syntax requires a statement.

28. **What is a string in Python?**  
    A string is a sequence of characters written inside single, double, or triple quotes. Strings are used to store text.

29. **How do you access characters in a string?**  
    You use indexing. For example, `name[0]` gives the first character of the string.

30. **What is string slicing?**  
    String slicing means extracting part of a string using positions. For example, `name[1:4]` gives characters from index 1 to 3.

31. **What are some common string methods?**  
    Common string methods include `lower()`, `upper()`, `strip()`, `replace()`, `split()`, and `join()`. These help manipulate text easily.

32. **What is a list in Python?**  
    A list is an ordered collection of items that can be changed. It can store different types of data, and items are written inside square brackets.

33. **How do you add or remove elements from a list?**  
    You can add items using `append()` or `insert()`. To remove items, you can use `remove()`, `pop()`, or `del`.

34. **What is a tuple?**  
    A tuple is an ordered collection like a list, but it cannot be modified after creation. It is written inside parentheses.

35. **What is a set?**  
    A set is an unordered collection of unique values. It is useful when you want to store only distinct items.

36. **What is a dictionary?**  
    A dictionary stores data in key-value pairs. It is useful when you want to access data using a key instead of a position.

37. **How do you access values in a dictionary?**  
    You access dictionary values using the key. For example, `student["name"]` returns the value stored for the key `name`.

38. **What is a function in Python?**  
    A function is a reusable block of code that performs a specific task. Functions help make code organized and avoid repetition.

39. **What are parameters and arguments?**  
    Parameters are variables written in the function definition. Arguments are the actual values passed when the function is called.

40. **What are `*args` and `**kwargs`?**  
    `*args` is used to pass multiple positional arguments to a function. `**kwargs` is used to pass multiple keyword arguments as key-value pairs.

41. **What is a module?**  
    A module is a Python file that contains code such as functions, classes, or variables. It helps organize code into reusable parts.

42. **What is a package?**  
    A package is a collection of modules organized in folders. It helps group related Python files together.

43. **How do you import a module?**  
    You can import a module using the `import` keyword. For example, `import math` loads the math module.

44. **What is exception handling?**  
    Exception handling is used to handle errors so the program does not crash suddenly. It helps make programs more stable.

45. **What are `try`, `except`, `else`, and `finally`?**  
    `try` contains code that may raise an error. `except` handles the error. `else` runs if no error occurs. `finally` always runs, whether there is an error or not.

46. **What is a class in Python?**  
    A class is a blueprint for creating objects. It defines the properties and behaviors of objects.

47. **What is an object?**  
    An object is an instance of a class. It contains real values based on the class definition.

48. **What is inheritance?**  
    Inheritance allows one class to use the properties and methods of another class. It helps reduce code duplication and supports reuse.

49. **What is a constructor?**  
    A constructor is a special method that runs automatically when an object is created. It is usually used to initialize values.

50. **What is the use of `self`?**  
    `self` refers to the current object inside a class. It is used to access variables and methods belonging to that object.

If you want, I can now make the **next set: beginner Python interview questions with answers** in the same easy revision style.

## 1. What is Python?
Python is a simple and popular programming language used for web apps, automation, data analysis, AI, and many other things.

```python
print("Hello, Python")
```

---

## 2. What are the key features of Python?
Python is easy to read, easy to write, supports many libraries, and works on different platforms.

```python
# Example of simple Python code
name = "Alice"
age = 25
print(name, age)
```

---

## 3. Is Python case-sensitive?
Yes, Python is case-sensitive. `name` and `Name` are treated as different variables.

```python
name = "John"
Name = "Mike"
print(name)
print(Name)
```

---

## 4. What are the different data types in Python?
Python has data types like `int`, `float`, `str`, `bool`, `list`, `tuple`, `set`, and `dict`.

```python
x = 10
y = 10.5
z = "Hello"
a = True

print(type(x))
print(type(y))
print(type(z))
print(type(a))
```

---

## 5. What is the difference between a list and a tuple?
A list can be changed, but a tuple cannot be changed after creation.

```python
my_list = [1, 2, 3]
my_list.append(4)
print(my_list)

my_tuple = (1, 2, 3)
print(my_tuple)
```

---

## 6. What is the difference between `==` and `is`?
`==` checks value equality. `is` checks whether two variables are the same object in memory.

```python
a = [1, 2]
b = [1, 2]
c = a

print(a == b)   # True
print(a is b)   # False
print(a is c)   # True
```

---

## 7. What are mutable and immutable objects?
Mutable objects can be changed after creation. Immutable objects cannot be changed.

```python
# Mutable
lst = [1, 2, 3]
lst[0] = 100
print(lst)

# Immutable
text = "hello"
# text[0] = "H"   # This will give an error
```

---

## 8. What is indentation in Python?
Indentation means spaces at the start of a line. Python uses it to define code blocks.

```python
if True:
    print("This is indented")
```

---

## 9. What are Python keywords?
Keywords are reserved words in Python like `if`, `else`, `for`, `while`, `def`, and `class`.

```python
# Example use of keywords
if 5 > 2:
    print("Five is greater")
```

---

## 10. What is the purpose of comments in Python?
Comments are used to explain code. Python ignores them while running.

```python
# This is a comment
print("Comments are helpful")
```

---

## 11. How do you declare a variable in Python?
You declare a variable by assigning a value directly.

```python
name = "John"
age = 30
print(name, age)
```

---

## 12. What is type casting in Python?
Type casting means converting one data type into another.

```python
num_str = "10"
num_int = int(num_str)

print(num_int)
print(type(num_int))
```

---

## 13. What is the use of `print()`?
`print()` displays output on the screen.

```python
print("Hello World")
```

---

## 14. What is the use of `input()`?
`input()` takes input from the user.

```python
name = input("Enter your name: ")
print("Hello", name)
```

---

## 15. What are operators in Python?
Operators are symbols used to perform operations like math, comparison, and logic.

```python
a = 10
b = 5
print(a + b)
print(a > b)
print(a and b)
```

---

## 16. What are arithmetic operators?
These are used for math operations.

```python
a = 10
b = 3

print(a + b)   # addition
print(a - b)   # subtraction
print(a * b)   # multiplication
print(a / b)   # division
print(a % b)   # remainder
print(a // b)  # floor division
print(a ** b)  # power
```

---

## 17. What are comparison operators?
These compare two values and return `True` or `False`.

```python
a = 10
b = 20

print(a == b)
print(a != b)
print(a > b)
print(a < b)
```

---

## 18. What are logical operators?
Logical operators combine conditions.

```python
x = 10
y = 20

print(x > 5 and y > 10)
print(x > 15 or y > 10)
print(not(x > 5))
```

---

## 19. What is the use of `if`, `elif`, and `else`?
They are used for decision-making.

```python
marks = 75

if marks >= 90:
    print("Excellent")
elif marks >= 60:
    print("Good")
else:
    print("Need improvement")
```

---

## 20. What are loops in Python?
Loops repeat a block of code.

```python
for i in range(3):
    print(i)
```

---

## 21. What is the difference between `for` and `while` loops?
`for` is used when the number of iterations is known. `while` runs until a condition becomes false.

```python
# for loop
for i in range(3):
    print(i)

# while loop
x = 0
while x < 3:
    print(x)
    x += 1
```

---

## 22. What is the use of `break`, `continue`, and `pass`?
`break` stops the loop, `continue` skips one loop step, and `pass` means do nothing.

```python
for i in range(5):
    if i == 3:
        break
    print(i)

for i in range(5):
    if i == 3:
        continue
    print(i)

if True:
    pass
```

---

## 23. What is a string in Python?
A string is text written inside quotes.

```python
text = "Hello Python"
print(text)
```

---

## 24. How do you access characters in a string?
You use indexing.

```python
text = "Python"
print(text[0])
print(text[1])
```

---

## 25. What is string slicing?
It means taking a part of a string.

```python
text = "Python"
print(text[0:3])
print(text[2:])
```

---

## 26. What are common string methods?
Some common methods are `lower()`, `upper()`, `strip()`, `replace()`, and `split()`.

```python
text = "  Hello World  "
print(text.lower())
print(text.upper())
print(text.strip())
print(text.replace("World", "Python"))
print(text.split())
```

---

## 27. What is a list in Python?
A list is an ordered collection that can be changed.

```python
my_list = [10, 20, 30]
print(my_list)
```

---

## 28. How do you add or remove elements from a list?
Use `append()` to add and `remove()` or `pop()` to delete.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.append(4)
print(nums)

nums.remove(2)
print(nums)

nums.pop()
print(nums)
```

---

## 29. What is a tuple?
A tuple is like a list, but it cannot be changed.

```python
my_tuple = (1, 2, 3)
print(my_tuple)
```

---

## 30. What is a set?
A set stores unique values only.

```python
my_set = {1, 2, 2, 3}
print(my_set)
```

---

## 31. What is a dictionary?
A dictionary stores data in key-value form.

```python
student = {"name": "John", "age": 25}
print(student)
print(student["name"])
```

---

## 32. What is a function in Python?
A function is a reusable block of code.

```python
def greet():
    print("Hello")

greet()
```

---

## 33. What are parameters and arguments?
Parameters are variables in the function definition. Arguments are values passed to the function.

```python
def greet(name):
    print("Hello", name)

greet("Alice")
```

---

## 34. What are `*args` and `**kwargs`?
`*args` is used for many positional arguments. `**kwargs` is used for many keyword arguments.

```python
def test(*args):
    print(args)

test(1, 2, 3)

def test2(**kwargs):
    print(kwargs)

test2(name="John", age=25)
```

---

## 35. What is a module?
A module is a Python file containing code like functions or variables.

```python
import math
print(math.sqrt(16))
```

---

## 36. What is a package?
A package is a collection of modules.

```python
# Example idea:
# mypackage/
#   __init__.py
#   module1.py
#   module2.py
```

---

## 37. What is exception handling?
It is used to handle errors safely.

```python
try:
    x = 10 / 0
except ZeroDivisionError:
    print("Cannot divide by zero")
```

---

## 38. What are `try`, `except`, `else`, and `finally`?
`try` checks risky code, `except` handles errors, `else` runs if no error, and `finally` always runs.

```python
try:
    x = 10 / 2
except ZeroDivisionError:
    print("Error")
else:
    print("No error")
finally:
    print("Done")
```

---

## 39. What is a class in Python?
A class is a blueprint for creating objects.

```python
class Car:
    pass
```

---

## 40. What is an object?
An object is an instance of a class.

```python
class Car:
    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name

car1 = Car("BMW")
print(car1.name)
```

---

## 41. What is inheritance?
Inheritance lets one class use another class’s properties and methods.

```python
class Animal:
    def sound(self):
        print("Animal sound")

class Dog(Animal):
    pass

d = Dog()
d.sound()
```

---

## 42. What is a constructor?
A constructor is a special method used to initialize object values.

```python
class Person:
    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name

p = Person("John")
print(p.name)
```

---

## 43. What is the use of `self`?
`self` refers to the current object inside a class.

```python
class Student:
    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name

s = Student("Amit")
print(s.name)
```

```text
Aman
Rahul
```

```python
print(a == b)
print(a is b)
```

```text

False
```

```python
    print(i)
```

```text
1
2
```

## 20. `continue`
**Answer:** Skips current iteration.

```python
for i in range(5):
    if i == 2:
        continue
    print(i)
```

**Output:**
```text

1
3
4
```

## 21. `pass`
**Answer:** Does nothing.

```python
for i in range(3):
    pass
print("Loop completed")
```

```text

```


**Output:**
```text
yth
```

---

## 25. Common string methods
**Answer:** Used to modify strings.

```python
s = "  hello python  "
print(s.strip())
print(s.upper())
print(s.replace("python", "world"))
```

**Output:**
```text
hello python
  HELLO PYTHON  
  hello world  
```

---

## 26. List
**Answer:** Ordered and changeable collection.

```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
print(a)
```

**Output:**
```text
[1, 2, 3]
```

---

## 27. Add/remove items in list
**Answer:** Use `append()`, `remove()`, `pop()`.

```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
a.append(4)
print(a)
a.remove(2)
print(a)
```

**Output:**
```text
[1, 2, 3, 4]
[1, 3, 4]
```

---

## 28. Tuple
**Answer:** Ordered but not changeable.

```python
t = (1, 2, 3)
print(t)
```

**Output:**
```text
(1, 2, 3)
```

---

## 29. Set
**Answer:** Unordered collection of unique items.

```python
s = {1, 2, 2, 3}
print(s)
```

**Output:**
```text
{1, 2, 3}
```

---

## 30. Dictionary
**Answer:** Stores data as key-value pairs.

```python
d = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
print(d["name"])
```

**Output:**
```text
Aman
```

---

## 31. Function
**Answer:** Reusable block of code.

```python
def greet():
    print("Hello")

greet()
```

**Output:**
```text
Hello
```

---

## 32. Parameters and arguments
**Answer:** Parameters are in function definition, arguments are values passed.

```python
def add(a, b):
    print(a + b)

add(2, 3)
```

**Output:**
```text
5
```

---

## 33. `*args`
**Answer:** Used to pass multiple values.

```python
def my_func(*args):
    print(args)

my_func(1, 2, 3)
```

**Output:**
```text
(1, 2, 3)
```

---

## 34. `**kwargs`
**Answer:** Used to pass key-value pairs.

```python
def my_func(**kwargs):
    print(kwargs)

my_func(name="Aman", age=25)
```

**Output:**
```text
{'name': 'Aman', 'age': 25}
```

---

## 35. Module
**Answer:** A Python file with code.

```python
import math
print(math.sqrt(16))
```

**Output:**
```text
4.0
```

---

## 36. Exception handling
**Answer:** Handles errors safely.

```python
try:
    print(10 / 0)
except ZeroDivisionError:
    print("Cannot divide by zero")
```

**Output:**
```text
Cannot divide by zero
```

---

## 37. `try`, `except`, `else`, `finally`
**Answer:** Used for error handling.

```python
try:
    x = 10
    print(x)
except:
    print("Error")
else:
    print("No error")
finally:
    print("Done")
```

**Output:**
```text
10
No error
Done
```

---

## 38. Class
**Answer:** Blueprint for creating objects.

```python
class Car:
    pass

print(Car())
```

**Output:**
```text
<__main__.Car object at ...>
```

---

## 39. Object
**Answer:** An instance of a class.

```python
class Car:
    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name

c = Car("BMW")
print(c.name)
```

**Output:**
```text
BMW
```

---

## 40. Inheritance
**Answer:** One class can use another class’s features.

```python
class Animal:
    def sound(self):
        print("Animal sound")

class Dog(Animal):
    pass

d = Dog()
d.sound()
```

**Output:**
```text
Animal sound
```

---

## 41. Constructor
**Answer:** Runs automatically when object is created.

```python
class Person:
    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name

p = Person("Aman")
print(p.name)
```

**Output:**
```text
Aman
```

---

## 42. `self`
**Answer:** Refers to the current object.

```python
class Person:
    def say_hi(self):
        print("Hi")

p = Person()
p.say_hi()
```

**Output:**
```text
Hi
```

# 1) Python Introduction

## What is Python?
Python is a high-level programming language.  
It is easy to read and write, so beginners can learn it quickly.  
It is used in web development, data analysis, automation, AI, machine learning, and data engineering.

## Why Python is popular?
- simple syntax
- easy to learn
- large community
- many useful libraries
- used in many fields

## Simple code
```python
print("Hello, Python")
```

## Output
```text
Hello, Python
```

---

# 2) Variables in Python

## What is a variable?
A variable is a name that stores data.  
You can think of it like a box where you keep a value.

### Example
```python
name = "Aman"
age = 25
print(name)
print(age)
```

### Output
```text
Aman
25
```

## Uses of variables
- store values
- use them later in code
- make code readable

## Important point
In Python, you do not need to declare the type separately.

```python
x = 10
y = "Hello"
z = 3.5
```

---

# 3) Data Types in Python

## Common data types
- `int` → whole number
- `float` → decimal number
- `str` → text
- `bool` → True/False
- `list` → ordered, changeable collection
- `tuple` → ordered, unchangeable collection
- `set` → unordered unique collection
- `dict` → key-value collection

### Example
```python
a = 10
b = 10.5
c = "Python"
d = True

print(type(a))
print(type(b))
print(type(c))
print(type(d))
```

### Output
```text
<class 'int'>
<class 'float'>
<class 'str'>
<class 'bool'>
```

---

# 4) List in Python

## Definition
A list is an ordered collection of items.  
It is **mutable**, which means we can change it after creating it.  
A list can store multiple values, and those values can be of different types.

## Use of list
- when you want to store multiple values
- when values may change
- when order matters

## Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
print(fruits)
```

## Output
```text
['apple', 'banana', 'mango']
```

---

## Common list methods with use, code, output

### 1. `append()`
**Use:** Adds one item at the end.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.append(4)
print(nums)
```

**Output**
```text
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

### 2. `insert()`
**Use:** Adds item at a specific position.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 4]
nums.insert(2, 3)
print(nums)
```

**Output**
```text
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

### 3. `extend()`
**Use:** Adds multiple items at the end.

```python
a = [1, 2]
b = [3, 4]
a.extend(b)
print(a)
```

**Output**
```text
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

### 4. `remove()`
**Use:** Removes first matching value.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3, 2]
nums.remove(2)
print(nums)
```

**Output**
```text
[1, 3, 2]
```

---

### 5. `pop()`
**Use:** Removes item by index. If no index is given, removes last item.

```python
nums = [10, 20, 30]
x = nums.pop()
print(nums)
print(x)
```

**Output**
```text
[10, 20]
30
```

---

### 6. `clear()`
**Use:** Removes all items.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.clear()
print(nums)
```

**Output**
```text
[]
```

---

### 7. `index()`
**Use:** Finds position of a value.

```python
nums = [10, 20, 30]
print(nums.index(20))
```

**Output**
```text
1
```

---

### 8. `count()`
**Use:** Counts how many times a value appears.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 2, 3]
print(nums.count(2))
```

**Output**
```text
2
```

---

### 9. `sort()`
**Use:** Sorts list in ascending order.

```python
nums = [3, 1, 2]
nums.sort()
print(nums)
```

**Output**
```text
[1, 2, 3]
```

---

### 10. `reverse()`
**Use:** Reverses the list order.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.reverse()
print(nums)
```

**Output**
```text
[3, 2, 1]
```

---

### 11. `copy()`
**Use:** Creates a new copy of the list.

```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
b = a.copy()
print(b)
```

**Output**
```text
[1, 2, 3]
```

---

## Interview point for list
A list is one of the most used data structures because it is flexible and easy to modify.

---

# 5) Tuple in Python

## Definition
A tuple is an ordered collection of items, but it is **immutable**, meaning we cannot change it after creation.

## Use of tuple
- when data should not change
- for fixed values
- faster than list in some cases

## Example
```python
colors = ("red", "green", "blue")
print(colors)
```

## Output
```text
('red', 'green', 'blue')
```

---

## Tuple methods

### 1. `count()`
**Use:** Counts occurrences of a value.

```python
t = (1, 2, 2, 3)
print(t.count(2))
```

**Output**
```text
2
```

### 2. `index()`
**Use:** Returns first position of a value.

```python
t = (10, 20, 30)
print(t.index(20))
```

**Output**
```text
1
```

---

## Important tuple point
Tuple has only 2 main methods because it cannot be changed.

---

# 6) Set in Python

## Definition
A set is an unordered collection of unique items.  
Duplicate values are not allowed.

## Use of set
- to store unique values
- to remove duplicates
- to perform mathematical operations like union and intersection

## Example
```python
s = {1, 2, 2, 3}
print(s)
```

## Output
```text
{1, 2, 3}
```

---

## Common set methods

### 1. `add()`
**Use:** Adds one item.

```python
s = {1, 2}
s.add(3)
print(s)
```

**Output**
```text
{1, 2, 3}
```

---

### 2. `update()`
**Use:** Adds multiple items.

```python
s = {1, 2}
s.update([3, 4])
print(s)
```

**Output**
```text
{1, 2, 3, 4}
```

---

### 3. `remove()`
**Use:** Removes item, error if not found.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.remove(2)
print(s)
```

**Output**
```text
{1, 3}
```

---

### 4. `discard()`
**Use:** Removes item, no error if not found.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.discard(4)
print(s)
```

**Output**
```text
{1, 2, 3}
```

---

### 5. `pop()`
**Use:** Removes a random item.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
x = s.pop()
print(x)
print(s)
```

**Output**
```text
2
{1, 3}
```

---

### 6. `clear()`
**Use:** Removes all items.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.clear()
print(s)
```

**Output**
```text
set()
```

---

## Set operations
- union
- intersection
- difference

### Example
```python
a = {1, 2, 3}
b = {3, 4, 5}
print(a | b)
print(a & b)
print(a - b)
```

### Output
```text
{1, 2, 3, 4, 5}
{3}
{1, 2}
```

---

# 7) Dictionary in Python

## Definition
A dictionary stores data in **key-value pairs**.  
Keys are unique. Values can repeat.

## Use of dictionary
- when data is stored with labels
- when quick lookup is needed
- for structured information

## Example
```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
print(student)
```

## Output
```text
{'name': 'Aman', 'age': 25}
```

---

## Common dictionary methods

### 1. `get()`
**Use:** Gets value by key safely.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
print(student.get("name"))
```

**Output**
```text
Aman
```

---

### 2. `keys()`
**Use:** Returns all keys.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
print(student.keys())
```

**Output**
```text
dict_keys(['name', 'age'])
```

---

### 3. `values()`
**Use:** Returns all values.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
print(student.values())
```

**Output**
```text
dict_values(['Aman', 25])
```

---

### 4. `items()`
**Use:** Returns key-value pairs.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
print(student.items())
```

**Output**
```text
dict_items([('name', 'Aman'), ('age', 25)])
```

---

### 5. `update()`
**Use:** Adds or updates values.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman"}
student.update({"age": 25})
print(student)
```

**Output**
```text
{'name': 'Aman', 'age': 25}
```

---

### 6. `pop()`
**Use:** Removes a key and returns its value.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
x = student.pop("age")
print(x)
print(student)
```

**Output**
```text
25
{'name': 'Aman'}
```

---

### 7. `clear()`
**Use:** Removes all items.

```python
student = {"name": "Aman", "age": 25}
student.clear()
print(student)
```

**Output**
```text
{}
```

---

## Interview point for dictionary
Dictionary is very important because it gives fast access using keys.

# 3) What are the basic data types in Python?

Common basic data types are:

- `int` → whole numbers
- `float` → decimal numbers
- `str` → text
- `bool` → True/False
- `list` → ordered, changeable collection
- `tuple` → ordered, unchangeable collection
- `set` → unordered collection of unique values
- `dict` → key-value pairs

```python
a = 10
b = 10.5
c = "Python"
```

# 4) What is the difference between list, tuple, set, and dict?

## List
A **list** is an ordered collection that can be changed.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'banana', 'mango']
```

## Tuple
A **tuple** is an ordered collection that cannot be changed.

### Example
```python
fruits = ("apple", "banana", "mango")
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
('apple', 'banana', 'mango')
```

## Set
A **set** stores unique values only.

### Example
```python
numbers = {1, 2, 3, 3, 4}
print(numbers)
```

### Output
```python
{1, 2, 3, 4}
```

## Dict
A **dictionary** stores data in key-value form.

### Example
```python
person = {"name": "Rahul", "age": 25}
print(person)
```

### Output
```python
{'name': 'Rahul', 'age': 25}
```

---

# 5) List in Python

A **list** is one of the most used data structures in Python.  
It is:
- ordered
- changeable
- allows duplicate values

### Example
```python
numbers = [10, 20, 30, 40]
print(numbers)
```

### Output
```python
[10, 20, 30, 40]
```

---

## List methods with uses, explanation, code, and output

---

### 1. `append()`
Adds one item at the end of the list.

### Use
When you want to add a single new item.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana"]
fruits.append("mango")
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'banana', 'mango']
```

---

### 2. `extend()`
Adds multiple items from another list.

### Use
When you want to add many items at once.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana"]
fruits.extend(["mango", "grapes"])
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'banana', 'mango', 'grapes']
```

---

### 3. `insert()`
Adds an item at a specific position.

### Use
When you want to place an item in the middle.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "mango"]
fruits.insert(1, "banana")
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'banana', 'mango']
```

---

### 4. `remove()`
Removes the first matching value.

### Use
When you know the item value you want to delete.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
fruits.remove("banana")
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'mango']
```

---

### 5. `pop()`
Removes and returns an item by index.  
If no index is given, it removes the last item.

### Use
When you want to get and delete an item.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
item = fruits.pop()
print(item)
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
mango
['apple', 'banana']
```

---

### 6. `clear()`
Removes all items from the list.

### Use
When you want to empty the list.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana"]
fruits.clear()
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
[]
```

---

### 7. `index()`
Returns the position of a value.

### Use
When you want to know where an item is.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
print(fruits.index("banana"))
```

### Output
```python
1
```

---

### 8. `count()`
Returns how many times a value appears.

### Use
When you want to count a repeated item.

### Example
```python
nums = [1, 2, 2, 3, 2]
print(nums.count(2))
```

### Output
```python
3
```

---

### 9. `sort()`
Sorts the list in ascending order.

### Use
When you want ordered values.

### Example
```python
nums = [4, 1, 3, 2]
nums.sort()
print(nums)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

### 10. `reverse()`
Reverses the order of list items.

### Use
When you want the opposite order.

### Example
```python
nums = [1, 2, 3, 4]
nums.reverse()
print(nums)
```

### Output
```python
[4, 3, 2, 1]
```

---

### 11. `copy()`
Creates a shallow copy of the list.

### Use
When you want a new list with same values.

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
b = a.copy()
print(b)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3]
```

---

# 6) Tuple in Python

A **tuple** is:
- ordered
- immutable
- allows duplicate values

It is used when you do not want data to change.

### Example
```python
colors = ("red", "green", "blue")
print(colors)
```

### Output
```python
('red', 'green', 'blue')
```

---

## Tuple methods

Tuple has only **2 main methods**:

### 1. `count()`
Counts how many times a value appears.

### Example
```python
nums = (1, 2, 2, 3)
print(nums.count(2))
```

### Output
```python
2
```

### 2. `index()`
Returns the first position of a value.

### Example
```python
nums = (10, 20, 30)
print(nums.index(20))
```

### Output
```python
1
```

---

# 7) Set in Python

A **set**:
- is unordered
- does not allow duplicates
- is mutable
- is useful for unique values

### Example
```python
nums = {1, 2, 3, 3, 4}
print(nums)
```

### Output
```python
{1, 2, 3, 4}
```

---

## Set methods

### 1. `add()`
Adds one item.

```python
s = {1, 2}
s.add(3)
print(s)
```

Output:
```python
{1, 2, 3}
```

### 2. `update()`
Adds multiple items.

```python
s = {1, 2}
s.update([3, 4])
print(s)
```

Output:
```python
{1, 2, 3, 4}
```

### 3. `remove()`
Removes item, gives error if not found.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.remove(2)
print(s)
```

Output:
```python
{1, 3}
```

### 4. `discard()`
Removes item, no error if not found.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.discard(5)
print(s)
```

Output:
```python
{1, 2, 3}
```

### 5. `pop()`
Removes one random item.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
x = s.pop()
print(x)
print(s)
```

Output will vary because set is unordered.

### 6. `clear()`
Removes all items.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.clear()
print(s)
```

Output:
```python
set()
```

---

# 8) Dictionary in Python

A **dictionary** stores data as:
- key : value

It is:
- unordered
- changeable
- keys must be unique

### Example
```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22, "city": "Delhi"}
print(student)
```

### Output
```python
{'name': 'Amit', 'age': 22, 'city': 'Delhi'}
```

---

## Dictionary methods

### 1. `keys()`
Returns all keys.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
print(student.keys())
```

Output:
```python
dict_keys(['name', 'age'])
```

### 2. `values()`
Returns all values.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
print(student.values())
```

Output:
```python
dict_values(['Amit', 22])
```

### 3. `items()`
Returns key-value pairs.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
print(student.items())
```

Output:
```python
dict_items([('name', 'Amit'), ('age', 22)])
```

### 4. `get()`
Returns value for a key safely.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
print(student.get("name"))
```

Output:
```python
Amit
```

### 5. `update()`
Adds or changes key-value pairs.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
student.update({"city": "Delhi"})
print(student)
```

Output:
```python
{'name': 'Amit', 'age': 22, 'city': 'Delhi'}
```

### 6. `pop()`
Removes a key and returns its value.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
x = student.pop("age")
print(x)
print(student)
```

Output:
```python
22
{'name': 'Amit'}
```

### 7. `popitem()`
Removes the last inserted item.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
x = student.popitem()
print(x)
print(student)
```

Output:
```python
('age', 22)
{'name': 'Amit'}
```

### 8. `clear()`
Removes all items.

```python
student = {"name": "Amit", "age": 22}
student.clear()
print(student)
```

Output:
```python
{}
```

---

# 9) Difference between `append()` and `extend()`

- `append()` adds **one item**
- `extend()` adds **many items**

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2]
a.append([3, 4])
print(a)

b = [1, 2]
b.extend([3, 4])
print(b)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, [3, 4]]
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

# 10) What is the difference between `remove()` and `pop()`?

- `remove()` deletes by **value**
- `pop()` deletes by **index**

### Example
```python
nums = [10, 20, 30, 40]
nums.remove(20)
print(nums)

nums2 = [10, 20, 30, 40]
x = nums2.pop(1)
print(x)
print(nums2)
```

### Output
```python
[10, 30, 40]
20
[10, 30, 40]
```

# 1) What is a function in Python?

A **function** is a reusable block of code.  
You write code once and use it many times.

### Why use it?
- reduces repetition
- makes code clean
- easier to debug

### Example
```python
def greet():
    print("Hello, welcome to Python!")

greet()
```

### Output
```python
Hello, welcome to Python!
```

---

# 2) How do you pass arguments to a function?

Arguments are values sent to a function.

### Example
```python
def greet(name):
    print("Hello", name)

greet("Rahul")
```

### Output
```python
Hello Rahul
```

---

# 3) What is the difference between parameter and argument?

- **Parameter** = variable written in function definition
- **Argument** = actual value passed while calling the function

### Example
```python
def greet(name):   # name is parameter
    print("Hello", name)

greet("Amit")      # Amit is argument
```

### Output
```python
Hello Amit
```

---

# 4) What is the difference between `for` and `while` loop?

## `for` loop
Used when you know how many times you want to repeat.

### Example
```python
for i in range(3):
    print(i)
```

### Output
```python
0
1
2
```

## `while` loop
Used when you want to repeat until a condition becomes false.

### Example
```python
i = 0
while i < 3:
    print(i)
    i += 1
```

### Output
```python
0
1
2
```

---

# 5) What is a list comprehension?

List comprehension is a short way to create a list.

### Example
```python
nums = [x*x for x in range(5)]
print(nums)
```

### Output
```python
[0, 1, 4, 9, 16]
```

### Use
It makes code shorter and cleaner.

---

# 6) How do you remove duplicates from a list?

You can use a `set`, because set stores unique values only.

### Example
```python
nums = [1, 2, 2, 3, 4, 4]
unique_nums = list(set(nums))
print(unique_nums)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

Note: order may change because set is unordered.

---

# 7) What is a string in Python?

A string is text written inside quotes.

### Example
```python
name = "Python"
print(name)
```

### Output
```python
Python
```

---

## String methods

### 1. `lower()`
Converts text to lowercase.

```python
text = "HELLO"
print(text.lower())
```

Output:
```python
hello
```

### 2. `upper()`
Converts text to uppercase.

```python
text = "hello"
print(text.upper())
```

Output:
```python
HELLO
```

### 3. `strip()`
Removes extra spaces from beginning and end.

```python
text = "  Python  "
print(text.strip())
```

Output:
```python
Python
```

### 4. `replace()`
Replaces one word or character with another.

```python
text = "I like Java"
print(text.replace("Java", "Python"))
```

Output:
```python
I like Python
```

### 5. `split()`
Splits a string into a list.

```python
text = "a,b,c"
print(text.split(","))
```

Output:
```python
['a', 'b', 'c']
```

### 6. `join()`
Joins items into one string.

```python
words = ["I", "love", "Python"]
print(" ".join(words))
```

Output:
```python
I love Python
```

---

# 8) What is slicing in Python?

Slicing means taking a part of a string, list, or tuple.

### Syntax
```python
[start : end : step]
```

### Example
```python
text = "Python"
print(text[0:3])
print(text[1:5])
print(text[::-1])
```

### Output
```python
Pyt
ytho
nohtyP
```

---

# 9) What is the difference between `append()` and `insert()`?

- `append()` adds item at the end
- `insert()` adds item at a specific position

### Example
```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.append(4)
print(nums)

nums.insert(1, 10)
print(nums)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
[1, 10, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

# 10) What is a module in Python?

A module is a Python file containing code like functions, variables, or classes.

### Example
```python
import math
print(math.sqrt(16))
```

### Output
```python
4.0
```

---

# 11) What is a package in Python?

A package is a folder containing multiple modules.

### Simple idea
- module = one Python file
- package = collection of Python files

---

# 12) How do you handle exceptions in Python?

Exceptions are errors that happen during program execution.

You use `try` and `except`.

### Example
```python
try:
    x = 10 / 0
except ZeroDivisionError:
    print("Cannot divide by zero")
```

### Output
```python
Cannot divide by zero
```

---

## Exception handling keywords

### `try`
Code that may cause error

### `except`
Runs if error happens

### `finally`
Runs whether error happens or not

### Example
```python
try:
    num = int("abc")
except ValueError:
    print("Invalid number")
finally:
    print("Program ended")
```

### Output
```python
Invalid number
Program ended
```

---

# 13) What is file handling in Python?

File handling means reading or writing data in files.

### Read file
```python
file = open("sample.txt", "r")
print(file.read())
file.close()
```

### Write file
```python
file = open("sample.txt", "w")
file.write("Hello Python")
file.close()
```

### Better way using `with`
```python
with open("sample.txt", "r") as file:
    print(file.read())
```

### Why use `with`?
It automatically closes the file.

---

# 14) What is `len()`?

`len()` returns the number of items.

### Example
```python
nums = [1, 2, 3, 4]
print(len(nums))
```

### Output
```python
4
```

---

# 15) What is type casting?

Type casting means converting one data type into another.

### Example
```python
a = "10"
b = int(a)
print(b + 5)
```

### Output
```python
15
```

---

# 16) What is `input()`?

`input()` takes value from user.

### Example
```python
name = input("Enter your name: ")
print("Hello", name)
```

### Output
```python
Enter your name: Rahul
Hello Rahul
```

---

# 17) What is the difference between `==` and `is`?

- `==` checks **value**
- `is` checks **identity** (same memory location)

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2]
b = [1, 2]

print(a == b)
print(a is b)
```

### Output
```python
True
False
```

---

# 18) What is a lambda function?

A lambda function is a small anonymous function.

### Example
```python
add = lambda x, y: x + y
print(add(2, 3))
```

### Output
```python
5
```

### Use
Useful for short operations.

---

# 19) What is the difference between `map()`, `filter()`, and `reduce()`?

## `map()`
Applies a function to each item.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
result = list(map(lambda x: x * 2, nums))
print(result)
```

Output:
```python
[2, 4, 6]
```

## `filter()`
Keeps only items that satisfy a condition.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3, 4]
result = list(filter(lambda x: x % 2 == 0, nums))
print(result)
```

Output:
```python
[2, 4]
```

## `reduce()`
Combines items into one value.

```python
from functools import reduce

nums = [1, 2, 3, 4]
result = reduce(lambda x, y: x + y, nums)
print(result)
```

Output:
```python
10
```

---

# 20) What is copy vs assignment?

## Assignment
Both variables point to same object.

```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
b = a
b.append(4)
print(a)
print(b)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

## Copy
New object is created.

```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
b = a.copy()
b.append(4)
print(a)
print(b)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3]
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

# Topic 1: Python Basics

## 1. What is Python?
Python is a **high-level programming language** used to write programs in a simple and readable way.

### Easy explanation
Think of Python like English for computers.  
It is easier to read than many other languages.

### Why people use Python
- easy to learn
- readable syntax
- used in web development, automation, data science, AI, ML, testing, and scripting
- large community support

### Example
```python
print("Hello, Python!")
```

### Output
```python
Hello, Python!
```

---

## 2. What are the main features of Python?
### Answer in easy language
Python is popular because:
- it is simple
- it is readable
- it supports object-oriented programming
- it has many built-in libraries
- it works on different platforms
- it is good for quick development

### Example
```python
a = 10
b = 20
print(a + b)
```

### Output
```python
30
```

---

## 3. Is Python compiled or interpreted?
Python is mainly an **interpreted language**.

### Easy explanation
When you run Python code, it is executed line by line by the Python interpreter.

### Interview note
In real use, Python first converts code into bytecode, then the interpreter runs it.

---

## 4. What is indentation in Python?
Indentation means **spaces at the beginning of a line**.

### Easy explanation
Python uses indentation to show blocks of code.

### Example
```python
age = 18

if age >= 18:
    print("You are eligible to vote")
```

### Output
```python
You are eligible to vote
```

### Why important
If indentation is wrong, Python gives an error.

---

## 5. What are variables in Python?
Variables are used to store values.

### Easy explanation
A variable is like a box with a name.

### Example
```python
name = "John"
age = 25
print(name)
print(age)
```

### Output
```python
John
25
```

---

## 6. What are Python data types?
Python has different types of values such as:
- `int` for numbers
- `float` for decimal numbers
- `str` for text
- `bool` for true/false
- `list`
- `tuple`
- `set`
- `dict`

### Example
```python
x = 10
y = 5.5
z = "Python"
flag = True

print(type(x))
print(type(y))
print(type(z))
print(type(flag))
```

### Output
```python
<class 'int'>
<class 'float'>
<class 'str'>
<class 'bool'>
```

---

## 7. What is the difference between `==` and `is`?
- `==` checks **value equality**
- `is` checks whether two variables point to the **same object**

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2]
b = [1, 2]
c = a

print(a == b)
print(a is b)
print(a is c)
```

### Output
```python
True
False
True
```

### Easy explanation
- `==` asks: “Do these have same contents?”
- `is` asks: “Are these the same object in memory?”

---

## 8. What is mutable and immutable?
### Mutable
Can be changed after creation.

Examples:
- list
- dict
- set

### Immutable
Cannot be changed after creation.

Examples:
- int
- float
- string
- tuple

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
a.append(4)
print(a)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

## 9. What is type casting?
Changing one data type into another.

### Example
```python
x = "100"
y = int(x)
print(y + 10)
```

### Output
```python
110
```

---

## 10. What is the difference between `print()` and `return`?
- `print()` shows output on screen
- `return` sends value back from a function

### Example
```python
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

result = add(2, 3)
print(result)
```

### Output
```python
5
```

# Topic 2: List in Python

## What is a list?
A list is an ordered collection of items.

### Easy explanation
A list is like a container where you can store multiple values together.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'banana', 'mango']
```

### Key points
- ordered
- mutable
- allows duplicates
- can store mixed data types

### Example
```python
data = [1, "hello", 3.5, True]
print(data)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 'hello', 3.5, True]
```

---

## List methods with uses, definition, code, output

### 1. `append()`
Adds one item at the end.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.append(4)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

### 2. `extend()`
Adds multiple items from another list.

```python
a = [1, 2]
a.extend([3, 4])
print(a)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

### 3. `insert()`
Adds item at a specific position.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 4]
nums.insert(2, 3)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

### 4. `remove()`
Removes first matching value.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3, 2]
nums.remove(2)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 3, 2]
```

### 5. `pop()`
Removes item at index and returns it.

```python
nums = [10, 20, 30]
x = nums.pop()
print(x)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
30
[10, 20]
```

### 6. `clear()`
Removes all items.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.clear()
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[]
```

### 7. `index()`
Returns position of first match.

```python
nums = [5, 10, 15]
print(nums.index(10))
```

Output:
```python
1
```

### 8. `count()`
Counts occurrences of a value.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 2, 3]
print(nums.count(2))
```

Output:
```python
2
```

### 9. `sort()`
Sorts list in place.

```python
nums = [3, 1, 2]
nums.sort()
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3]
```

### 10. `reverse()`
Reverses list in place.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.reverse()
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[3, 2, 1]
```

### 11. `copy()`
Creates shallow copy.

```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
b = a.copy()
print(b)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3]
```

# 1) What is the difference between `print()` and `input()`?

## `print()`
Used to show output on the screen.

```python
print("Hello World")
```

### Output
```python
Hello World
```

## `input()`
Used to take input from the user.

```python
name = input("Enter your name: ")
print("Hello", name)
```

### Example input
```python
Rahul
```

### Output
```python
Enter your name: Rahul
Hello Rahul
```

### Easy explanation
- `print()` sends message **to user**
- `input()` takes message **from user**

---

# 2) What is the `if-else` statement?

Used to make decisions.

```python
age = 20

if age >= 18:
    print("Adult")
else:
    print("Minor")
```

### Output
```python
Adult
```

### Easy explanation
- if condition is true → run first block
- otherwise → run else block

---

# 3) What is `elif`?

Used when there are more than two conditions.

```python
marks = 75

if marks >= 90:
    print("Grade A")
elif marks >= 60:
    print("Grade B")
else:
    print("Grade C")
```

### Output
```python
Grade B
```

---

# 4) What is a loop?

A loop repeats code again and again.

There are two main loops:
- `for`
- `while`

---

# 5) What is a `for` loop?

Used when you know how many times to repeat.

```python
for i in range(5):
    print(i)
```

### Output
```python
0
1
2
3
4
```

### Easy explanation
`range(5)` means numbers from 0 to 4.

---

# 6) What is a `while` loop?

Used when repetition depends on a condition.

```python
i = 1
while i <= 5:
    print(i)
    i += 1
```

### Output
```python
1
2
3
4
5
```

### Important
If you forget `i += 1`, the loop may run forever.

---

# 7) What is `break`?

Stops the loop completely.

```python
for i in range(1, 6):
    if i == 3:
        break
    print(i)
```

### Output
```python
1
2
```

---

# 8) What is `continue`?

Skips the current iteration and goes to the next one.

```python
for i in range(1, 6):
    if i == 3:
        continue
    print(i)
```

### Output
```python
1
2
4
5
```

---

# 9) What is `pass`?

Used when Python expects code, but you don’t want to write anything yet.

```python
for i in range(3):
    pass
```

### Easy explanation
It does nothing.

---

# 10) What is a function?

A function is a reusable block of code.

```python
def greet():
    print("Hello!")

greet()
```

### Output
```python
Hello!
```

### Easy explanation
Instead of writing same code again and again, put it inside a function.

---

# 11) Function with parameters

```python
def greet(name):
    print("Hello", name)

greet("Anil")
```

### Output
```python
Hello Anil
```

---

# 12) Function with return

```python
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

result = add(5, 3)
print(result)
```

### Output
```python
8
```

A string is text inside quotes.

```python

print(name)
```

### Output
```python

```

Used to get part of a string.


### Output


# 15) String methods

## `lower()`
```python
text = "HELLO"
print(text.lower())
```

Output:
```python
hello
```

## `upper()`
```python
text = "hello"
print(text.upper())
```

Output:
```python
HELLO
```

## `strip()`
Removes extra spaces.

```python
text = "  hello  "
print(text.strip())
```

Output:
```python
hello
```

## `replace()`
```python
text = "I like Java"
print(text.replace("Java", "Python"))
```

Output:
```python
I like Python
```

## `split()`
```python
text = "a,b,c"
print(text.split(","))
```

Output:
```python
['a', 'b', 'c']
```

## `join()`
```python
words = ["a", "b", "c"]
print("-".join(words))
```

Output:
```python
a-b-c
```

---

# 16) What is a list?

A list stores multiple items.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
print(nums)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3]
```

---

# 17) Common list methods

## `append()`
Adds one item at end.

```python
nums = [1, 2]
nums.append(3)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3]
```

## `remove()`
Removes first matching item.

```python
nums = [1, 2, 3, 2]
nums.remove(2)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 3, 2]
```

## `pop()`
Removes and returns item.

```python
nums = [10, 20, 30]
x = nums.pop()
print(x)
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
30
[10, 20]
```

## `sort()`
```python
nums = [3, 1, 2]
nums.sort()
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[1, 2, 3]
```

## `reverse()`
```python
nums = [1, 2, 3]
nums.reverse()
print(nums)
```

Output:
```python
[3, 2, 1]
```

---

# 18) What is a tuple?

A tuple is like a list, but it cannot be changed.

```python
t = (1, 2, 3)
print(t)
```

### Output
```python
(1, 2, 3)
```

### Easy explanation
- list = changeable
- tuple = fixed

---

# 19) What is a dictionary?

Dictionary stores data in key-value pairs.

```python
student = {"name": "Rahul", "age": 25}
print(student)
```

### Output
```python
{'name': 'Rahul', 'age': 25}
```

### Easy explanation
Like a real dictionary:
- key = word
- value = meaning

---

# 20) Common dictionary methods

## `keys()`
```python
student = {"name": "Rahul", "age": 25}
print(student.keys())
```

Output:
```python
dict_keys(['name', 'age'])
```

## `values()`
```python
print(student.values())
```

Output:
```python
dict_values(['Rahul', 25])
```

## `items()`
```python
print(student.items())
```

Output:
```python
dict_items([('name', 'Rahul'), ('age', 25)])
```

## `get()`
```python
print(student.get("name"))
```

Output:
```python
Rahul
```

## `update()`
```python
student.update({"city": "Delhi"})
print(student)
```

Output:
```python
{'name': 'Rahul', 'age': 25, 'city': 'Delhi'}
```

---

# 21) What is a set?

A set stores unique items only.

```python
s = {1, 2, 3, 2}
print(s)
```

### Output
```python
{1, 2, 3}
```

### Easy explanation
Duplicates are automatically removed.

---

# 22) Set methods

## `add()`
```python

```

## `update()`

Output:

```python
{1, 2, 3, 4}
```

## `remove()`
```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.remove(2)
print(s)
```

Output:
```python

```

## `discard()`
```python
s = {1, 2, 3}
s.discard(5)
print(s)
```

Output:
```python
{1, 2, 3}
```

# 23) What is exception handling?

Used to handle errors.

```python

    x = 10 / 0
except ZeroDivisionError:
    print("Cannot divide by zero")
```

### Output
```python
Cannot divide by zero
```

### Easy explanation
Instead of program crashing, we show a friendly message.

Used to read and write files.

```python
f.close()
```

```python
f = open("test.txt", "r")
print(f.read())
f.close()
```

### Output
```python
Hello File
```

### Output

Absolutely — here are **basic Python interview questions with simple answers** in easy language.

---

# 1) What is Python?
Python is a **programming language** used to write instructions for computers.

### Easy meaning:
It is simple, readable, and widely used in web development, automation, data science, and AI.

### Example
```python
print("Hello, Python!")
```

### Output
```python
Hello, Python!
```

---

# 2) Why is Python popular?
Python is popular because:
- it is easy to learn
- it has simple syntax
- it supports many libraries
- it is used in many fields like AI, data science, and automation

---

# 3) Is Python compiled or interpreted?
Python is mainly an **interpreted language**.

### Easy meaning:
Python code is executed line by line.

---

# 4) What is indentation in Python?
Indentation means **spaces at the start of a line**.

### Easy meaning:
Python uses indentation to decide which code belongs together.

### Example
```python
if True:
    print("This is inside if")
```

### Output
```python
This is inside if
```

---

# 5) What are variables?
Variables are used to **store values**.

### Example
```python
name = "Alice"
age = 25
print(name)
print(age)
```

### Output
```python
Alice
25
```

---

# 6) What are data types in Python?
Data types tell us what kind of value a variable holds.

### Common types:
- `int` → whole numbers
- `float` → decimal numbers
- `str` → text
- `bool` → True/False
- `list`, `tuple`, `set`, `dict`

### Example
```python
x = 10
y = 3.5
z = "Python"
flag = True

print(type(x))
print(type(y))
print(type(z))
print(type(flag))
```

### Output
```python
<class 'int'>
<class 'float'>
<class 'str'>
<class 'bool'>
```

---

# 7) What is the difference between `==` and `is`?
- `==` checks if values are equal
- `is` checks if both variables point to the same object

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2]
b = [1, 2]
c = a

print(a == b)
print(a is b)
print(a is c)
```

### Output
```python
True
False
True
```

---

# 8) What is mutable and immutable?
### Mutable
Can be changed after creation.
Examples: list, dict, set

### Immutable
Cannot be changed after creation.
Examples: int, float, string, tuple

### Example
```python
a = [1, 2, 3]
a.append(4)
print(a)
```

### Output
```python
[1, 2, 3, 4]
```

---

# 9) What is a list?
A list is an **ordered collection** of items.

### Example
```python
fruits = ["apple", "banana", "mango"]
print(fruits)
```

### Output
```python
['apple', 'banana', 'mango']
```

### Easy meaning:
A list is like a box where you keep many items together.
