## Copilot

Here's a **complete, simple, easy-to-memorize guide on RAG fundamentals** with code.

---

# Simple way to remember RAG

```
RAG = FIND + ANSWER

Step 1: FIND relevant documents
Step 2: ANSWER using those documents
```

---

# 1) What is RAG?

RAG = **Retrieval Augmented Generation**

## Simple meaning
Instead of just asking LLM directly,
you first **find relevant information**
then give it to LLM to **answer**.

---

## Real life example
Imagine you are giving an exam.

**Without RAG:**
You answer from memory only.
You may forget or make mistakes.

**With RAG:**
You are allowed to refer to notes.
Your answers are more accurate.

---

## Simple diagram
```
WITHOUT RAG:
User Question → LLM → Answer
(may hallucinate)

WITH RAG:
User Question → Search Documents → Find Relevant Docs
                                          ↓
                              LLM reads docs + Question
                                          ↓
                                   Accurate Answer
```

---

# 2) Why RAG is needed

## Problems without RAG

### Problem 1: Hallucination
LLM makes up answers confidently.

### Problem 2: Outdated knowledge
LLM training data has a cutoff date.

### Problem 3: No private data
LLM does not know your company documents.

### Problem 4: No real-time data
LLM cannot access live information.

---

## RAG solves all of these

| Problem | RAG solution |
|---|---|
| Hallucination | answers from real documents |
| Outdated knowledge | add new documents anytime |
| No private data | add your own documents |
| No real-time data | update knowledge base |

---

# 3) Retrieval Step

The retrieval step means **finding relevant documents** for a query.

---

## Simple flow
```
User query
    ↓
Convert query to vector (embedding)
    ↓
Search vector database
    ↓
Get top matching documents
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# retrieval_step.py
# ==========================================
# Simple retrieval step example
# ==========================================

# Sample knowledge base
knowledge_base = [
    "Python is a programming language used in AI.",
    "RAG stands for Retrieval Augmented Generation.",
    "Decorators modify functions without changing code.",
    "NumPy is used for numerical computing.",
    "LLMs are large language models trained on text.",
    "FastAPI is a Python web framework.",
    "Pandas is used for data analysis.",
    "Machine learning is a subset of AI.",
]

def retrieve(query, knowledge_base, top_k=3):
    """
    Simple keyword-based retrieval.
    Returns top_k most relevant documents.
    """
    query_words = query.lower().split()
    scored_docs = []

    for doc in knowledge_base:
        score = 0
        for word in query_words:
            if word in doc.lower():
                score += 1
        if score > 0:
            scored_docs.append((score, doc))

    # Sort by score (highest first)
    scored_docs.sort(reverse=True)

    # Return top k documents
    return [doc for score, doc in scored_docs[:top_k]]


# Test retrieval
query = "What is Python used for?"
results = retrieve(query, knowledge_base)

print(f"Query: {query}")
print(f"\nRetrieved documents:")
for i, doc in enumerate(results, 1):
    print(f"  {i}. {doc}")
```

### Output
```
Query: What is Python used for?

Retrieved documents:
  1. Python is a programming language used in AI.
  2. LLMs are large language models trained on text.
  3. Machine learning is a subset of AI.
```

---

# 4) Generation Step

The generation step means **LLM reads retrieved documents and generates an answer**.

---

## Simple flow
```
Retrieved documents
    +
User question
    ↓
LLM reads both
    ↓
Generates accurate answer
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# generation_step.py
# ==========================================
# Simple generation step example
# ==========================================

def generate_answer(query, context_docs):
    """
    Combines query and context into a prompt
    and sends to LLM for generation.
    """

    # Build context from retrieved docs
    context = "\n".join(context_docs)

    # Build prompt
    prompt = f"""
Answer the question using only the context below.
If the answer is not in the context, say "I don't know."

Context:
{context}

Question: {query}

Answer:
"""
    return prompt


# Test generation step
query = "What is Python used for?"
context_docs = [
    "Python is a programming language used in AI.",
    "Python is great for data science and web development.",
]

prompt = generate_answer(query, context_docs)
print(prompt)
```

### Output
```
Answer the question using only the context below.
If the answer is not in the context, say "I don't know."

Context:
Python is a programming language used in AI.
Python is great for data science and web development.

Question: What is Python used for?

Answer:
```

---

# 5) Grounded Responses

Grounded response means the answer is **based on real documents**, not just guessing.

---

## Simple meaning
```
NOT grounded:
LLM guesses from training → may be wrong

GROUNDED:
LLM uses real documents → more accurate
```

---

## Example

```python
# grounded_vs_not_grounded.py
# ==========================================
# Showing difference between grounded
# and ungrounded responses
# ==========================================

# Ungrounded prompt
ungrounded_prompt = """
Question: What is our company's refund policy?
Answer:
"""
# LLM does not know your company policy
# It will guess or hallucinate

# Grounded prompt
company_policy = """
Our company offers a 30-day money-back guarantee.
Refund requests must be submitted via email.
Refunds are processed within 5-7 business days.
"""

grounded_prompt = f"""
Answer the question using only the context below.

Context:
{company_policy}

Question: What is our company's refund policy?
Answer:
"""
# LLM reads the actual policy and answers correctly

print("Ungrounded prompt:")
print(ungrounded_prompt)
print("\nGrounded prompt:")
print(grounded_prompt)
```

---

# 6) Hallucination Reduction

Hallucination = LLM gives wrong answer confidently.

RAG reduces this by giving the LLM real information.

---

## How RAG reduces hallucination

```python
# hallucination_reduction.py
# ==========================================
# How RAG reduces hallucination
# ==========================================

# Technique 1: Only use context
prompt_technique_1 = """
Answer ONLY from the context below.
If the answer is not in the context,
say "I don't have that information."

Context: {context}
Question: {question}
"""

# Technique 2: Ask LLM to cite sources
prompt_technique_2 = """
Answer the question using the context.
After your answer, mention which part
of the context you used.

Context: {context}
Question: {question}
"""

# Technique 3: Ask for confidence
prompt_technique_3 = """
Answer the question using the context.
At the end, rate your confidence:
- High: answer clearly in context
- Medium: partially in context
- Low: not in context

Context: {context}
Question: {question}
"""

techniques = {
    "Only use context": prompt_technique_1,
    "Cite sources": prompt_technique_2,
    "Rate confidence": prompt_technique_3
}

for name, technique in techniques.items():
    print(f"Technique: {name}")
    print(f"{technique[:100]}...")
    print()
```

---

# 7) Knowledge Base Setup

The knowledge base is the **collection of documents** your RAG system searches.

---

## Simple structure
```
knowledge_base/
├── python_docs.txt
├── company_policy.txt
├── product_info.txt
└── faq.txt
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# knowledge_base_setup.py
# ==========================================
# Setting up a knowledge base
# ==========================================

import os

class KnowledgeBase:
    def __init__(self):
        # Stores all documents
        self.documents = []

    def add_text(self, text, metadata=None):
        """
        Adds a text document to knowledge base.
        """
        self.documents.append({
            "text": text,
            "metadata": metadata or {}
        })
        print(f"Added: {text[:50]}...")

    def add_from_file(self, file_path):
        """
        Loads documents from a text file.
        """
        if not os.path.exists(file_path):
            print(f"File not found: {file_path}")
            return

        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            text = f.read()
            self.documents.append({
                "text": text,
                "metadata": {"source": file_path}
            })
        print(f"Loaded file: {file_path}")

    def add_from_list(self, text_list):
        """
        Adds multiple texts at once.
        """
        for text in text_list:
            self.add_text(text)

    def get_all_texts(self):
        """
        Returns all document texts.
        """
        return [doc["text"] for doc in self.documents]

    def size(self):
        return len(self.documents)


# Setup knowledge base
kb = KnowledgeBase()

# Add documents
kb.add_text(
    "Python is a programming language used in AI.",
    metadata={"category": "Python", "level": "beginner"}
)

kb.add_text(
    "RAG combines retrieval and generation.",
    metadata={"category": "AI", "level": "intermediate"}
)

kb.add_from_list([
    "NumPy is used for numerical computing.",
    "Pandas is used for data analysis.",
    "FastAPI is a modern Python web framework.",
])

print(f"\nKnowledge base size: {kb.size()}")
print(f"\nAll documents:")
for doc in kb.get_all_texts():
    print(f"  - {doc}")
```

---

# 8) Document Ingestion

Document ingestion means **loading documents** into your RAG system.

---

## Types of documents
- text files
- PDF files
- web pages
- CSV files
- JSON files

---

## Simple code

```python
# document_ingestion.py
# ==========================================
# Document ingestion pipeline
# ==========================================

import json
import csv

class DocumentIngester:

    @staticmethod
    def from_text(text):
        """Load from plain text."""
        return [{"text": text, "source": "text"}]

    @staticmethod
    def from_txt_file(file_path):
        """Load from .txt file."""
        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            text = f.read()
        return [{"text": text, "source": file_path}]

    @staticmethod
    def from_json_file(file_path):
        """Load from .json file."""
        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            data = json.load(f)
        documents = []
        if isinstance(data, list):
            for item in data:
                documents.append({
                    "text": str(item),
                    "source": file_path
                })
        return documents

    @staticmethod
    def from_csv_file(file_path, text_column):
        """Load from .csv file."""
        documents = []
        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            reader = csv.DictReader(f)
            for row in reader:
                documents.append({
                    "text": row[text_column],
                    "source": file_path
                })
        return documents

    @staticmethod
    def from_list(texts):
        """Load from a list of strings."""
        return [
            {"text": text, "source": "list"}
            for text in texts
        ]


# Test ingestion
ingester = DocumentIngester()

# From text
docs = ingester.from_text("Python is a great language.")
print("From text:", docs)

# From list
docs = ingester.from_list([
    "Python is used for AI.",
    "RAG is important for LLMs.",
    "Embeddings capture meaning."
])
print("\nFrom list:")
for doc in docs:
    print(f"  - {doc['text']}")
```

---

# 9) Chunking

Chunking means **splitting large documents into smaller pieces**.

---

## Why chunking is important
```
PROBLEM:
Large document → too big for context window
LLM cannot process very long text

SOLUTION:
Split into small chunks
Each chunk fits in context
Retrieve only relevant chunks
```

---

## Types of chunking

```python
# chunking.py
# ==========================================
# Different ways to chunk documents
# ==========================================

class TextChunker:

    @staticmethod
    def fixed_size_chunks(text, chunk_size=100, overlap=20):
        """
        Splits text into fixed size chunks.
        overlap = how many characters repeat
        between chunks to maintain context.
        """
        chunks = []
        start = 0

        while start < len(text):
            end = start + chunk_size
            chunk = text[start:end]
            chunks.append(chunk)
            # Move start forward but keep overlap
            start += chunk_size - overlap

        return chunks

    @staticmethod
    def sentence_chunks(text):
        """
        Splits text by sentences.
        """
        sentences = text.split(". ")
        return [s.strip() for s in sentences if s.strip()]

    @staticmethod
    def paragraph_chunks(text):
        """
        Splits text by paragraphs.
        """
        paragraphs = text.split("\n\n")
        return [p.strip() for p in paragraphs if p.strip()]

    @staticmethod
    def word_chunks(text, words_per_chunk=50, overlap=10):
        """
        Splits text by word count.
        """
        words = text.split()
        chunks = []
        start = 0

        while start < len(words):
            end = start + words_per_chunk
            chunk = " ".join(words[start:end])
            chunks.append(chunk)
            start += words_per_chunk - overlap

        return chunks


# Test chunking
chunker = TextChunker()

long_text = """
Python is a programming language. It is used in AI and data science.
Python has simple syntax. Many developers love Python.

RAG stands for Retrieval Augmented Generation. It combines retrieval
with generation. RAG reduces hallucination in LLMs.

NumPy is used for numerical computing. Pandas is used for data
analysis. Both are important Python libraries.
"""

# Fixed size
fixed_chunks = chunker.fixed_size_chunks(long_text, chunk_size=100)
print(f"Fixed size chunks: {len(fixed_chunks)}")
for i, c in enumerate(fixed_chunks[:2], 1):
    print(f"  Chunk {i}: {c[:60]}...")

# Sentence chunks
sentence_chunks = chunker.sentence_chunks(long_text)
print(f"\nSentence chunks: {len(sentence_chunks)}")
for i, c in enumerate(sentence_chunks[:3], 1):
    print(f"  Chunk {i}: {c}")

# Paragraph chunks
para_chunks = chunker.paragraph_chunks(long_text)
print(f"\nParagraph chunks: {len(para_chunks)}")
for i, c in enumerate(para_chunks[:2], 1):
    print(f"  Chunk {i}: {c[:60]}...")

# Word chunks
word_chunks = chunker.word_chunks(long_text, words_per_chunk=20)
print(f"\nWord chunks: {len(word_chunks)}")
for i, c in enumerate(word_chunks[:2], 1):
    print(f"  Chunk {i}: {c}")
```

---

# 10) Indexing

Indexing means **organizing chunks into a searchable structure**.

---

## Simple idea
```
Without index:
Search every document one by one → slow

With index:
Organized structure → fast search
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# indexing.py
# ==========================================
# Simple indexing example
# ==========================================

class SimpleIndex:
    def __init__(self):
        # Store documents with id
        self.documents = {}
        # Inverted index: word → list of doc ids
        self.inverted_index = {}
        self.next_id = 0

    def add_document(self, text, metadata=None):
        """
        Adds document to index.
        """
        doc_id = self.next_id
        self.next_id += 1

        # Store document
        self.documents[doc_id] = {
            "text": text,
            "metadata": metadata or {}
        }

        # Build inverted index
        words = text.lower().split()
        for word in set(words):
            if word not in self.inverted_index:
                self.inverted_index[word] = []
            self.inverted_index[word].append(doc_id)

        return doc_id

    def search(self, query, top_k=3):
        """
        Searches index for relevant documents.
        """
        query_words = query.lower().split()
        doc_scores = {}

        # Score each document
        for word in query_words:
            if word in self.inverted_index:
                for doc_id in self.inverted_index[word]:
                    doc_scores[doc_id] = doc_scores.get(doc_id, 0) + 1

        # Sort by score
        sorted_docs = sorted(
            doc_scores.items(),
            key=lambda x: x[1],
            reverse=True
        )

        # Return top k
        results = []
        for doc_id, score in sorted_docs[:top_k]:
            results.append({
                "text": self.documents[doc_id]["text"],
                "score": score,
                "metadata": self.documents[doc_id]["metadata"]
            })

        return results


# Test indexing
index = SimpleIndex()

# Add documents
index.add_document("Python is great for AI", {"category": "Python"})
index.add_document("RAG combines retrieval and generation", {"category": "AI"})
index.add_document("Python is used for data science", {"category": "Python"})
index.add_document("LLMs are trained on large text", {"category": "AI"})
index.add_document("NumPy is a Python library", {"category": "Python"})

# Search
results = index.search("Python AI")
print("Search results for 'Python AI':")
for r in results:
    print(f"  Score: {r['score']} | {r['text']}")
```

---

# 11) Query Retrieval

Query retrieval means **converting user question into a search** and getting relevant documents.

---

## Full query retrieval example

```python
# query_retrieval.py
# ==========================================
# Full query retrieval pipeline
# ==========================================

class QueryRetriever:
    def __init__(self, documents):
        self.documents = documents

    def preprocess_query(self, query):
        """
        Cleans and prepares the query.
        """
        # Remove extra spaces
        query = query.strip()
        # Lowercase
        query = query.lower()
        # Remove question marks
        query = query.replace("?", "")
        return query

    def retrieve(self, query, top_k=3):
        """
        Full retrieval pipeline:
        1. Preprocess query
        2. Score documents
        3. Return top k
        """
        # Step 1: Preprocess
        clean_query = self.preprocess_query(query)
        print(f"Clean query: {clean_query}")

        # Step 2: Score documents
        query_words = clean_query.split()
        scored_docs = []

        for doc in self.documents:
            score = 0
            for word in query_words:
                if word in doc.lower():
                    score += 1
            if score > 0:
                scored_docs.append((score, doc))

        # Step 3: Sort and return top k
        scored_docs.sort(reverse=True)
        results = [doc for score, doc in scored_docs[:top_k]]

        print(f"Found {len(results)} relevant documents")
        return results

    def format_context(self, documents):
        """
        Formats retrieved documents into context string.
        """
        if not documents:
            return "No relevant context found."

        context = "Relevant information:\n"
        for i, doc in enumerate(documents, 1):
            context += f"{i}. {doc}\n"

        return context


# Test full pipeline
documents = [
    "Python is a programming language used in AI.",
    "RAG stands for Retrieval Augmented Generation.",
    "Decorators modify functions without changing code.",
    "NumPy is used for numerical computing in Python.",
    "LLMs are large language models trained on text.",
    "FastAPI is a Python web framework.",
    "Machine learning is a subset of AI.",
]

retriever = QueryRetriever(documents)

# Test queries
queries = [
    "What is Python used for?",
    "How does RAG work?",
    "What is machine learning?",
]

for query in queries:
    print(f"\nQuery: {query}")
    results = retriever.retrieve(query, top_k=2)
    context = retriever.format_context(results)
    print(context)
```

---

# Full RAG pipeline combined

```python
# full_rag_pipeline.py
# ==========================================
# Complete RAG pipeline from scratch
# ==========================================

class RAGPipeline:
    def __init__(self):
        # Knowledge base
        self.documents = []

    # ==========================================
    # Step 1: Add documents
    # ==========================================
    def add_documents(self, texts):
        self.documents.extend(texts)
        print(f"Added {len(texts)} documents")
        print(f"Total documents: {len(self.documents)}")

    # ==========================================
    # Step 2: Chunk documents
    # ==========================================
    def chunk_documents(self, chunk_size=100):
        chunked = []
        for doc in self.documents:
            words = doc.split()
            for i in range(0, len(words), chunk_size):
                chunk = " ".join(words[i:i+chunk_size])
                chunked.append(chunk)
        self.documents = chunked
        print(f"Chunked into {len(self.documents)} pieces")

    # ==========================================
    # Step 3: Retrieve relevant docs
    # ==========================================
    def retrieve(self, query, top_k=3):
        query_words = query.lower().split()
        scored = []

        for doc in self.documents:
            score = sum(
                1 for word in query_words
                if word in doc.lower()
            )
            if score > 0:
                scored.append((score, doc))

        scored.sort(reverse=True)
        return [doc for score, doc in scored[:top_k]]

    # ==========================================
    # Step 4: Build prompt
    # ==========================================
    def build_prompt(self, query, context_docs):
        context = "\n".join(
            [f"{i+1}. {doc}"
             for i, doc in enumerate(context_docs)]
        )

        return f"""
You are a helpful assistant.
Answer the question using only the context below.
If the answer is not in the context,
say "I don't have that information."

Context:
{context}

Question: {query}

Answer:
"""

    # ==========================================
    # Step 5: Full RAG query
    # ==========================================
    def query(self, user_question):
        print(f"\nQuestion: {user_question}")

        # Retrieve
        context_docs = self.retrieve(user_question)
        print(f"Retrieved {len(context_docs)} documents")

        # Build prompt
        prompt = self.build_prompt(user_question, context_docs)
        print(f"\nPrompt built successfully")
        print(f"\n{prompt}")

        # In real code: send prompt to LLM
        # response = llm.generate(prompt)
        # return response

        return prompt


# ==========================================
# Test full pipeline
# ==========================================
rag = RAGPipeline()

# Add knowledge base
rag.add_documents([
    "Python is a programming language used in AI and data science.",
    "RAG stands for Retrieval Augmented Generation.",
    "RAG reduces hallucination by grounding answers in real documents.",
    "Decorators in Python modify functions without changing their code.",
    "NumPy is used for numerical computing.",
    "Pandas is used for data analysis in Python.",
    "LLMs are large language models trained on massive text datasets.",
    "Machine learning is a subset of artificial intelligence.",
    "FastAPI is a modern Python web framework for building APIs.",
    "Embeddings are vector representations that capture semantic meaning.",
])

# Query
rag.query("What is Python used for?")
rag.query("How does RAG reduce hallucination?")
```

---

# Easy memory sheet

```
RAG = FIND + ANSWER

What RAG is       → find docs then answer
Why needed        → hallucination, outdated data, private data
Retrieval step    → find relevant documents
Generation step   → LLM reads docs and answers
Grounded response → answer from real documents
Hallucination     → wrong confident answer - RAG reduces it
Knowledge base    → your document collection
Document ingestion→ loading documents
Chunking          → splitting docs into small pieces
Indexing          → organizing for fast search
Query retrieval   → searching relevant docs for a question
```

---

# Interview-ready one-line answers

## What is RAG?
RAG is a technique that retrieves relevant documents first and then uses them as context for an LLM to generate accurate answers.

## Why is RAG needed?
To reduce hallucination, add private knowledge, and give LLMs access to up-to-date information.

## What is chunking?
Splitting large documents into smaller pieces so they fit in the LLM context window.

## What is grounding?
Basing the LLM answer on real retrieved documents instead of guessing.

# 1) Chatbots

A chatbot is a **conversational AI** that talks with users naturally.

---

## Key features
- remembers conversation history
- responds naturally
- can have a personality
- handles multi-turn conversations

---

## Full code

```python
# chatbot.py
# ==========================================
# Simple chatbot with memory
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class Chatbot:
    def __init__(self, name, personality):
        self.name = name
        # Conversation history
        self.history = []
        # System prompt defines personality
        self.system_prompt = f"""
You are {name}, a helpful AI assistant.
Personality: {personality}
Rules:
- Be friendly and polite
- Keep answers clear and simple
- Remember what user said earlier
"""

    def chat(self, user_message):
        """
        Sends message and gets response.
        Remembers full conversation.
        """
        # Add user message to history
        self.history.append({
            "role": "user",
            "content": user_message
        })

        # Build messages for LLM
        messages = [
            {"role": "system", "content": self.system_prompt}
        ] + self.history

        # Call LLM
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=messages,
            temperature=0.7
        )

        # Get answer
        answer = response.choices[0].message.content

        # Add answer to history
        self.history.append({
            "role": "assistant",
            "content": answer
        })

        return answer

    def clear_history(self):
        self.history = []
        print("Chat history cleared")

    def show_history(self):
        for msg in self.history:
            print(f"{msg['role'].upper()}: {msg['content']}")


# Run chatbot
bot = Chatbot(
    name="PyBot",
    personality="Python expert, friendly teacher"
)

print("PyBot: Hello! I am PyBot. Ask me anything about Python!")

while True:
    user_input = input("You: ").strip()

    if user_input.lower() in ["quit", "exit"]:
        print("PyBot: Goodbye!")
        break

    if user_input.lower() == "clear":
        bot.clear_history()
        continue

    if user_input.lower() == "history":
        bot.show_history()
        continue

    response = bot.chat(user_input)
    print(f"PyBot: {response}\n")
```

---

# 2) Q&A Systems

A Q&A system answers questions **based on specific documents or knowledge base**.

---

## Key features
- answers from given context
- does not guess
- says "I don't know" if not in context

---

## Full code

```python
# qa_system.py
# ==========================================
# Q&A system with knowledge base
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class QASystem:
    def __init__(self, knowledge_base):
        self.knowledge_base = knowledge_base

    def find_context(self, question, top_k=3):
        """
        Finds relevant context from knowledge base.
        Simple keyword search.
        """
        question_words = question.lower().split()
        scored = []

        for doc in self.knowledge_base:
            score = sum(
                1 for word in question_words
                if word in doc.lower()
            )
            if score > 0:
                scored.append((score, doc))

        scored.sort(reverse=True)
        return [doc for score, doc in scored[:top_k]]

    def answer(self, question):
        """
        Finds context and generates answer.
        """
        # Find relevant context
        context_docs = self.find_context(question)

        if not context_docs:
            return "I don't have information about that."

        context = "\n".join(context_docs)

        # Build prompt
        prompt = f"""
Answer the question using ONLY the context below.
If the answer is not in the context,
say exactly: "I don't have that information."

Context:
{context}

Question: {question}

Answer:
"""
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[
                {"role": "user", "content": prompt}
            ],
            temperature=0
        )

        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test Q&A system
knowledge_base = [
    "Python was created by Guido van Rossum in 1991.",
    "Python is used in AI, data science, and web development.",
    "Decorators modify functions without changing their code.",
    "RAG stands for Retrieval Augmented Generation.",
    "LLMs are large language models trained on text data.",
    "NumPy is a Python library for numerical computing.",
    "Pandas is used for data analysis and manipulation.",
    "FastAPI is a modern Python web framework.",
]

qa = QASystem(knowledge_base)

questions = [
    "Who created Python?",
    "What is RAG?",
    "What is NumPy used for?",
    "What is the capital of France?",
]

for q in questions:
    print(f"Q: {q}")
    print(f"A: {qa.answer(q)}\n")
```

---

# 3) Summarization

Summarization means **shortening long text** while keeping the key points.

---

## Types
- short summary
- bullet points
- executive summary
- one-line summary

---

## Full code

```python
# summarization.py
# ==========================================
# Text summarization patterns
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class Summarizer:

    def summarize_short(self, text):
        """One paragraph summary."""
        prompt = f"""
Summarize this text in 2-3 sentences.
Keep only the most important points.

Text: {text}

Summary:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def summarize_bullets(self, text):
        """Bullet point summary."""
        prompt = f"""
Summarize this text as 5 bullet points.
Each bullet should be one clear sentence.

Text: {text}

Bullet points:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def summarize_one_line(self, text):
        """One line summary."""
        prompt = f"""
Summarize this text in exactly one sentence.

Text: {text}

One line summary:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def summarize_executive(self, text):
        """Executive summary with sections."""
        prompt = f"""
Write an executive summary with these sections:
1. Overview (1 sentence)
2. Key points (3 bullets)
3. Conclusion (1 sentence)

Text: {text}

Executive Summary:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.3
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test summarizer
text = """
Python is a high-level programming language known for its
simplicity and readability. It was created by Guido van Rossum
in 1991 and has since become one of the most popular languages
in the world. Python is used in web development, data science,
artificial intelligence, automation, and many other fields.
Its simple syntax makes it ideal for beginners while its powerful
libraries make it suitable for professional developers.
Popular libraries include NumPy, Pandas, TensorFlow, and Django.
"""

summarizer = Summarizer()

print("SHORT SUMMARY:")
print(summarizer.summarize_short(text))

print("\nBULLET SUMMARY:")
print(summarizer.summarize_bullets(text))

print("\nONE LINE:")
print(summarizer.summarize_one_line(text))

print("\nEXECUTIVE SUMMARY:")
print(summarizer.summarize_executive(text))
```

# 4) Extraction

Extraction means **pulling out specific information** from text.

---

## Use cases
- extract names, dates, emails
- extract product details
- extract key facts
- parse structured data

---

## Full code

```python
# extraction.py
# ==========================================
# Information extraction patterns
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI
import json

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class Extractor:

    def extract_entities(self, text):
        """
        Extracts names, dates, places, emails.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Extract all entities from this text.
Return as JSON with these keys:
- names: list of person names
- dates: list of dates
- places: list of places
- emails: list of emails
- organizations: list of organizations

Text: {text}

Return ONLY valid JSON, no extra text.
"""
        result = self._call_llm(prompt)
        return json.loads(result)

    def extract_product_info(self, text):
        """
        Extracts product details from description.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Extract product information from this text.
Return as JSON with these keys:
- product_name
- price
- features (list)
- category
- availability

Text: {text}

Return ONLY valid JSON.
"""
        result = self._call_llm(prompt)
        return json.loads(result)

    def extract_resume_info(self, text):
        """
        Extracts resume/CV information.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Extract resume information from this text.
Return as JSON with these keys:
- name
- email
- phone
- skills (list)
- experience (list)
- education (list)

Text: {text}

Return ONLY valid JSON.
"""
        result = self._call_llm(prompt)
        return json.loads(result)

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test extraction
extractor = Extractor()

# Entity extraction
news_text = """
John Smith met Sarah Johnson in New York on January 15, 2024.
They discussed the merger of TechCorp and DataInc.
Contact them at john@techcorp.com or sarah@datainc.com.
"""

entities = extractor.extract_entities(news_text)
print("EXTRACTED ENTITIES:")
print(json.dumps(entities, indent=2))

# Product extraction
product_text = """
The iPhone 16 Pro is available for $999.
It features a 6.7 inch display, 48MP camera,
A18 chip, and 256GB storage.
Available in Black and Silver.
"""

product = extractor.extract_product_info(product_text)
print("\nEXTRACTED PRODUCT INFO:")
print(json.dumps(product, indent=2))
```

# 5) Classification

Classification means **putting text into categories**.

---

## Use cases
- sentiment analysis
- topic classification
- spam detection
- intent detection

---

## Full code

```python
# classification.py
# ==========================================
# Text classification patterns
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class Classifier:

    def sentiment_analysis(self, text):
        """
        Classifies sentiment: positive, negative, neutral.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Classify the sentiment of this text.
Return ONLY one word: Positive, Negative, or Neutral.

Text: {text}

Sentiment:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt).strip()

    def topic_classification(self, text, topics):
        """
        Classifies text into given topics.
        """
        topics_str = ", ".join(topics)
        prompt = f"""
Classify this text into one of these topics:
{topics_str}

Return ONLY the topic name, nothing else.

Text: {text}

Topic:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt).strip()

    def spam_detection(self, text):
        """
        Detects if text is spam.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Is this text spam or not spam?
Return ONLY one word: Spam or NotSpam.

Text: {text}

Result:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt).strip()

    def intent_detection(self, text):
        """
        Detects user intent.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Detect the intent of this user message.
Choose from: greeting, question, complaint,
request, goodbye, other.

Return ONLY the intent word.

Text: {text}

Intent:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt).strip()

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test classification
classifier = Classifier()

# Sentiment
texts = [
    "I love Python programming!",
    "This code is terrible.",
    "Python is a programming language."
]

print("SENTIMENT ANALYSIS:")
for text in texts:
    sentiment = classifier.sentiment_analysis(text)
    print(f"  '{text}' → {sentiment}")

# Topic classification
topics = ["Technology", "Sports", "Politics", "Health", "Entertainment"]
articles = [
    "Python 4.0 released with new features",
    "Manchester United wins championship",
    "New health guidelines released",
]

print("\nTOPIC CLASSIFICATION:")
for article in articles:
    topic = classifier.topic_classification(article, topics)
    print(f"  '{article}' → {topic}")

# Intent detection
messages = [
    "Hello there!",
    "How does Python work?",
    "This product is broken!",
    "Can you help me?",
    "Bye bye!"
]

print("\nINTENT DETECTION:")
for msg in messages:
    intent = classifier.intent_detection(msg)
    print(f"  '{msg}' → {intent}")
```

# 6) Translation

Translation means **converting text from one language to another**.

---

## Full code

```python
# translation.py
# ==========================================
# Translation patterns
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class Translator:

    def translate(self, text, target_language):
        """
        Translates text to target language.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Translate this text to {target_language}.
Return ONLY the translation, no extra text.

Text: {text}

Translation:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def detect_and_translate(self, text, target_language):
        """
        Detects language and translates.
        """
        prompt = f"""
1. Detect the language of this text.
2. Translate it to {target_language}.

Return as:
Detected language: ...
Translation: ...

Text: {text}
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def translate_multiple(self, text, languages):
        """
        Translates to multiple languages.
        """
        languages_str = ", ".join(languages)
        prompt = f"""
Translate this text to these languages: {languages_str}

Return as JSON like:
{{
    "language_name": "translation",
    ...
}}

Text: {text}

Return ONLY valid JSON.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.1
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test translation
translator = Translator()

text = "Python is an amazing programming language."

print("TRANSLATION:")
print(translator.translate(text, "Spanish"))
print(translator.translate(text, "French"))
print(translator.translate(text, "Hindi"))

print("\nDETECT AND TRANSLATE:")
print(translator.detect_and_translate(
    "Bonjour, comment allez-vous?",
    "English"
))

print("\nMULTIPLE LANGUAGES:")
print(translator.translate_multiple(
    text,
    ["Spanish", "French", "German"]
))
```

# 7) Content Generation

Content generation means **creating new content** like articles, emails, posts.

---

## Full code

```python
# content_generation.py
# ==========================================
# Content generation patterns
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class ContentGenerator:

    def write_blog_post(self, topic, tone="professional"):
        """
        Generates a blog post.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Write a blog post about: {topic}
Tone: {tone}

Structure:
- Title
- Introduction (2 sentences)
- 3 main sections with headings
- Conclusion (2 sentences)

Keep it under 400 words.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def write_email(self, purpose, recipient, key_points):
        """
        Generates a professional email.
        """
        points = "\n".join(key_points)
        prompt = f"""
Write a professional email.
Purpose: {purpose}
Recipient: {recipient}
Key points to cover:
{points}

Format: Subject line + email body.
Keep it concise and professional.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def write_social_post(self, topic, platform):
        """
        Generates social media post.
        """
        limits = {
            "twitter": "280 characters",
            "linkedin": "300 words",
            "instagram": "150 words with hashtags"
        }

        limit = limits.get(platform.lower(), "200 words")

        prompt = f"""
Write a {platform} post about: {topic}
Limit: {limit}
Make it engaging and appropriate for {platform}.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def write_product_description(self, product, features):
        """
        Generates product description.
        """
        features_str = "\n".join(features)
        prompt = f"""
Write a compelling product description for: {product}

Features:
{features_str}

Make it persuasive and professional.
Keep under 150 words.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.7
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test content generation
generator = ContentGenerator()

print("BLOG POST:")
print(generator.write_blog_post("Python for beginners", "friendly"))

print("\nEMAIL:")
print(generator.write_email(
    purpose="Project update",
    recipient="Manager",
    key_points=[
        "Project is 80% complete",
        "Deadline is next Friday",
        "Need approval for extra budget"
    ]
))

print("\nSOCIAL POST:")
print(generator.write_social_post("Python tips", "twitter"))
```

# 8) Code Assistants

Code assistants help with **writing, reviewing, explaining, and debugging code**.

---

## Full code

```python
# code_assistant.py
# ==========================================
# Code assistant patterns
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class CodeAssistant:

    def generate_code(self, description, language="Python"):
        """
        Generates code from description.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Write {language} code for this:
{description}

Rules:
- Add clear comments
- Follow best practices
- Keep it simple and readable

Return ONLY the code, no extra explanation.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def explain_code(self, code):
        """
        Explains what code does.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Explain this code in simple terms.
- What does it do overall?
- What does each part do?
- Any important points to note?

Code:
{code}
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def review_code(self, code):
        """
        Reviews code for issues.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Review this code and provide feedback on:
1. Bugs or errors
2. Performance issues
3. Security issues
4. Code style improvements
5. Best practices

Code:
{code}

Format as numbered list.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def debug_code(self, code, error_message):
        """
        Debugs code given an error message.
        """
        prompt = f"""
This code has an error.

Code:
{code}

Error:
{error_message}

Please:
1. Identify the bug
2. Explain why it happens
3. Provide fixed code
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def convert_code(self, code, from_lang, to_lang):
        """
        Converts code from one language to another.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Convert this {from_lang} code to {to_lang}.
Keep the same logic and add comments.

Code:
{code}

Return ONLY the {to_lang} code.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[
                {
                    "role": "system",
                    "content": "You are an expert programmer."
                },
                {"role": "user", "content": prompt}
            ],
            temperature=0.2
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test code assistant
assistant = CodeAssistant()

print("GENERATE CODE:")
print(assistant.generate_code(
    "A function that takes a list and returns only even numbers"
))

print("\nEXPLAIN CODE:")
code = """
def factorial(n):
    if n == 0:
        return 1
    return n * factorial(n-1)
"""
print(assistant.explain_code(code))

print("\nDEBUG CODE:")
buggy_code = """
def divide(a, b):
    return a / b

print(divide(10, 0))
"""
print(assistant.debug_code(
    buggy_code,
    "ZeroDivisionError: division by zero"
))
```

# 9) Document Assistants

Document assistants help users **interact with documents** - ask questions, get summaries, extract info.

---

## Full code

```python
# document_assistant.py
# ==========================================
# Document assistant pattern
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class DocumentAssistant:
    def __init__(self):
        self.document = None
        self.document_name = None

    def load_document(self, text, name="document"):
        """
        Loads a document into the assistant.
        """
        self.document = text
        self.document_name = name
        print(f"Document loaded: {name}")
        print(f"Length: {len(text)} characters")

    def load_from_file(self, file_path):
        """
        Loads document from file.
        """
        with open(file_path, "r") as f:
            self.document = f.read()
        self.document_name = file_path
        print(f"Loaded: {file_path}")

    def ask(self, question):
        """
        Ask a question about the document.
        """
        if not self.document:
            return "No document loaded."

        prompt = f"""
Answer the question using ONLY this document.
If not in document, say "Not found in document."

Document:
{self.document}

Question: {question}

Answer:
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def summarize(self):
        """
        Summarizes the document.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Summarize this document in:
1. One sentence overview
2. 5 key bullet points
3. One sentence conclusion

Document:
{self.document}
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def extract_key_info(self):
        """
        Extracts key information.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Extract key information from this document:
- Main topic
- Key people mentioned
- Key dates
- Key facts
- Action items (if any)

Document:
{self.document}

Return as a structured list.
"""
        return self._call_llm(prompt)

    def _call_llm(self, prompt):
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.1
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content


# Test document assistant
assistant = DocumentAssistant()

document = """
Python Programming Language Overview

Python was created by Guido van Rossum and released in 1991.
It is a high-level, interpreted programming language known for
its simplicity and readability.

Python is widely used in:
- Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning
- Web Development (Django, Flask, FastAPI)
- Data Science and Analytics
- Automation and Scripting

Key features include:
- Simple and readable syntax
- Large standard library
- Strong community support
- Cross-platform compatibility

Python 3 was released in 2008 and is the current version.
Python 2 reached end of life in January 2020.
"""

assistant.load_document(document, "Python Overview")

print("ASK QUESTION:")
print(assistant.ask("Who created Python?"))

print("\nSUMMARY:")
print(assistant.summarize())

print("\nKEY INFO:")
print(assistant.extract_key_info())
```

# 10) Search Assistants

Search assistants help users **find relevant information** from a large collection.

---

## Full code

```python
# search_assistant.py
# ==========================================
# Search assistant pattern
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class SearchAssistant:
    def __init__(self):
        self.knowledge_base = []

    def add_documents(self, documents):
        """
        Adds documents to search index.
        """
        for doc in documents:
            self.knowledge_base.append(doc)
        print(f"Added {len(documents)} documents")

    def search(self, query, top_k=3):
        """
        Finds most relevant documents.
        """
        query_words = query.lower().split()
        scored = []

        for doc in self.knowledge_base:
            score = sum(
                1 for word in query_words
                if word in doc["content"].lower()
            )
            if score > 0:
                scored.append((score, doc))

        scored.sort(reverse=True)
        return [doc for score, doc in scored[:top_k]]

    def smart_search(self, query):
        """
        Searches and generates a smart answer.
        """
        # Find relevant docs
        results = self.search(query)

        if not results:
            return {
                "answer": "No relevant documents found.",
                "sources": []
            }

        # Build context
        context = "\n".join([
            f"[{doc['title']}]: {doc['content']}"
            for doc in results
        ])

        # Generate answer
        prompt = f"""
Answer this question using the search results below.
Be concise and accurate.

Search results:
{context}

Question: {query}

Answer:
"""
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.1
        )

        answer = response.choices[0].message.content

        return {
            "answer": answer,
            "sources": [doc["title"] for doc in results]
        }


# Test search assistant
search = SearchAssistant()

# Add documents
search.add_documents([
    {
        "title": "Python Basics",
        "content": "Python is a programming language created in 1991."
    },
    {
        "title": "Python AI",
        "content": "Python is widely used in AI and machine learning."
    },
    {
        "title": "RAG Guide",
        "content": "RAG combines retrieval and generation for accurate AI answers."
    },
    {
        "title": "NumPy Guide",
        "content": "NumPy is used for numerical computing in Python."
    },
    {
        "title": "Pandas Guide",
        "content": "Pandas is used for data analysis and manipulation."
    },
])

# Search
queries = [
    "What is Python?",
    "How is Python used in AI?",
    "What is RAG?",
]

for query in queries:
    print(f"\nQuery: {query}")
    result = search.smart_search(query)
    print(f"Answer: {result['answer']}")
    print(f"Sources: {result['sources']}")
```

# Quick revision table

| Pattern | What it does | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Chatbot | Conversation with memory | Customer support bot |
| Q&A | Answer from documents | FAQ bot |
| Summarization | Shorten text | Article summary |
| Extraction | Pull specific data | Extract names/dates |
| Classification | Categorize text | Sentiment analysis |
| Translation | Convert language | English to Spanish |
| Content generation | Create new content | Blog posts, emails |
| Code assistant | Help with code | Generate, explain, debug |
| Document assistant | Interact with docs | Ask questions about PDF |
| Search assistant | Find relevant info | Smart search engine |

---

# Interview-ready one-line answers

## Chatbot
A conversational AI that maintains history and responds naturally to user messages.

## Q&A
A system that answers questions based on a specific knowledge base or document.

## Summarization
Condensing long text into shorter form while retaining key information.

## Extraction
Pulling specific structured information from unstructured text.

## Classification
Categorizing text into predefined groups like sentiment or topic.

## Translation
Converting text from one language to another using an LLM.

## Content generation
Using an LLM to create original content like blogs, emails, or posts.

## Code assistant
An AI tool that helps generate, explain, review, and debug code.

## Document assistant
An AI that allows users to interact with and query documents.

## Search assistant
A smart search system that retrieves relevant documents and generates answers.

## Copilot

Here's a **complete, simple, easy-to-revise guide on AI Agent Fundamentals**.

---

# Easy way to remember AI Agent

```
A chatbot TALKS
An AI agent THINKS + ACTS + REMEMBERS
```

---

# 1) What is an AI Agent?

An AI agent is a system that can:
- **think** about a problem
- **plan** steps to solve it
- **use tools** to take action
- **remember** what happened
- **work toward a goal** on its own

---

## Simple real-life example
```
You ask: "Research Python, write a summary, save it to a file"

Chatbot:
- Cannot do this
- Just replies with text

AI Agent:
- Step 1: Searches for Python info
- Step 2: Reads the results
- Step 3: Writes a summary
- Step 4: Saves to file
- Done!
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# what_is_agent.py
# ==========================================
# Simple AI Agent concept
# ==========================================

class SimpleAgent:
    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name
        self.memory = []
        self.tools = {}

    def add_tool(self, name, function):
        """Adds a tool the agent can use."""
        self.tools[name] = function
        print(f"Tool added: {name}")

    def think(self, task):
        """Agent thinks about what to do."""
        print(f"\nThinking about: {task}")
        return f"Plan to solve: {task}"

    def act(self, tool_name, input_data):
        """Agent uses a tool."""
        if tool_name in self.tools:
            result = self.tools[tool_name](input_data)
            self.memory.append({
                "tool": tool_name,
                "input": input_data,
                "result": result
            })
            return result
        return "Tool not found"

    def run(self, task):
        """
        Agent runs a task:
        Think → Plan → Act → Remember
        """
        print(f"\nAgent: {self.name}")
        print(f"Task: {task}")

        # Think
        plan = self.think(task)
        print(f"Plan: {plan}")

        # Act
        result = self.act("search", task)
        print(f"Result: {result}")

        return result


# Create agent
agent = SimpleAgent("MyAgent")

# Add tools
agent.add_tool("search", lambda q: f"Search results for: {q}")
agent.add_tool("calculator", lambda x: eval(x))
agent.add_tool("save", lambda t: f"Saved: {t}")

# Run task
agent.run("Find information about Python")
```

---

# 2) Agent vs Chatbot

```
CHATBOT                    AI AGENT
────────────────────────────────────
Just replies               Thinks + Acts
No tools                   Has tools
No planning                Plans steps
No autonomy                Works alone
Single response            Multi-step
Reactive only              Proactive
```

---

## Simple example

```python
# agent_vs_chatbot.py
# ==========================================
# Showing difference between chatbot
# and AI agent
# ==========================================

class Chatbot:
    def respond(self, message):
        """
        Chatbot just responds.
        No tools, no planning.
        """
        print(f"User: {message}")
        print(f"Chatbot: I understand you want to know about {message}")
        print("(Just replies, cannot take action)")


class AIAgent:
    def __init__(self):
        self.steps_taken = []

    def run(self, task):
        """
        Agent plans and executes steps.
        """
        print(f"\nUser: {task}")
        print("Agent thinking...")

        # Step 1: Plan
        steps = self.plan(task)
        print(f"Plan: {steps}")

        # Step 2: Execute each step
        for step in steps:
            result = self.execute(step)
            self.steps_taken.append(result)
            print(f"  ✓ {step}: Done")

        print(f"Agent: Task completed in {len(steps)} steps!")

    def plan(self, task):
        return [
            "Search for information",
            "Process the results",
            "Generate summary",
            "Save output"
        ]

    def execute(self, step):
        return f"Executed: {step}"


# Compare
task = "Research Python and save a summary"

print("=== CHATBOT ===")
bot = Chatbot()
bot.respond(task)

print("\n=== AI AGENT ===")
agent = AIAgent()
agent.run(task)
```

---

# 3) Agent Planning

Planning means the agent **breaks a big task into smaller steps**.

---

## Simple idea
```
Big task:
"Write a blog post about Python"

Agent plan:
Step 1: Research Python topics
Step 2: Create an outline
Step 3: Write introduction
Step 4: Write main content
Step 5: Write conclusion
Step 6: Review and save
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# agent_planning.py
# ==========================================
# Agent planning example
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class PlanningAgent:

    def create_plan(self, task):
        """
        Uses LLM to create a step-by-step plan.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Create a step-by-step plan for this task.
Return as numbered list.
Keep each step simple and clear.
Maximum 5 steps.

Task: {task}

Plan:
"""
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.3
        )

        plan_text = response.choices[0].message.content
        # Split into steps
        steps = [
            line.strip()
            for line in plan_text.split("\n")
            if line.strip()
        ]
        return steps

    def execute_plan(self, task):
        """
        Creates and executes a plan.
        """
        print(f"Task: {task}")
        print("\nCreating plan...")

        steps = self.create_plan(task)

        print(f"\nPlan ({len(steps)} steps):")
        for step in steps:
            print(f"  {step}")

        print("\nExecuting steps...")
        results = []

        for i, step in enumerate(steps, 1):
            print(f"  Step {i}: {step} → Done ✓")
            results.append(f"Step {i} completed")

        print("\nAll steps completed!")
        return results


# Test planning
agent = PlanningAgent()
agent.execute_plan(
    "Research and write a blog post about Python for beginners"
)
```

---

# 4) Tool Use

Tools are **functions the agent can call** to do real work.

---

## Common tools
```
calculator   → solve math
search       → find information
file_reader  → read files
file_writer  → save files
api_caller   → call external APIs
code_runner  → run code
email_sender → send emails
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# agent_tools.py
# ==========================================
# Agent tool use example
# ==========================================

import math
import datetime

class AgentTools:

    @staticmethod
    def calculator(expression):
        """Math calculator tool."""
        try:
            result = eval(expression)
            return f"Result: {result}"
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error: {e}"

    @staticmethod
    def get_current_time():
        """Gets current date and time."""
        now = datetime.datetime.now()
        return f"Current time: {now.strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')}"

    @staticmethod
    def search_knowledge(query, knowledge_base):
        """Searches knowledge base."""
        results = [
            doc for doc in knowledge_base
            if any(
                word in doc.lower()
                for word in query.lower().split()
            )
        ]
        return results[:3] if results else ["No results found"]

    @staticmethod
    def save_to_file(filename, content):
        """Saves content to file."""
        with open(filename, "w") as f:
            f.write(content)
        return f"Saved to {filename}"

    @staticmethod
    def word_counter(text):
        """Counts words in text."""
        count = len(text.split())
        return f"Word count: {count}"


class ToolAgent:
    def __init__(self):
        self.tools = AgentTools()
        self.tool_map = {
            "calculator": self.tools.calculator,
            "time": self.tools.get_current_time,
            "word_counter": self.tools.word_counter,
        }

    def use_tool(self, tool_name, *args):
        """Uses a specific tool."""
        if tool_name in self.tool_map:
            print(f"Using tool: {tool_name}")
            result = self.tool_map[tool_name](*args)
            print(f"Tool result: {result}")
            return result
        return "Tool not found"


# Test tools
agent = ToolAgent()

print("=== TOOL USE ===")
agent.use_tool("calculator", "25 * 4 + 10")
agent.use_tool("time")
agent.use_tool("word_counter", "Python is a great language for AI")
```

---

# 5) Decision Making

Decision making means the agent **chooses what to do next** based on the situation.

---

## Simple idea
```
User asks question
    ↓
Agent decides:
  - Do I need to search?
  - Do I need to calculate?
  - Do I need to read a file?
  - Can I answer directly?
    ↓
Takes the right action
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# agent_decision.py
# ==========================================
# Agent decision making example
# ==========================================

class DecisionAgent:

    def decide_action(self, user_input):
        """
        Decides what action to take
        based on user input.
        """
        user_lower = user_input.lower()

        # Decision rules
        if any(word in user_lower for word in
               ["calculate", "math", "+", "-", "*", "/"]):
            return "calculator"

        elif any(word in user_lower for word in
                 ["search", "find", "what is", "tell me"]):
            return "search"

        elif any(word in user_lower for word in
                 ["save", "write", "store"]):
            return "save"

        elif any(word in user_lower for word in
                 ["time", "date", "today"]):
            return "get_time"

        else:
            return "direct_answer"

    def execute_decision(self, user_input):
        """
        Makes decision and executes action.
        """
        print(f"\nUser: {user_input}")

        action = self.decide_action(user_input)
        print(f"Decision: Use {action}")

        if action == "calculator":
            print("Action: Running calculator...")
        elif action == "search":
            print("Action: Searching knowledge base...")
        elif action == "save":
            print("Action: Saving to file...")
        elif action == "get_time":
            print("Action: Getting current time...")
        else:
            print("Action: Answering directly...")


# Test decisions
agent = DecisionAgent()

inputs = [
    "Calculate 25 * 4",
    "What is Python?",
    "Save this note",
    "What is today's date?",
    "Hello!"
]

for inp in inputs:
    agent.execute_decision(inp)
```

---

# 6) Memory

Memory lets the agent **remember past actions and conversations**.

---

## Types of memory
```
SHORT-TERM  → current conversation only
LONG-TERM   → saved permanently
EPISODIC    → remembers specific events
SEMANTIC    → stores facts and knowledge
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# agent_memory.py
# ==========================================
# Agent memory example
# ==========================================

import json
import datetime

class AgentMemory:

    def __init__(self):
        # Short-term: current session only
        self.short_term = []
        # Long-term: saved facts
        self.long_term = {}

    def remember_short(self, role, content):
        """
        Saves to short-term memory.
        Forgets after session ends.
        """
        self.short_term.append({
            "role": role,
            "content": content,
            "time": datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()
        })
        # Keep only last 10 messages
        if len(self.short_term) > 10:
            self.short_term.pop(0)

    def remember_long(self, key, value):
        """
        Saves to long-term memory.
        Persists across sessions.
        """
        self.long_term[key] = {
            "value": value,
            "saved_at": datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()
        }
        print(f"Saved to long-term memory: {key}")

    def recall_short(self):
        """Gets recent conversation."""
        return self.short_term

    def recall_long(self, key):
        """Gets a saved fact."""
        return self.long_term.get(key, {}).get("value", None)

    def save_to_file(self, filename):
        """Saves long-term memory to file."""
        with open(filename, "w") as f:
            json.dump(self.long_term, f, indent=2)
        print(f"Memory saved to {filename}")

    def load_from_file(self, filename):
        """Loads long-term memory from file."""
        try:
            with open(filename, "r") as f:
                self.long_term = json.load(f)
            print(f"Memory loaded from {filename}")
        except FileNotFoundError:
            print("No saved memory found")

    def show_memory(self):
        """Shows all memory."""
        print(f"\nShort-term ({len(self.short_term)} messages):")
        for msg in self.short_term:
            print(f"  {msg['role']}: {msg['content']}")

        print(f"\nLong-term ({len(self.long_term)} facts):")
        for key, val in self.long_term.items():
            print(f"  {key}: {val['value']}")


# Test memory
memory = AgentMemory()

# Short-term memory
memory.remember_short("user", "My name is Aman")
memory.remember_short("assistant", "Hello Aman!")
memory.remember_short("user", "I like Python")
memory.remember_short("assistant", "Great choice!")

# Long-term memory
memory.remember_long("user_name", "Aman")
memory.remember_long("user_interest", "Python")
memory.remember_long("last_topic", "AI agents")

# Recall
print("User name:", memory.recall_long("user_name"))
print("User interest:", memory.recall_long("user_interest"))

# Show all memory
memory.show_memory()
```

---

# 7) Reflection

Reflection means the agent **reviews its own actions** and improves.

---

## Simple idea
```
Agent takes action
    ↓
Agent checks:
  - Was it correct?
  - Was it complete?
  - Can it be improved?
    ↓
Agent improves response
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# agent_reflection.py
# ==========================================
# Agent reflection example
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class ReflectiveAgent:

    def generate_answer(self, question):
        """First attempt at answering."""
        prompt = f"Answer this question: {question}"
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.7
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content

    def reflect(self, question, answer):
        """
        Reviews the answer and improves it.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Review this answer and improve it.

Question: {question}
Answer: {answer}

Check:
1. Is it accurate?
2. Is it complete?
3. Is it clear?

Provide an improved answer.

Improved answer:
"""
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.3
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content

    def run_with_reflection(self, question):
        """
        Answers and then reflects to improve.
        """
        print(f"Question: {question}")

        # First answer
        print("\nGenerating initial answer...")
        first_answer = self.generate_answer(question)
        print(f"Initial: {first_answer}")

        # Reflect and improve
        print("\nReflecting on answer...")
        improved_answer = self.reflect(question, first_answer)
        print(f"Improved: {improved_answer}")

        return improved_answer


# Test reflection
agent = ReflectiveAgent()
agent.run_with_reflection("What is RAG in AI?")
```

---

# 8) Multi-step Reasoning

Multi-step reasoning means the agent **thinks through multiple steps** to reach an answer.

---

## Simple idea
```
Simple question:
"What is 2+2?" → Direct answer

Multi-step question:
"If Python has 50 libraries and I use 20%,
how many am I using and how many are left?"

Step 1: Calculate 20% of 50 = 10
Step 2: Subtract 10 from 50 = 40
Step 3: Answer = using 10, left = 40
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# multi_step_reasoning.py
# ==========================================
# Multi-step reasoning example
# ==========================================

from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class MultiStepAgent:

    def reason(self, problem):
        """
        Uses chain-of-thought reasoning.
        Thinks step by step.
        """
        prompt = f"""
Solve this problem step by step.
Show your thinking for each step.
At the end, give the final answer.

Problem: {problem}

Let me think step by step:
"""
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}],
            temperature=0.1
        )
        return response.choices[0].message.content

    def multi_step_task(self, task):
        """
        Breaks complex task into steps
        and executes each one.
        """
        print(f"Complex task: {task}")

        # Step 1: Break into sub-tasks
        breakdown_prompt = f"""
Break this task into clear sub-tasks.
Return as numbered list.
Maximum 5 sub-tasks.

Task: {task}
"""
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[{"role": "user", "content": breakdown_prompt}],
            temperature=0.1
        )

        subtasks = response.choices[0].message.content
        print(f"\nSub-tasks:\n{subtasks}")

        # Step 2: Execute each sub-task
        print("\nExecuting sub-tasks...")
        results = []

        for i, line in enumerate(subtasks.split("\n"), 1):
            if line.strip():
                print(f"  ✓ Executing: {line.strip()}")
                results.append(line.strip())

        print("\nAll steps completed!")
        return results


# Test multi-step reasoning
agent = MultiStepAgent()

print("=== STEP BY STEP REASONING ===")
answer = agent.reason(
    "A store has 100 Python books. They sell 30% on Monday "
    "and 20% of the remaining on Tuesday. How many are left?"
)
print(answer)
```

---

# 9) Goal-oriented Behavior

Goal-oriented means the agent **keeps working until the goal is achieved**.

---

## Simple idea
```
Normal chatbot:
User asks → Bot replies → Done

Goal-oriented agent:
User sets goal → Agent works → Checks progress
→ Continues until goal is done
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# goal_oriented.py
# ==========================================
# Goal-oriented agent example
# ==========================================

class GoalOrientedAgent:

    def __init__(self):
        self.goal = None
        self.completed_steps = []
        self.is_goal_achieved = False

    def set_goal(self, goal):
        """Sets the goal."""
        self.goal = goal
        self.is_goal_achieved = False
        self.completed_steps = []
        print(f"Goal set: {goal}")

    def check_goal(self):
        """Checks if goal is achieved."""
        required_steps = 3
        if len(self.completed_steps) >= required_steps:
            self.is_goal_achieved = True
        return self.is_goal_achieved

    def take_action(self, step_number):
        """Takes one action toward goal."""
        actions = {
            1: "Gathering information",
            2: "Processing data",
            3: "Generating output",
            4: "Reviewing result",
            5: "Finalizing"
        }
        action = actions.get(step_number, "Working...")
        self.completed_steps.append(action)
        print(f"  Step {step_number}: {action} ✓")
        return action

    def run_until_goal(self):
        """
        Keeps running until goal is achieved.
        """
        if not self.goal:
            print("No goal set!")
            return

        print(f"\nWorking toward goal: {self.goal}")
        step = 1

        while not self.is_goal_achieved:
            self.take_action(step)
            self.check_goal()
            step += 1

            # Safety limit
            if step > 10:
                print("Max steps reached")
                break

        if self.is_goal_achieved:
            print(f"\nGoal achieved: {self.goal}")
            print(f"Steps taken: {len(self.completed_steps)}")


# Test goal-oriented agent
agent = GoalOrientedAgent()
agent.set_goal("Write and save a Python tutorial")
agent.run_until_goal()
```

---

# 10) Autonomous Workflows

Autonomous workflows means the agent **runs a full workflow on its own** without human help at each step.

---

## Simple idea
```
Human starts task → Agent runs everything → Human gets result

No need to supervise each step.
```

---

## Full code

```python
# autonomous_workflow.py
# ==========================================
# Autonomous workflow agent
# ==========================================

import datetime

class AutonomousAgent:

    def __init__(self, name):
        self.name = name
        self.memory = []
        self.logs = []

    def log(self, message):
        """Logs agent activity."""
        timestamp = datetime.datetime.now().strftime("%H:%M:%S")
        log_entry = f"[{timestamp}] {message}"
        self.logs.append(log_entry)
        print(f"  {log_entry}")

    def search(self, query):
        """Simulated search tool."""
        self.log(f"Searching for: {query}")
        return f"Search results for {query}: Found relevant information"

    def summarize(self, text):
        """Simulated summarize tool."""
        self.log(f"Summarizing text...")
        return f"Summary: Key points from {text[:30]}..."

    def save(self, filename, content):
        """Simulated save tool."""
        self.log(f"Saving to {filename}...")
        return f"Saved successfully to {filename}"

    def send_report(self, report):
        """Simulated report sender."""
        self.log("Sending report...")
        return "Report sent successfully"

    def run_workflow(self, goal):
        """
        Runs complete workflow autonomously.
        No human intervention needed.
        """
        print(f"\n{'='*50}")
        print(f"Agent: {self.name}")
        print(f"Goal: {goal}")
        print(f"{'='*50}")
        print("Starting autonomous workflow...\n")

        # Step 1: Search
        search_result = self.search(goal)
        self.memory.append(search_result)

        # Step 2: Summarize
        summary = self.summarize(search_result)
        self.memory.append(summary)

        # Step 3: Save
        save_result = self.save("output.txt", summary)
        self.memory.append(save_result)

        # Step 4: Send report
        report = f"Completed: {goal}\nSummary: {summary}"
        send_result = self.send_report(report)

        # Step 5: Show completion
        print(f"\n{'='*50}")
        print("WORKFLOW COMPLETED!")
        print(f"Steps taken: {len(self.logs)}")
        print(f"Goal achieved: {goal}")
        print(f"{'='*50}")

        return {
            "goal": goal,
            "steps": len(self.logs),
            "status": "completed",
            "summary": summary
        }

    def show_logs(self):
        """Shows all agent logs."""
        print("\nAgent Logs:")
        for log in self.logs:
            print(f"  {log}")


# Test autonomous workflow
agent = AutonomousAgent("ResearchBot")
result = agent.run_workflow(
    "Research Python AI frameworks and create a summary report"
)

print("\nFinal Result:")
for key, value in result.items():
    print(f"  {key}: {value}")

agent.show_logs()
```

# Quick revision sheet

```
WHAT IS AGENT   → thinks + plans + acts + remembers
AGENT VS CHATBOT→ chatbot talks, agent acts
PLANNING        → breaks big task into steps
TOOL USE        → calculator, search, save, API
DECISION MAKING → chooses right tool for task
MEMORY          → short-term + long-term
REFLECTION      → reviews and improves own work
MULTI-STEP      → thinks through many steps
GOAL-ORIENTED   → keeps working until done
AUTONOMOUS      → runs full workflow alone
```

# Interview-ready one-line answers

## What is an AI agent?
An AI agent is a system that uses an LLM to plan, make decisions, use tools, and autonomously complete tasks.

## Agent vs chatbot?
A chatbot only replies to messages. An agent plans, uses tools, and takes actions to complete goals.

## What is agent planning?
Breaking a complex task into smaller executable steps.

## What is tool use?
The agent's ability to call external functions like search, calculator, or file operations.

## What is memory in agents?
Short-term memory stores current conversation. Long-term memory stores facts across sessions.

## What is reflection?
The agent reviewing and improving its own responses or actions.

## What is multi-step reasoning?
Thinking through a problem in multiple logical steps to reach the correct answer.

## What is autonomous workflow?
An agent completing a full task from start to finish without human intervention at each step.
