## Copilot

Here's a **complete, simple, easy-to-revise guide on async/await in Python**.

---

# Easy way to remember async/await

```
NORMAL CODE:
Task 1 → wait → Task 2 → wait → Task 3
(slow, one by one)

ASYNC CODE:
Task 1 start → Task 2 start → Task 3 start
All run together → All finish faster
```

---

# 1) What is async/await?

`async/await` is a way to run **multiple tasks at the same time** without waiting for each one to finish.

---

## Real life example
```
NORMAL (sync):
Make tea    → wait 3 min
Make coffee → wait 3 min
Make juice  → wait 3 min
Total = 9 minutes

ASYNC:
Start tea + Start coffee + Start juice
All together → wait 3 min
Total = 3 minutes
```

---

## Simple code comparison

```python
# sync_vs_async.py
# ==========================================
# Comparing sync vs async
# ==========================================

import asyncio
import time

# ==========================================
# SYNCHRONOUS (normal) - slow
# ==========================================
def sync_task(name, seconds):
    print(f"Starting {name}")
    time.sleep(seconds)          # blocks everything
    print(f"Done {name}")

def sync_main():
    start = time.time()

    sync_task("Task 1", 2)
    sync_task("Task 2", 2)
    sync_task("Task 3", 2)

    end = time.time()
    print(f"Sync total time: {end - start:.1f} seconds")

# ==========================================
# ASYNCHRONOUS (async) - fast
# ==========================================
async def async_task(name, seconds):
    print(f"Starting {name}")
    await asyncio.sleep(seconds)  # does NOT block
    print(f"Done {name}")

async def async_main():
    start = time.time()

    # Run all tasks together
    await asyncio.gather(
        async_task("Task 1", 2),
        async_task("Task 2", 2),
        async_task("Task 3", 2)
    )

    end = time.time()
    print(f"Async total time: {end - start:.1f} seconds")


# Run sync
print("=== SYNC ===")
sync_main()

# Run async
print("\n=== ASYNC ===")
asyncio.run(async_main())
```

### Output
```
=== SYNC ===
Starting Task 1
Done Task 1
Starting Task 2
Done Task 2
Starting Task 3
Done Task 3
Sync total time: 6.0 seconds

=== ASYNC ===
Starting Task 1
Starting Task 2
Starting Task 3
Done Task 1
Done Task 2
Done Task 3
Async total time: 2.0 seconds
```

---

# 2) Basic keywords

## `async def`
Makes a function **asynchronous**.

## `await`
Pauses current task and **lets other tasks run**.

## `asyncio.run()`
Starts the **event loop** and runs async function.

## `asyncio.gather()`
Runs **multiple async tasks together**.

---

## Simple example

```python
# basic_async.py
# ==========================================
# Basic async/await keywords
# ==========================================

import asyncio

# async def = asynchronous function
async def say_hello():
    print("Hello")
    await asyncio.sleep(1)   # await = pause here
    print("World")

# Run it
asyncio.run(say_hello())
```

### Output
```
Hello
World
```

---

# 3) How event loop works

```
EVENT LOOP is like a manager:

Task 1 starts → hits await → pauses
Event loop picks Task 2
Task 2 starts → hits await → pauses
Event loop picks Task 3
Task 3 starts → hits await → pauses
Task 1 ready → resumes
Task 2 ready → resumes
Task 3 ready → resumes
```

---

## Simple code

```python
# event_loop.py
# ==========================================
# Understanding event loop
# ==========================================

import asyncio

async def task(name, delay):
    print(f"{name}: Started")
    await asyncio.sleep(delay)
    print(f"{name}: Finished after {delay}s")
    return f"{name} done"

async def main():
    print("Event loop started\n")

    # Run tasks concurrently
    results = await asyncio.gather(
        task("A", 3),
        task("B", 1),
        task("C", 2)
    )

    print(f"\nAll results: {results}")

asyncio.run(main())
```

### Output
```
Event loop started

A: Started
B: Started
C: Started
B: Finished after 1s
C: Finished after 2s
A: Finished after 3s

All results: ['A done', 'B done', 'C done']
```

---

# 4) asyncio.gather()

`gather()` runs **multiple tasks at same time** and waits for all to finish.

---

## Simple code

```python
# asyncio_gather.py
# ==========================================
# asyncio.gather() example
# ==========================================

import asyncio

async def fetch_data(source, delay):
    """Simulates fetching data from a source."""
    print(f"Fetching from {source}...")
    await asyncio.sleep(delay)
    print(f"Got data from {source}")
    return f"Data from {source}"

async def main():

    # Run all fetches at the same time
    results = await asyncio.gather(
        fetch_data("Database", 3),
        fetch_data("API", 1),
        fetch_data("Cache", 0.5),
    )

    print("\nAll data received:")
    for result in results:
        print(f"  - {result}")

asyncio.run(main())
```

### Output
```
Fetching from Database...
Fetching from API...
Fetching from Cache...
Got data from Cache
Got data from API
Got data from Database

All data received:
  - Data from Database
  - Data from API
  - Data from Cache
```

---

# 5) asyncio.create_task()

`create_task()` starts a task **immediately in background**.

---

## Simple code

```python
# create_task.py
# ==========================================
# asyncio.create_task() example
# ==========================================

import asyncio

async def background_task(name, delay):
    await asyncio.sleep(delay)
    print(f"Background task done: {name}")
    return name

async def main():

    print("Creating tasks...")

    # Create tasks - they start immediately
    task1 = asyncio.create_task(
        background_task("Task1", 2)
    )
    task2 = asyncio.create_task(
        background_task("Task2", 1)
    )
    task3 = asyncio.create_task(
        background_task("Task3", 3)
    )

    print("Tasks created, doing other work...")
    await asyncio.sleep(0.1)
    print("Still doing other work...")

    # Wait for all tasks
    results = await asyncio.gather(task1, task2, task3)
    print(f"\nAll tasks done: {results}")

asyncio.run(main())
```

---

# 6) async/await with AI API calls

Most useful in AI apps when calling **multiple LLM APIs at once**.

---

## Simple code

```python
# async_ai_calls.py
# ==========================================
# Async AI API calls example
# ==========================================

import asyncio
from openai import AsyncOpenAI

# AsyncOpenAI = async version of OpenAI client
client = AsyncOpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

async def ask_llm(question):
    """
    Calls LLM asynchronously.
    Does not block other calls.
    """
    print(f"Asking: {question[:30]}...")

    response = await client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=[
            {"role": "user", "content": question}
        ]
    )

    answer = response.choices[0].message.content
    print(f"Got answer for: {question[:30]}...")
    return answer

async def ask_multiple():
    """
    Asks multiple questions at same time.
    Much faster than one by one.
    """
    questions = [
        "What is Python?",
        "What is RAG?",
        "What is an AI agent?",
        "What are embeddings?",
        "What is a vector database?",
    ]

    print(f"Asking {len(questions)} questions concurrently...\n")

    # All questions asked at same time
    answers = await asyncio.gather(
        *[ask_llm(q) for q in questions]
    )

    print("\nAll answers received!")
    for q, a in zip(questions, answers):
        print(f"\nQ: {q}")
        print(f"A: {a[:100]}...")

asyncio.run(ask_multiple())
```

---

# 7) async with (Async Context Manager)

Used for **resources that need async open/close**.

---

## Simple code

```python
# async_context.py
# ==========================================
# Async context manager example
# ==========================================

import asyncio
import aiohttp       # pip install aiohttp

async def fetch_url(session, url):
    """
    Fetches a URL asynchronously.
    """
    async with session.get(url) as response:
        # async with = async context manager
        status = response.status
        print(f"URL: {url} → Status: {status}")
        return status

async def fetch_multiple_urls():
    """
    Fetches multiple URLs at once.
    """
    urls = [
        "https://httpbin.org/get",
        "https://httpbin.org/status/200",
        "https://httpbin.org/status/404",
    ]

    # async with = opens session asynchronously
    async with aiohttp.ClientSession() as session:
        results = await asyncio.gather(
            *[fetch_url(session, url) for url in urls]
        )

    print(f"\nAll statuses: {results}")

asyncio.run(fetch_multiple_urls())
```

---

# 8) async for (Async Iterator)

Used for **iterating over async streams**.

---

## Simple code

```python
# async_for.py
# ==========================================
# Async for loop example
# ==========================================

import asyncio

async def async_data_stream():
    """
    Simulates async data stream.
    Like reading from API or database.
    """
    data = ["item1", "item2", "item3", "item4", "item5"]
    for item in data:
        await asyncio.sleep(0.5)
        yield item             # async generator

async def process_stream():
    """
    Processes items as they arrive.
    """
    print("Processing stream...")

    # async for = iterate async generator
    async for item in async_data_stream():
        print(f"  Received: {item}")

    print("Stream complete!")

asyncio.run(process_stream())
```

---

# 9) Error handling in async

```python
# async_error_handling.py
# ==========================================
# Error handling in async code
# ==========================================

import asyncio

async def risky_task(name, should_fail=False):
    """
    Task that might fail.
    """
    await asyncio.sleep(1)

    if should_fail:
        raise ValueError(f"Task {name} failed!")

    return f"{name} succeeded"

async def safe_task(name, should_fail=False):
    """
    Task with error handling.
    """
    try:
        result = await risky_task(name, should_fail)
        return result
    except ValueError as e:
        print(f"Error caught: {e}")
        return f"{name} failed safely"

async def main():

    # Run tasks - some may fail
    results = await asyncio.gather(
        safe_task("Task1", should_fail=False),
        safe_task("Task2", should_fail=True),
        safe_task("Task3", should_fail=False),
        return_exceptions=True   # don't stop on error
    )

    print("\nResults:")
    for r in results:
        print(f"  - {r}")

asyncio.run(main())
```

---

# 10) Timeout in async

```python
# async_timeout.py
# ==========================================
# Timeout handling in async
# ==========================================

import asyncio

async def slow_task():
    """Task that takes too long."""
    print("Slow task started...")
    await asyncio.sleep(10)    # takes 10 seconds
    return "Done"

async def fast_task():
    """Task that is fast."""
    print("Fast task started...")
    await asyncio.sleep(1)
    return "Fast done"

async def main():

    # Timeout example
    try:
        # Wait max 3 seconds
        result = await asyncio.wait_for(
            slow_task(),
            timeout=3.0
        )
        print(result)

    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        print("Task timed out after 3 seconds!")

    # Fast task works fine
    try:
        result = await asyncio.wait_for(
            fast_task(),
            timeout=3.0
        )
        print(result)

    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        print("This should not timeout")

asyncio.run(main())
```

---

# 11) Full async AI app example

```python
# full_async_ai_app.py
# ==========================================
# Full async AI application
# ==========================================

import asyncio
import time
from openai import AsyncOpenAI

client = AsyncOpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

class AsyncAIApp:

    def __init__(self):
        self.results = []

    async def call_llm(self, prompt, task_name):
        """
        Single async LLM call.
        """
        try:
            print(f"  Starting: {task_name}")
            response = await asyncio.wait_for(
                client.chat.completions.create(
                    model="gpt-4",
                    messages=[
                        {"role": "user", "content": prompt}
                    ],
                    max_tokens=100
                ),
                timeout=30.0
            )
            answer = response.choices[0].message.content
            print(f"  Done: {task_name}")
            return {"task": task_name, "answer": answer}

        except asyncio.TimeoutError:
            return {"task": task_name, "answer": "Timeout"}
        except Exception as e:
            return {"task": task_name, "answer": f"Error: {e}"}

    async def run_all_tasks(self, tasks):
        """
        Runs all tasks concurrently.
        """
        print(f"Running {len(tasks)} tasks concurrently...\n")
        start = time.time()

        # Run all at same time
        results = await asyncio.gather(
            *[self.call_llm(prompt, name)
              for name, prompt in tasks.items()]
        )

        end = time.time()
        print(f"\nAll done in {end - start:.1f} seconds")
        return results

    def show_results(self, results):
        """Shows all results."""
        print("\n=== RESULTS ===")
        for result in results:
            print(f"\nTask: {result['task']}")
            print(f"Answer: {result['answer'][:100]}...")


async def main():
    app = AsyncAIApp()

    # Multiple AI tasks
    tasks = {
        "Summarize Python":
            "Summarize Python in one sentence",
        "Explain RAG":
            "Explain RAG in one sentence",
        "Define Agent":
            "Define AI agent in one sentence",
        "What is LLM":
            "What is an LLM in one sentence",
        "Explain Embedding":
            "What is an embedding in one sentence",
    }

    results = await app.run_all_tasks(tasks)
    app.show_results(results)

asyncio.run(main())
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
async def     → makes function async
await         → pause and let others run
asyncio.run() → starts event loop
asyncio.gather() → run many tasks together
asyncio.create_task() → start task in background
asyncio.wait_for()   → add timeout
async with    → async context manager
async for     → async loop

SYNC  = one by one = slow
ASYNC = all together = fast

Best for:
- multiple API calls
- network requests
- file operations
- database queries
```

---

# Interview-ready one-line answers

## What is async/await?
A way to run multiple I/O tasks concurrently without blocking the program.

## What is the event loop?
The event loop manages and switches between async tasks efficiently.

## What is asyncio.gather()?
It runs multiple async tasks at the same time and waits for all to finish.

## When should you use async?
When making multiple API calls, network requests, or I/O operations that involve waiting.

## Difference between sync and async?
Sync runs tasks one by one. Async runs tasks concurrently, making better use of waiting time.

# What is FastAPI?

FastAPI is a modern, fast, and easy-to-use Python web framework used to build APIs. It was created by Sebastián Ramírez and is built on top of two powerful libraries — Starlette for the web parts and Pydantic for data validation. FastAPI is one of the fastest Python frameworks available, almost as fast as NodeJS and Go. It automatically generates interactive API documentation using Swagger UI, which means you can test your API directly from the browser without writing any extra code. FastAPI uses Python type hints to validate request and response data automatically, which reduces bugs and saves development time. It also has built-in support for async/await, making it perfect for building AI applications, chatbots, and LLM-powered APIs. Companies use FastAPI to build production-ready APIs quickly because it combines speed, simplicity, and powerful features in one package.

---

# 1) Basic FastAPI app

```python
# main.py
# ==========================================
# Basic FastAPI application
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI

# Create FastAPI app
app = FastAPI(
    title="My First API",
    description="Learning FastAPI",
    version="1.0.0"
)

# Root endpoint
@app.get("/")
def home():
    return {"message": "Welcome to FastAPI!"}

# Simple endpoint
@app.get("/hello")
def hello():
    return {"message": "Hello World"}

# Endpoint with name
@app.get("/hello/{name}")
def hello_name(name: str):
    return {"message": f"Hello {name}!"}
```

# 2) HTTP Methods

```python
# http_methods.py
# ==========================================
# GET, POST, PUT, DELETE examples
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI
from pydantic import BaseModel
from typing import Optional

app = FastAPI()

# Fake database
items_db = {}

# Pydantic model for validation
class Item(BaseModel):
    name: str
    price: float
    description: Optional[str] = None

# ==========================================
# GET - Read data
# ==========================================
@app.get("/items")
def get_all_items():
    """Get all items."""
    return {"items": items_db}

@app.get("/items/{item_id}")
def get_item(item_id: int):
    """Get one item by ID."""
    if item_id not in items_db:
        return {"error": "Item not found"}
    return {"item": items_db[item_id]}

# ==========================================
# POST - Create data
# ==========================================
@app.post("/items/{item_id}")
def create_item(item_id: int, item: Item):
    """Create a new item."""
    if item_id in items_db:
        return {"error": "Item already exists"}
    items_db[item_id] = item
    return {"message": "Item created", "item": item}

# ==========================================
# PUT - Update data
# ==========================================
@app.put("/items/{item_id}")
def update_item(item_id: int, item: Item):
    """Update an existing item."""
    if item_id not in items_db:
        return {"error": "Item not found"}
    items_db[item_id] = item
    return {"message": "Item updated", "item": item}

# ==========================================
# DELETE - Delete data
# ==========================================
@app.delete("/items/{item_id}")
def delete_item(item_id: int):
    """Delete an item."""
    if item_id not in items_db:
        return {"error": "Item not found"}
    del items_db[item_id]
    return {"message": "Item deleted"}
```

# 3) Query Parameters

```python
# query_params.py
# ==========================================
# Query parameters example
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI
from typing import Optional

app = FastAPI()

products = [
    {"id": 1, "name": "Python Book", "category": "books", "price": 500},
    {"id": 2, "name": "AI Course", "category": "courses", "price": 1000},
    {"id": 3, "name": "JS Book", "category": "books", "price": 400},
    {"id": 4, "name": "ML Course", "category": "courses", "price": 1500},
    {"id": 5, "name": "Flask Book", "category": "books", "price": 600},
]

@app.get("/products")
def get_products(
    category: Optional[str] = None,
    min_price: Optional[float] = None,
    max_price: Optional[float] = None,
    limit: int = 10
):
    """
    Get products with filters.
    Example: /products?category=books&min_price=400&limit=2
    """
    result = products

    # Filter by category
    if category:
        result = [p for p in result if p["category"] == category]

    # Filter by min price
    if min_price:
        result = [p for p in result if p["price"] >= min_price]

    # Filter by max price
    if max_price:
        result = [p for p in result if p["price"] <= max_price]

    # Limit results
    result = result[:limit]

    return {
        "total": len(result),
        "products": result
    }
```

### Test URLs
```
/products
/products?category=books
/products?min_price=500
/products?category=books&max_price=500
/products?limit=2
```

# 4) Request Body and Pydantic

```python
# pydantic_models.py
# ==========================================
# Pydantic models for data validation
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI
from pydantic import BaseModel, EmailStr, validator
from typing import Optional, List
from datetime import datetime

app = FastAPI()

# ==========================================
# Pydantic models
# ==========================================

class Address(BaseModel):
    street: str
    city: str
    country: str

class User(BaseModel):
    name: str
    age: int
    email: str
    address: Optional[Address] = None
    skills: List[str] = []

    # Custom validator
    @validator("age")
    def age_must_be_valid(cls, v):
        if v < 0 or v > 120:
            raise ValueError("Age must be between 0 and 120")
        return v

    @validator("name")
    def name_must_not_be_empty(cls, v):
        if not v.strip():
            raise ValueError("Name cannot be empty")
        return v


class UserResponse(BaseModel):
    id: int
    name: str
    email: str
    created_at: datetime


# Fake user database
users_db = {}
user_counter = 1

@app.post("/users", response_model=UserResponse)
def create_user(user: User):
    """
    Creates a new user.
    Pydantic validates the data automatically.
    """
    global user_counter

    new_user = {
        "id": user_counter,
        "name": user.name,
        "email": user.email,
        "created_at": datetime.now()
    }

    users_db[user_counter] = {**user.dict(), **new_user}
    user_counter += 1

    return new_user

@app.get("/users/{user_id}")
def get_user(user_id: int):
    if user_id not in users_db:
        return {"error": "User not found"}
    return users_db[user_id]

@app.get("/users")
def get_all_users():
    return {"users": list(users_db.values())}
```

---

# 5) Status Codes and Error Handling

```python
# error_handling.py
# ==========================================
# Status codes and error handling
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException, status
from pydantic import BaseModel
from typing import Optional

app = FastAPI()

class Product(BaseModel):
    name: str
    price: float
    stock: int

products_db = {
    1: {"name": "Python Book", "price": 500, "stock": 10},
    2: {"name": "AI Course", "price": 1000, "stock": 5},
}

@app.get("/products/{product_id}")
def get_product(product_id: int):
    """
    Returns product or raises 404 error.
    """
    if product_id not in products_db:
        # Raise HTTP exception
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND,
            detail=f"Product {product_id} not found"
        )
    return products_db[product_id]

@app.post(
    "/products/{product_id}",
    status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED
)
def create_product(product_id: int, product: Product):
    """
    Creates product, returns 201 on success.
    """
    if product_id in products_db:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST,
            detail="Product already exists"
        )

    if product.price < 0:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=status.HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY,
            detail="Price cannot be negative"
        )

    products_db[product_id] = product.dict()
    return {
        "message": "Product created successfully",
        "product": product
    }

@app.delete("/products/{product_id}")
def delete_product(product_id: int):
    if product_id not in products_db:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Product not found"
        )
    del products_db[product_id]
    return {"message": "Product deleted"}
```

# 6) Middleware and CORS

```python
# middleware.py
# ==========================================
# Middleware and CORS example
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI, Request
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware
import time
import logging

logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO)
logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

app = FastAPI()

# ==========================================
# CORS Middleware
# Allows frontend to call your API
# ==========================================
app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=["*"],        # Allow all origins
    allow_credentials=True,
    allow_methods=["*"],        # Allow all methods
    allow_headers=["*"],        # Allow all headers
)

# ==========================================
# Custom middleware - logs all requests
# ==========================================
@app.middleware("http")
async def log_requests(request: Request, call_next):
    """
    Runs before and after every request.
    """
    start = time.time()

    # Log incoming request
    logger.info(f"Request: {request.method} {request.url}")

    # Process request
    response = await call_next(request)

    # Log response time
    end = time.time()
    logger.info(
        f"Response: {response.status_code} "
        f"in {(end-start)*1000:.1f}ms"
    )

    return response

@app.get("/")
def home():
    return {"message": "Home page"}

@app.get("/about")
def about():
    return {"message": "About page"}
```

# 7) Async FastAPI

```python
# async_fastapi.py
# ==========================================
# Async FastAPI endpoints
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI
import asyncio
from openai import AsyncOpenAI

app = FastAPI()
client = AsyncOpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

# ==========================================
# Async endpoint
# ==========================================
@app.get("/async-hello")
async def async_hello():
    """Async endpoint."""
    await asyncio.sleep(1)
    return {"message": "Async Hello!"}

# ==========================================
# Async LLM endpoint
# ==========================================
@app.post("/ask")
async def ask_ai(question: str):
    """
    Calls LLM asynchronously.
    """
    response = await client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=[
            {"role": "user", "content": question}
        ]
    )
    answer = response.choices[0].message.content
    return {"question": question, "answer": answer}

# ==========================================
# Multiple async operations
# ==========================================
@app.get("/dashboard")
async def get_dashboard():
    """
    Gets multiple data sources concurrently.
    """
    async def get_users():
        await asyncio.sleep(1)
        return ["User1", "User2"]

    async def get_products():
        await asyncio.sleep(1)
        return ["Product1", "Product2"]

    async def get_stats():
        await asyncio.sleep(1)
        return {"total": 100}

    # All run at same time
    users, products, stats = await asyncio.gather(
        get_users(),
        get_products(),
        get_stats()
    )

    return {
        "users": users,
        "products": products,
        "stats": stats
    }
```

---

# 8) Full AI API with FastAPI

```python
# ai_api.py
# ==========================================
# Full AI API using FastAPI
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException
from pydantic import BaseModel
from typing import Optional, List
from openai import AsyncOpenAI
import asyncio

app = FastAPI(
    title="AI Assistant API",
    description="FastAPI + OpenAI",
    version="1.0.0"
)

client = AsyncOpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

# ==========================================
# Models
# ==========================================
class ChatRequest(BaseModel):
    message: str
    system_prompt: Optional[str] = "You are a helpful assistant"
    temperature: Optional[float] = 0.7

class ChatResponse(BaseModel):
    message: str
    answer: str
    tokens_used: int

class SummarizeRequest(BaseModel):
    text: str
    max_sentences: Optional[int] = 3

class TranslateRequest(BaseModel):
    text: str
    target_language: str

# ==========================================
# Conversation memory
# ==========================================
conversations = {}

# ==========================================
# Endpoints
# ==========================================

@app.get("/")
def home():
    return {
        "message": "AI API is running",
        "endpoints": [
            "/chat",
            "/summarize",
            "/translate",
            "/conversation/{session_id}"
        ]
    }

@app.post("/chat", response_model=ChatResponse)
async def chat(request: ChatRequest):
    """Single chat endpoint."""
    try:
        response = await client.chat.completions.create(
            model="gpt-4",
            messages=[
                {
                    "role": "system",
                    "content": request.system_prompt
                },
                {
                    "role": "user",
                    "content": request.message
                }
            ],
            temperature=request.temperature
        )

        return ChatResponse(
            message=request.message,
            answer=response.choices[0].message.content,
            tokens_used=response.usage.total_tokens
        )

    except Exception as e:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=500, detail=str(e))

@app.post("/summarize")
async def summarize(request: SummarizeRequest):
    """Summarizes text."""
    prompt = f"""
Summarize this text in {request.max_sentences} sentences.

Text: {request.text}
"""
    response = await client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}]
    )

    return {
        "original_length": len(request.text),
        "summary": response.choices[0].message.content
    }

@app.post("/translate")
async def translate(request: TranslateRequest):
    """Translates text."""
    prompt = f"""
Translate to {request.target_language}.
Return only translation.

Text: {request.text}
"""
    response = await client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=[{"role": "user", "content": prompt}]
    )

    return {
        "original": request.text,
        "language": request.target_language,
        "translation": response.choices[0].message.content
    }

@app.post("/conversation/{session_id}")
async def conversation(session_id: str, message: str):
    """
    Multi-turn conversation with memory.
    """
    # Initialize session
    if session_id not in conversations:
        conversations[session_id] = []

    # Add user message
    conversations[session_id].append({
        "role": "user",
        "content": message
    })

    # Call LLM with history
    response = await client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=[
            {
                "role": "system",
                "content": "You are a helpful assistant."
            }
        ] + conversations[session_id]
    )

    answer = response.choices[0].message.content

    # Save answer to history
    conversations[session_id].append({
        "role": "assistant",
        "content": answer
    })

    return {
        "session_id": session_id,
        "message": message,
        "answer": answer,
        "history_length": len(conversations[session_id])
    }

@app.delete("/conversation/{session_id}")
def clear_conversation(session_id: str):
    """Clears conversation history."""
    if session_id in conversations:
        del conversations[session_id]
    return {"message": f"Session {session_id} cleared"}
```

### Run
```bash
uvicorn ai_api:app --reload
```

# Practice code

```python
# practice_fastapi.py
# ==========================================
# Practice: Student management API
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException
from pydantic import BaseModel, validator
from typing import Optional, List

app = FastAPI(title="Student API")

# Models
class Student(BaseModel):
    name: str
    age: int
    grade: str
    subjects: List[str] = []

    @validator("age")
    def valid_age(cls, v):
        if v < 5 or v > 25:
            raise ValueError("Age must be 5-25")
        return v

class StudentUpdate(BaseModel):
    name: Optional[str] = None
    age: Optional[int] = None
    grade: Optional[str] = None

# Database
students_db = {}
counter = 1

# Create student
@app.post("/students", status_code=201)
def create_student(student: Student):
    global counter
    students_db[counter] = {
        "id": counter,
        **student.dict()
    }
    counter += 1
    return students_db[counter - 1]

# Get all students
@app.get("/students")
def get_students(grade: Optional[str] = None):
    students = list(students_db.values())
    if grade:
        students = [s for s in students if s["grade"] == grade]
    return {"total": len(students), "students": students}

# Get one student
@app.get("/students/{student_id}")
def get_student(student_id: int):
    if student_id not in students_db:
        raise HTTPException(404, "Student not found")
    return students_db[student_id]

# Update student
@app.put("/students/{student_id}")
def update_student(student_id: int, update: StudentUpdate):
    if student_id not in students_db:
        raise HTTPException(404, "Student not found")
    student = students_db[student_id]
    update_data = update.dict(exclude_unset=True)
    student.update(update_data)
    return student

# Delete student
@app.delete("/students/{student_id}")
def delete_student(student_id: int):
    if student_id not in students_db:
        raise HTTPException(404, "Student not found")
    del students_db[student_id]
    return {"message": "Student deleted"}

# Stats endpoint
@app.get("/stats")
def get_stats():
    total = len(students_db)
    grades = {}
    for s in students_db.values():
        grade = s["grade"]
        grades[grade] = grades.get(grade, 0) + 1
    return {
        "total_students": total,
        "by_grade": grades
    }
```

# Assignment

## Build a **Book Library API**

Build a complete REST API for managing a book library.

---

## Requirements

### Models
Create a `Book` model with:
- `title` (string, required)
- `author` (string, required)
- `price` (float, must be positive)
- `genre` (string, required)
- `available` (boolean, default True)
- `rating` (float, must be 0-5)

---

### Endpoints to build

```
GET    /books              → get all books
GET    /books/{id}         → get one book
POST   /books              → add new book
PUT    /books/{id}         → update book
DELETE /books/{id}         → delete book
GET    /books/search       → search by genre or author
GET    /stats              → total books, avg rating
POST   /books/{id}/borrow  → mark as unavailable
POST   /books/{id}/return  → mark as available
```

---

### Extra requirements
- add proper error handling
- add query parameters for filtering
- add data validation
- return proper status codes
- add CORS middleware
- add request logging middleware

---

### Bonus
- add async endpoints
- add pagination
- add sorting by price or rating

```
http://localhost:8000/docs
```

# Quick revision sheet

```
FastAPI         → fast Python web framework
uvicorn         → runs FastAPI server
@app.get()      → GET endpoint
@app.post()     → POST endpoint
@app.put()      → PUT endpoint
@app.delete()   → DELETE endpoint
BaseModel       → Pydantic data validation
HTTPException   → raise HTTP errors
status_code     → HTTP status codes
Query params    → /items?category=books
Path params     → /items/{id}
async def       → async endpoint
Middleware      → runs before/after every request
CORS            → allows frontend to call API
/docs           → Swagger UI auto docs
```

Here's a **complete FastAPI with SQLite/PostgreSQL database guide**.

---

# What is FastAPI with Database?

FastAPI works beautifully with SQL databases using SQLAlchemy, which is the most popular Python ORM (Object Relational Mapper). An ORM lets you interact with your database using Python code instead of writing raw SQL queries. SQLAlchemy acts as a bridge between your FastAPI application and your database. You define your database tables as Python classes called models, and SQLAlchemy handles all the SQL behind the scenes. For database schema management, we use Alembic which handles migrations — meaning when you change your database structure, Alembic tracks those changes and applies them safely. In this guide we will build a complete Student Management System API using FastAPI, SQLAlchemy, and SQLite first, then show how to switch to PostgreSQL. The project will cover database connection setup, creating models, writing CRUD operations, handling relationships between tables, and building clean API endpoints on top of all of it.

# Step 1: .env file

```bash
# .env
# ==========================================
# Database configuration
# ==========================================

# SQLite (for development)
DATABASE_URL=sqlite:///./school.db

# PostgreSQL (for production)
# DATABASE_URL=postgresql://username:password@localhost:5432/school_db
```

---

# Step 2: database.py

```python
# database.py
# ==========================================
# Database connection and session setup
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy import create_engine
from sqlalchemy.ext.declarative import declarative_base
from sqlalchemy.orm import sessionmaker
from dotenv import load_dotenv
import os

# Load environment variables
load_dotenv()

# Get database URL from .env
DATABASE_URL = os.getenv(
    "DATABASE_URL",
    "sqlite:///./school.db"
)

# ==========================================
# Create engine
# Engine = connection to database
# ==========================================
if "sqlite" in DATABASE_URL:
    # SQLite needs this extra argument
    engine = create_engine(
        DATABASE_URL,
        connect_args={"check_same_thread": False}
    )
else:
    # PostgreSQL
    engine = create_engine(DATABASE_URL)

# ==========================================
# Session maker
# Session = one database conversation
# ==========================================
SessionLocal = sessionmaker(
    autocommit=False,
    autoflush=False,
    bind=engine
)

# ==========================================
# Base class for all models
# ==========================================
Base = declarative_base()

# ==========================================
# Dependency - gives us a database session
# Used in every endpoint that needs DB
# ==========================================
def get_db():
    """
    Creates a new database session
    for each request.
    Closes it after request is done.
    """
    db = SessionLocal()
    try:
        yield db
    finally:
        db.close()
```

---

# Step 3: models.py

```python
# models.py
# ==========================================
# Database table definitions
# Each class = one table in database
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy import (
    Column, Integer, String,
    Float, Boolean, DateTime,
    ForeignKey, Text
)
from sqlalchemy.orm import relationship
from sqlalchemy.sql import func
from database import Base

# ==========================================
# Student table
# ==========================================
class Student(Base):
    # Table name in database
    __tablename__ = "students"

    # Columns
    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    name = Column(String(100), nullable=False)
    email = Column(String(100), unique=True, index=True)
    age = Column(Integer, nullable=False)
    grade = Column(String(10), nullable=False)
    phone = Column(String(20), nullable=True)
    is_active = Column(Boolean, default=True)

    # Timestamps
    created_at = Column(
        DateTime(timezone=True),
        server_default=func.now()
    )
    updated_at = Column(
        DateTime(timezone=True),
        onupdate=func.now()
    )

    # Relationship with Enrollment
    # One student can have many enrollments
    enrollments = relationship(
        "Enrollment",
        back_populates="student"
    )

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<Student {self.name}>"


# ==========================================
# Course table
# ==========================================
class Course(Base):
    __tablename__ = "courses"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    title = Column(String(200), nullable=False)
    description = Column(Text, nullable=True)
    instructor = Column(String(100), nullable=False)
    credits = Column(Integer, default=3)
    max_students = Column(Integer, default=30)
    price = Column(Float, default=0.0)
    is_active = Column(Boolean, default=True)

    created_at = Column(
        DateTime(timezone=True),
        server_default=func.now()
    )

    # Relationship with Enrollment
    enrollments = relationship(
        "Enrollment",
        back_populates="course"
    )

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<Course {self.title}>"


# ==========================================
# Enrollment table
# Links students and courses
# Many-to-Many relationship
# ==========================================
class Enrollment(Base):
    __tablename__ = "enrollments"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)

    # Foreign keys
    student_id = Column(
        Integer,
        ForeignKey("students.id"),
        nullable=False
    )
    course_id = Column(
        Integer,
        ForeignKey("courses.id"),
        nullable=False
    )

    # Enrollment details
    grade = Column(Float, nullable=True)
    status = Column(String(20), default="enrolled")

    enrolled_at = Column(
        DateTime(timezone=True),
        server_default=func.now()
    )

    # Relationships
    student = relationship(
        "Student",
        back_populates="enrollments"
    )
    course = relationship(
        "Course",
        back_populates="enrollments"
    )

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<Enrollment {self.student_id}-{self.course_id}>"
```

---

# Step 4: schemas.py

```python
# schemas.py
# ==========================================
# Pydantic schemas for request/response
# These validate data coming in and going out
# ==========================================

from pydantic import BaseModel, EmailStr, validator
from typing import Optional, List
from datetime import datetime

# ==========================================
# Student schemas
# ==========================================

class StudentBase(BaseModel):
    """Base fields for student."""
    name: str
    email: str
    age: int
    grade: str
    phone: Optional[str] = None

class StudentCreate(StudentBase):
    """Used when creating a student."""

    @validator("age")
    def validate_age(cls, v):
        if v < 5 or v > 30:
            raise ValueError("Age must be 5-30")
        return v

    @validator("name")
    def validate_name(cls, v):
        if len(v.strip()) < 2:
            raise ValueError("Name too short")
        return v.strip()

class StudentUpdate(BaseModel):
    """Used when updating a student."""
    name: Optional[str] = None
    age: Optional[int] = None
    grade: Optional[str] = None
    phone: Optional[str] = None
    is_active: Optional[bool] = None

class StudentResponse(StudentBase):
    """Used when returning student data."""
    id: int
    is_active: bool
    created_at: datetime

    class Config:
        # Allows reading from SQLAlchemy model
        orm_mode = True


# ==========================================
# Course schemas
# ==========================================

class CourseBase(BaseModel):
    title: str
    description: Optional[str] = None
    instructor: str
    credits: int = 3
    max_students: int = 30
    price: float = 0.0

class CourseCreate(CourseBase):
    @validator("price")
    def validate_price(cls, v):
        if v < 0:
            raise ValueError("Price cannot be negative")
        return v

    @validator("credits")
    def validate_credits(cls, v):
        if v < 1 or v > 10:
            raise ValueError("Credits must be 1-10")
        return v

class CourseUpdate(BaseModel):
    title: Optional[str] = None
    description: Optional[str] = None
    instructor: Optional[str] = None
    price: Optional[float] = None
    is_active: Optional[bool] = None

class CourseResponse(CourseBase):
    id: int
    is_active: bool
    created_at: datetime

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True


# ==========================================
# Enrollment schemas
# ==========================================

class EnrollmentCreate(BaseModel):
    student_id: int
    course_id: int

class EnrollmentUpdate(BaseModel):
    grade: Optional[float] = None
    status: Optional[str] = None

    @validator("grade")
    def validate_grade(cls, v):
        if v is not None and (v < 0 or v > 100):
            raise ValueError("Grade must be 0-100")
        return v

class EnrollmentResponse(BaseModel):
    id: int
    student_id: int
    course_id: int
    grade: Optional[float]
    status: str
    enrolled_at: datetime

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True
```

---

# Step 5: crud.py

```python
# crud.py
# ==========================================
# CRUD operations
# Create, Read, Update, Delete functions
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from sqlalchemy import or_
from models import Student, Course, Enrollment
from schemas import (
    StudentCreate, StudentUpdate,
    CourseCreate, CourseUpdate,
    EnrollmentCreate, EnrollmentUpdate
)
from typing import List, Optional


# ==========================================
# STUDENT CRUD
# ==========================================

def create_student(db: Session, student: StudentCreate):
    """Creates a new student in database."""
    db_student = Student(
        name=student.name,
        email=student.email,
        age=student.age,
        grade=student.grade,
        phone=student.phone
    )
    db.add(db_student)
    db.commit()
    db.refresh(db_student)
    return db_student


def get_student(db: Session, student_id: int):
    """Gets one student by ID."""
    return db.query(Student).filter(
        Student.id == student_id
    ).first()


def get_student_by_email(db: Session, email: str):
    """Gets student by email."""
    return db.query(Student).filter(
        Student.email == email
    ).first()


def get_students(
    db: Session,
    skip: int = 0,
    limit: int = 100,
    grade: Optional[str] = None,
    is_active: Optional[bool] = None,
    search: Optional[str] = None
):
    """
    Gets list of students with filters.
    skip = how many to skip (for pagination)
    limit = how many to return
    """
    query = db.query(Student)

    # Filter by grade
    if grade:
        query = query.filter(Student.grade == grade)

    # Filter by active status
    if is_active is not None:
        query = query.filter(Student.is_active == is_active)

    # Search by name or email
    if search:
        query = query.filter(
            or_(
                Student.name.contains(search),
                Student.email.contains(search)
            )
        )

    return query.offset(skip).limit(limit).all()


def update_student(
    db: Session,
    student_id: int,
    student_update: StudentUpdate
):
    """Updates a student."""
    db_student = get_student(db, student_id)
    if not db_student:
        return None

    # Update only provided fields
    update_data = student_update.dict(exclude_unset=True)
    for field, value in update_data.items():
        setattr(db_student, field, value)

    db.commit()
    db.refresh(db_student)
    return db_student


def delete_student(db: Session, student_id: int):
    """Deletes a student."""
    db_student = get_student(db, student_id)
    if not db_student:
        return False

    db.delete(db_student)
    db.commit()
    return True


# ==========================================
# COURSE CRUD
# ==========================================

def create_course(db: Session, course: CourseCreate):
    """Creates a new course."""
    db_course = Course(**course.dict())
    db.add(db_course)
    db.commit()
    db.refresh(db_course)
    return db_course


def get_course(db: Session, course_id: int):
    """Gets one course by ID."""
    return db.query(Course).filter(
        Course.id == course_id
    ).first()


def get_courses(
    db: Session,
    skip: int = 0,
    limit: int = 100,
    instructor: Optional[str] = None,
    is_active: Optional[bool] = None
):
    """Gets list of courses."""
    query = db.query(Course)

    if instructor:
        query = query.filter(
            Course.instructor.contains(instructor)
        )

    if is_active is not None:
        query = query.filter(Course.is_active == is_active)

    return query.offset(skip).limit(limit).all()


def update_course(
    db: Session,
    course_id: int,
    course_update: CourseUpdate
):
    """Updates a course."""
    db_course = get_course(db, course_id)
    if not db_course:
        return None

    update_data = course_update.dict(exclude_unset=True)
    for field, value in update_data.items():
        setattr(db_course, field, value)

    db.commit()
    db.refresh(db_course)
    return db_course


def delete_course(db: Session, course_id: int):
    """Deletes a course."""
    db_course = get_course(db, course_id)
    if not db_course:
        return False

    db.delete(db_course)
    db.commit()
    return True


# ==========================================
# ENROLLMENT CRUD
# ==========================================

def create_enrollment(
    db: Session,
    enrollment: EnrollmentCreate
):
    """Enrolls a student in a course."""

    # Check if already enrolled
    existing = db.query(Enrollment).filter(
        Enrollment.student_id == enrollment.student_id,
        Enrollment.course_id == enrollment.course_id
    ).first()

    if existing:
        return None

    db_enrollment = Enrollment(**enrollment.dict())
    db.add(db_enrollment)
    db.commit()
    db.refresh(db_enrollment)
    return db_enrollment


def get_student_enrollments(
    db: Session,
    student_id: int
):
    """Gets all enrollments for a student."""
    return db.query(Enrollment).filter(
        Enrollment.student_id == student_id
    ).all()


def get_course_enrollments(
    db: Session,
    course_id: int
):
    """Gets all enrollments for a course."""
    return db.query(Enrollment).filter(
        Enrollment.course_id == course_id
    ).all()


def update_enrollment(
    db: Session,
    enrollment_id: int,
    update: EnrollmentUpdate
):
    """Updates enrollment grade or status."""
    db_enrollment = db.query(Enrollment).filter(
        Enrollment.id == enrollment_id
    ).first()

    if not db_enrollment:
        return None

    update_data = update.dict(exclude_unset=True)
    for field, value in update_data.items():
        setattr(db_enrollment, field, value)

    db.commit()
    db.refresh(db_enrollment)
    return db_enrollment
```

---

# Step 6: routers/students.py

```python
# routers/students.py
# ==========================================
# Student API endpoints
# ==========================================

from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends, HTTPException, Query
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from typing import List, Optional
from database import get_db
import crud
import schemas

router = APIRouter(
    prefix="/students",
    tags=["Students"]
)

# ==========================================
# Create student
# ==========================================
@router.post(
    "/",
    response_model=schemas.StudentResponse,
    status_code=201
)
def create_student(
    student: schemas.StudentCreate,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Creates a new student."""

    # Check if email exists
    existing = crud.get_student_by_email(db, student.email)
    if existing:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=400,
            detail="Email already registered"
        )

    return crud.create_student(db, student)


# ==========================================
# Get all students
# ==========================================
@router.get(
    "/",
    response_model=List[schemas.StudentResponse]
)
def get_students(
    skip: int = Query(0, ge=0),
    limit: int = Query(10, ge=1, le=100),
    grade: Optional[str] = None,
    is_active: Optional[bool] = None,
    search: Optional[str] = None,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """
    Gets all students with filters.
    ?skip=0&limit=10&grade=A&search=john
    """
    students = crud.get_students(
        db,
        skip=skip,
        limit=limit,
        grade=grade,
        is_active=is_active,
        search=search
    )
    return students


# ==========================================
# Get one student
# ==========================================
@router.get(
    "/{student_id}",
    response_model=schemas.StudentResponse
)
def get_student(
    student_id: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Gets one student by ID."""
    student = crud.get_student(db, student_id)
    if not student:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Student not found"
        )
    return student


# ==========================================
# Update student
# ==========================================
@router.put(
    "/{student_id}",
    response_model=schemas.StudentResponse
)
def update_student(
    student_id: int,
    student_update: schemas.StudentUpdate,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Updates a student."""
    student = crud.update_student(
        db, student_id, student_update
    )
    if not student:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Student not found"
        )
    return student


# ==========================================
# Delete student
# ==========================================
@router.delete("/{student_id}")
def delete_student(
    student_id: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Deletes a student."""
    success = crud.delete_student(db, student_id)
    if not success:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Student not found"
        )
    return {"message": "Student deleted successfully"}


# ==========================================
# Get student enrollments
# ==========================================
@router.get(
    "/{student_id}/enrollments",
    response_model=List[schemas.EnrollmentResponse]
)
def get_student_enrollments(
    student_id: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Gets all courses a student is enrolled in."""
    student = crud.get_student(db, student_id)
    if not student:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Student not found"
        )
    return crud.get_student_enrollments(db, student_id)
```

---

# Step 7: routers/courses.py

```python
# routers/courses.py
# ==========================================
# Course API endpoints
# ==========================================

from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends, HTTPException, Query
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from typing import List, Optional
from database import get_db
import crud
import schemas

router = APIRouter(
    prefix="/courses",
    tags=["Courses"]
)

@router.post(
    "/",
    response_model=schemas.CourseResponse,
    status_code=201
)
def create_course(
    course: schemas.CourseCreate,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Creates a new course."""
    return crud.create_course(db, course)


@router.get(
    "/",
    response_model=List[schemas.CourseResponse]
)
def get_courses(
    skip: int = Query(0, ge=0),
    limit: int = Query(10, ge=1, le=100),
    instructor: Optional[str] = None,
    is_active: Optional[bool] = None,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Gets all courses."""
    return crud.get_courses(
        db,
        skip=skip,
        limit=limit,
        instructor=instructor,
        is_active=is_active
    )


@router.get(
    "/{course_id}",
    response_model=schemas.CourseResponse
)
def get_course(
    course_id: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Gets one course by ID."""
    course = crud.get_course(db, course_id)
    if not course:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Course not found"
        )
    return course


@router.put(
    "/{course_id}",
    response_model=schemas.CourseResponse
)
def update_course(
    course_id: int,
    course_update: schemas.CourseUpdate,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Updates a course."""
    course = crud.update_course(db, course_id, course_update)
    if not course:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Course not found"
        )
    return course


@router.delete("/{course_id}")
def delete_course(
    course_id: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Deletes a course."""
    success = crud.delete_course(db, course_id)
    if not success:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Course not found"
        )
    return {"message": "Course deleted successfully"}


@router.post("/enroll")
def enroll_student(
    enrollment: schemas.EnrollmentCreate,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Enrolls a student in a course."""

    # Check student exists
    student = crud.get_student(
        db, enrollment.student_id
    )
    if not student:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Student not found"
        )

    # Check course exists
    course = crud.get_course(db, enrollment.course_id)
    if not course:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Course not found"
        )

    # Enroll
    result = crud.create_enrollment(db, enrollment)
    if not result:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=400,
            detail="Student already enrolled"
        )

    return {
        "message": "Enrolled successfully",
        "enrollment": result
    }


@router.get(
    "/{course_id}/students"
)
def get_course_students(
    course_id: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
):
    """Gets all students in a course."""
    course = crud.get_course(db, course_id)
    if not course:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=404,
            detail="Course not found"
        )

    enrollments = crud.get_course_enrollments(
        db, course_id
    )
    return {
        "course": course.title,
        "total_students": len(enrollments),
        "enrollments": enrollments
    }
```

---

# Step 8: main.py

```python
# main.py
# ==========================================
# Main FastAPI application
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware
import models
from database import engine
from routers import students, courses

# ==========================================
# Create all tables in database
# ==========================================
models.Base.metadata.create_all(bind=engine)

# ==========================================
# Create FastAPI app
# ==========================================
app = FastAPI(
    title="School Management API",
    description="FastAPI + SQLAlchemy + SQLite",
    version="1.0.0"
)

# ==========================================
# CORS middleware
# ==========================================
app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=["*"],
    allow_methods=["*"],
    allow_headers=["*"],
)

# ==========================================
# Include routers
# ==========================================
app.include_router(students.router)
app.include_router(courses.router)

# ==========================================
# Root endpoint
# ==========================================
@app.get("/")
def home():
    return {
        "message": "School Management API",
        "docs": "/docs",
        "endpoints": {
            "students": "/students",
            "courses": "/courses",
            "enroll": "/courses/enroll"
        }
    }

# ==========================================
# Stats endpoint
# ==========================================
@app.get("/stats")
def get_stats(db=None):
    from database import SessionLocal
    from models import Student, Course, Enrollment

    db = SessionLocal()

    total_students = db.query(Student).count()
    active_students = db.query(Student).filter(
        Student.is_active == True
    ).count()
    total_courses = db.query(Course).count()
    total_enrollments = db.query(Enrollment).count()

    db.close()

    return {
        "total_students": total_students,
        "active_students": active_students,
        "total_courses": total_courses,
        "total_enrollments": total_enrollments
    }
```

---

```bash
uvicorn main:app --reload
```

# Quick revision sheet

```
SQLAlchemy    → Python ORM for databases
engine        → database connection
SessionLocal  → database session factory
Base          → base class for all models
get_db()      → dependency gives DB session
Column        → defines table column
ForeignKey    → links two tables
relationship  → Python-level table link
Depends()     → FastAPI dependency injection
orm_mode=True → allows Pydantic to read SQLAlchemy models
skip/limit    → pagination
exclude_unset → update only provided fields
```

- pagination

how to connect python with sql a

## Copilot

Here's a **complete guide on connecting Python with SQL databases**.

---

# What is Python with SQL?

Python can connect to SQL databases directly using database drivers and libraries. Without any ORM like SQLAlchemy, you can write raw SQL queries directly from Python code. This approach is called **DB-API** (Database Application Programming Interface). Python has a standard interface called **PEP 249** that all database drivers follow, which means once you learn one, others are very similar. The most common databases used with Python are SQLite (built into Python, no installation needed), MySQL (most popular for web apps), and PostgreSQL (most powerful for production). You connect to the database, create a cursor object, execute SQL queries, fetch results, and close the connection. This is the most basic and direct way to work with databases in Python, and understanding this helps you understand how ORMs like SQLAlchemy work under the hood.

---

# Databases covered

```
SQLite    → built into Python, no setup needed
MySQL     → most popular web database
PostgreSQL→ most powerful production database
```

# Part 1: SQLite

SQLite is the **easiest** to start with. No server needed.

---

## 1) Connect to SQLite

```python
# sqlite_connect.py
# ==========================================
# Connect to SQLite database
# ==========================================

import sqlite3

# ==========================================
# Connect to database
# If file does not exist, it creates it
# ==========================================
connection = sqlite3.connect("school.db")
print("Connected to SQLite!")

# ==========================================
# Create cursor
# Cursor is used to execute SQL queries
# ==========================================
cursor = connection.cursor()
print("Cursor created!")

# ==========================================
# Always close connection when done
# ==========================================
connection.close()
print("Connection closed!")
```

---

## 2) Create table

```python
# sqlite_create_table.py
# ==========================================
# Create tables in SQLite
# ==========================================

import sqlite3

connection = sqlite3.connect("school.db")
cursor = connection.cursor()

# ==========================================
# Create students table
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("""
    CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS students (
        id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
        name TEXT NOT NULL,
        email TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
        age INTEGER NOT NULL,
        grade TEXT NOT NULL,
        created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
    )
""")

# ==========================================
# Create courses table
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("""
    CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS courses (
        id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
        title TEXT NOT NULL,
        instructor TEXT NOT NULL,
        price REAL DEFAULT 0.0,
        created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
    )
""")

# ==========================================
# Save changes
# Always commit after create/insert/update/delete
# ==========================================
connection.commit()
print("Tables created successfully!")

connection.close()
```

---

## 3) Insert data

```python
# sqlite_insert.py
# ==========================================
# Insert data into SQLite
# ==========================================

import sqlite3

connection = sqlite3.connect("school.db")
cursor = connection.cursor()

# ==========================================
# Insert one record
# Use ? as placeholder - prevents SQL injection
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("""
    INSERT INTO students (name, email, age, grade)
    VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?)
""", ("Aman Singh", "aman@email.com", 20, "A"))

print(f"Inserted student ID: {cursor.lastrowid}")

# ==========================================
# Insert multiple records at once
# ==========================================
students = [
    ("Sara Khan", "sara@email.com", 22, "B"),
    ("Raj Patel", "raj@email.com", 21, "A"),
    ("Priya Sharma", "priya@email.com", 23, "B+"),
    ("Ahmed Ali", "ahmed@email.com", 20, "A+"),
]

cursor.executemany("""
    INSERT INTO students (name, email, age, grade)
    VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?)
""", students)

print(f"Inserted {cursor.rowcount} students!")

# Save changes
connection.commit()
connection.close()
```

---

## 4) Read data

```python
# sqlite_read.py
# ==========================================
# Read data from SQLite
# ==========================================

import sqlite3

connection = sqlite3.connect("school.db")
cursor = connection.cursor()

# ==========================================
# Fetch all records
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("SELECT * FROM students")
all_students = cursor.fetchall()

print("All students:")
for student in all_students:
    print(f"  {student}")

# ==========================================
# Fetch one record
# ==========================================
cursor.execute(
    "SELECT * FROM students WHERE id = ?", (1,)
)
one_student = cursor.fetchone()
print(f"\nOne student: {one_student}")

# ==========================================
# Fetch with conditions
# ==========================================
cursor.execute(
    "SELECT * FROM students WHERE grade = ?", ("A",)
)
grade_a = cursor.fetchall()
print(f"\nGrade A students:")
for s in grade_a:
    print(f"  {s}")

# ==========================================
# Fetch with column names
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("SELECT * FROM students")
columns = [desc[0] for desc in cursor.description]
rows = cursor.fetchall()

print(f"\nWith column names:")
for row in rows:
    student_dict = dict(zip(columns, row))
    print(f"  {student_dict}")

connection.close()
```

---

## 5) Update and Delete

```python
# sqlite_update_delete.py
# ==========================================
# Update and Delete in SQLite
# ==========================================

import sqlite3

connection = sqlite3.connect("school.db")
cursor = connection.cursor()

# ==========================================
# Update one record
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("""
    UPDATE students
    SET grade = ?
    WHERE id = ?
""", ("A+", 1))

print(f"Updated rows: {cursor.rowcount}")

# ==========================================
# Update multiple records
# ==========================================
cursor.execute("""
    UPDATE students
    SET grade = ?
    WHERE age < ?
""", ("A", 21))

print(f"Updated young students: {cursor.rowcount}")

# ==========================================
# Delete one record
# ==========================================
cursor.execute(
    "DELETE FROM students WHERE id = ?", (5,)
)
print(f"Deleted rows: {cursor.rowcount}")

# ==========================================
# Delete with condition
# ==========================================
cursor.execute(
    "DELETE FROM students WHERE grade = ?", ("C",)
)
print(f"Deleted grade C students: {cursor.rowcount}")

connection.commit()
connection.close()
```

---

## 6) Using context manager (best practice)

```python
# sqlite_context.py
# ==========================================
# Using context manager - cleaner way
# ==========================================

import sqlite3

# ==========================================
# with statement auto closes connection
# ==========================================
with sqlite3.connect("school.db") as connection:
    cursor = connection.cursor()

    # Insert
    cursor.execute("""
        INSERT INTO students (name, email, age, grade)
        VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?)
    """, ("Test User", "test@email.com", 25, "B"))

    connection.commit()
    print("Inserted successfully")

# Connection automatically closed here
print("Connection closed automatically")
```

---

## 7) Full SQLite CRUD class

```python
# sqlite_crud_class.py
# ==========================================
# Full SQLite CRUD class
# ==========================================

import sqlite3
from typing import Optional, List

class SQLiteDB:

    def __init__(self, db_name: str):
        self.db_name = db_name
        self.setup_tables()

    def get_connection(self):
        """Creates and returns connection."""
        conn = sqlite3.connect(self.db_name)
        # Return rows as dictionaries
        conn.row_factory = sqlite3.Row
        return conn

    def setup_tables(self):
        """Creates tables if they don't exist."""
        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            conn.execute("""
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS students (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    email TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,
                    age INTEGER,
                    grade TEXT,
                    created_at TIMESTAMP
                    DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
                )
            """)
            conn.commit()
        print("Tables ready!")

    # ==========================================
    # CREATE
    # ==========================================
    def create_student(
        self, name, email, age, grade
    ):
        """Inserts a new student."""
        try:
            with self.get_connection() as conn:
                cursor = conn.execute("""
                    INSERT INTO students
                    (name, email, age, grade)
                    VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?)
                """, (name, email, age, grade))
                conn.commit()
                return cursor.lastrowid
        except sqlite3.IntegrityError:
            print(f"Email {email} already exists!")
            return None

    # ==========================================
    # READ
    # ==========================================
    def get_all_students(self):
        """Gets all students."""
        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            cursor = conn.execute(
                "SELECT * FROM students"
            )
            return [dict(row) for row in cursor]

    def get_student_by_id(self, student_id: int):
        """Gets one student by ID."""
        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            cursor = conn.execute(
                "SELECT * FROM students WHERE id = ?",
                (student_id,)
            )
            row = cursor.fetchone()
            return dict(row) if row else None

    def search_students(self, search_term: str):
        """Searches students by name or email."""
        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            cursor = conn.execute("""
                SELECT * FROM students
                WHERE name LIKE ?
                OR email LIKE ?
            """, (
                f"%{search_term}%",
                f"%{search_term}%"
            ))
            return [dict(row) for row in cursor]

    # ==========================================
    # UPDATE
    # ==========================================
    def update_student(
        self,
        student_id: int,
        name: Optional[str] = None,
        grade: Optional[str] = None,
        age: Optional[int] = None
    ):
        """Updates student details."""
        # Build dynamic update query
        updates = []
        values = []

        if name:
            updates.append("name = ?")
            values.append(name)
        if grade:
            updates.append("grade = ?")
            values.append(grade)
        if age:
            updates.append("age = ?")
            values.append(age)

        if not updates:
            return False

        values.append(student_id)
        query = f"""
            UPDATE students
            SET {', '.join(updates)}
            WHERE id = ?
        """

        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            cursor = conn.execute(query, values)
            conn.commit()
            return cursor.rowcount > 0

    # ==========================================
    # DELETE
    # ==========================================
    def delete_student(self, student_id: int):
        """Deletes a student."""
        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            cursor = conn.execute(
                "DELETE FROM students WHERE id = ?",
                (student_id,)
            )
            conn.commit()
            return cursor.rowcount > 0

    # ==========================================
    # STATS
    # ==========================================
    def get_stats(self):
        """Gets database statistics."""
        with self.get_connection() as conn:
            total = conn.execute(
                "SELECT COUNT(*) FROM students"
            ).fetchone()[0]

            avg_age = conn.execute(
                "SELECT AVG(age) FROM students"
            ).fetchone()[0]

            by_grade = conn.execute("""
                SELECT grade, COUNT(*) as count
                FROM students
                GROUP BY grade
            """).fetchall()

            return {
                "total_students": total,
                "average_age": round(avg_age or 0, 1),
                "by_grade": {
                    row[0]: row[1]
                    for row in by_grade
                }
            }


# ==========================================
# Test the class
# ==========================================
db = SQLiteDB("school.db")

# Create
print("Creating students...")
db.create_student("Aman", "aman@email.com", 20, "A")
db.create_student("Sara", "sara@email.com", 22, "B")
db.create_student("Raj", "raj@email.com", 21, "A")
db.create_student("Priya", "priya@email.com", 23, "B+")

# Read
print("\nAll students:")
for s in db.get_all_students():
    print(f"  {s}")

# Search
print("\nSearch 'am':")
for s in db.search_students("am"):
    print(f"  {s}")

# Update
db.update_student(1, grade="A+")
print("\nUpdated student 1:")
print(db.get_student_by_id(1))

# Delete
db.delete_student(4)
print("\nAfter delete:")
for s in db.get_all_students():
    print(f"  {s}")

# Stats
print("\nStats:")
print(db.get_stats())
```

# Part 2: MySQL

```python
# mysql_connection.py
# ==========================================
# Connect Python to MySQL
# ==========================================

import mysql.connector
from mysql.connector import Error

# ==========================================
# Connect to MySQL
# ==========================================
def create_connection():
    try:
        connection = mysql.connector.connect(
            host="localhost",
            port=3306,
            user="root",
            password="your_password",
            database="school_db"
        )
        if connection.is_connected():
            print("Connected to MySQL!")
            return connection
    except Error as e:
        print(f"Error: {e}")
        return None

# ==========================================
# Create database
# ==========================================
def create_database():
    try:
        connection = mysql.connector.connect(
            host="localhost",
            user="root",
            password="your_password"
        )
        cursor = connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute(
            "CREATE DATABASE IF NOT EXISTS school_db"
        )
        print("Database created!")
        connection.close()
    except Error as e:
        print(f"Error: {e}")

# ==========================================
# Create table
# ==========================================
def create_tables(connection):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute("""
        CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS students (
            id INT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
            name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
            email VARCHAR(100) UNIQUE NOT NULL,
            age INT,
            grade VARCHAR(10),
            created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
        )
    """)
    connection.commit()
    print("Table created!")

# ==========================================
# Insert data
# ==========================================
def insert_student(connection, name, email, age, grade):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    query = """
        INSERT INTO students (name, email, age, grade)
        VALUES (%s, %s, %s, %s)
    """
    # MySQL uses %s as placeholder
    cursor.execute(query, (name, email, age, grade))
    connection.commit()
    print(f"Inserted ID: {cursor.lastrowid}")
    return cursor.lastrowid

# ==========================================
# Read data
# ==========================================
def get_all_students(connection):
    cursor = connection.cursor(dictionary=True)
    cursor.execute("SELECT * FROM students")
    return cursor.fetchall()

# ==========================================
# Update data
# ==========================================
def update_student(connection, student_id, grade):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute("""
        UPDATE students SET grade = %s
        WHERE id = %s
    """, (grade, student_id))
    connection.commit()
    print(f"Updated {cursor.rowcount} rows")

# ==========================================
# Delete data
# ==========================================
def delete_student(connection, student_id):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute(
        "DELETE FROM students WHERE id = %s",
        (student_id,)
    )
    connection.commit()
    print(f"Deleted {cursor.rowcount} rows")

# ==========================================
# Run everything
# ==========================================
create_database()
conn = create_connection()

if conn:
    create_tables(conn)
    insert_student(conn, "Aman", "aman@email.com", 20, "A")
    insert_student(conn, "Sara", "sara@email.com", 22, "B")

    students = get_all_students(conn)
    print("\nAll students:")
    for s in students:
        print(f"  {s}")

    update_student(conn, 1, "A+")
    delete_student(conn, 2)

    conn.close()
```
