# Part 3: PostgreSQL

```python
# postgresql_connection.py
# ==========================================
# Connect Python to PostgreSQL
# ==========================================

import psycopg2
from psycopg2.extras import RealDictCursor

# ==========================================
# Connect to PostgreSQL
# ==========================================
def create_connection():
    try:
        connection = psycopg2.connect(
            host="localhost",
            port=5432,
            database="school_db",
            user="postgres",
            password="your_password"
        )
        print("Connected to PostgreSQL!")
        return connection
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error: {e}")
        return None

# ==========================================
# Create table
# ==========================================
def create_tables(connection):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute("""
        CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS students (
            id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
            name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
            email VARCHAR(100) UNIQUE NOT NULL,
            age INTEGER,
            grade VARCHAR(10),
            created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
        )
    """)
    connection.commit()
    print("Tables created!")

# ==========================================
# Insert data
# ==========================================
def insert_student(connection, name, email, age, grade):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute("""
        INSERT INTO students (name, email, age, grade)
        VALUES (%s, %s, %s, %s)
        RETURNING id
    """, (name, email, age, grade))
    # PostgreSQL uses %s like MySQL
    student_id = cursor.fetchone()[0]
    connection.commit()
    print(f"Inserted ID: {student_id}")
    return student_id

# ==========================================
# Read data - returns dicts
# ==========================================
def get_all_students(connection):
    # RealDictCursor returns rows as dicts
    cursor = connection.cursor(
        cursor_factory=RealDictCursor
    )
    cursor.execute("SELECT * FROM students")
    return cursor.fetchall()

# ==========================================
# Update data
# ==========================================
def update_student(connection, student_id, grade):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute("""
        UPDATE students SET grade = %s
        WHERE id = %s
    """, (grade, student_id))
    connection.commit()
    print(f"Updated {cursor.rowcount} rows")

# ==========================================
# Delete data
# ==========================================
def delete_student(connection, student_id):
    cursor = connection.cursor()
    cursor.execute(
        "DELETE FROM students WHERE id = %s",
        (student_id,)
    )
    connection.commit()
    print(f"Deleted {cursor.rowcount} rows")

# ==========================================
# Run everything
# ==========================================
conn = create_connection()

if conn:
    create_tables(conn)
    insert_student(conn, "Aman", "aman@email.com", 20, "A")
    insert_student(conn, "Sara", "sara@email.com", 22, "B")

    students = get_all_students(conn)
    print("\nAll students:")
    for s in students:
        print(f"  {dict(s)}")

    update_student(conn, 1, "A+")
    delete_student(conn, 2)

    conn.close()
```

---

# Part 4: Universal DB class

Works with all three databases.

```python
# universal_db.py
# ==========================================
# Universal database class
# Works with SQLite, MySQL, PostgreSQL
# ==========================================

import sqlite3
from typing import Optional

class UniversalDB:

    def __init__(self, db_type="sqlite", **kwargs):
        """
        db_type = sqlite / mysql / postgresql
        """
        self.db_type = db_type
        self.config = kwargs
        self.connection = None
        self.connect()

    def connect(self):
        """Connects to the database."""
        if self.db_type == "sqlite":
            self.connection = sqlite3.connect(
                self.config.get("database", "app.db")
            )
            self.connection.row_factory = sqlite3.Row

        elif self.db_type == "mysql":
            import mysql.connector
            self.connection = mysql.connector.connect(
                **self.config
            )

        elif self.db_type == "postgresql":
            import psycopg2
            self.connection = psycopg2.connect(
                **self.config
            )
        print(f"Connected to {self.db_type}!")

    def get_placeholder(self):
        """
        SQLite uses ?
        MySQL and PostgreSQL use %s
        """
        if self.db_type == "sqlite":
            return "?"
        return "%s"

    def execute(self, query, params=None):
        """Executes a query."""
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        if params:
            cursor.execute(query, params)
        else:
            cursor.execute(query)
        self.connection.commit()
        return cursor

    def fetchall(self, query, params=None):
        """Executes query and returns all rows."""
        cursor = self.execute(query, params)
        rows = cursor.fetchall()
        if self.db_type == "sqlite":
            return [dict(row) for row in rows]
        return rows

    def fetchone(self, query, params=None):
        """Executes query and returns one row."""
        cursor = self.execute(query, params)
        row = cursor.fetchone()
        if row and self.db_type == "sqlite":
            return dict(row)
        return row

    def close(self):
        """Closes connection."""
        if self.connection:
            self.connection.close()
            print("Connection closed!")


# ==========================================
# Test with SQLite
# ==========================================
db = UniversalDB(
    db_type="sqlite",
    database="test.db"
)

p = db.get_placeholder()

# Create table
db.execute(f"""
    CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS students (
        id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
        name TEXT,
        grade TEXT
    )
""")

# Insert
db.execute(
    f"INSERT INTO students (name, grade) VALUES ({p}, {p})",
    ("Aman", "A")
)
db.execute(
    f"INSERT INTO students (name, grade) VALUES ({p}, {p})",
    ("Sara", "B")
)

# Read
students = db.fetchall("SELECT * FROM students")
print("Students:")
for s in students:
    print(f"  {s}")

db.close()
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
SQLite
  import sqlite3
  connect   → sqlite3.connect("db.db")
  placeholder → ?

MySQL
  import mysql.connector
  connect   → mysql.connector.connect(host, user, password, database)
  placeholder → %s

PostgreSQL
  import psycopg2
  connect   → psycopg2.connect(host, database, user, password)
  placeholder → %s

Common steps for all:
  1. connect()
  2. cursor()
  3. execute(query, params)
  4. commit()
  5. fetchall() / fetchone()
  6. close()

Never use f-string in SQL → SQL injection risk
Always use placeholders → ? or %s
```

---

# Interview-ready answers

## What is Python DB-API?
A standard interface for Python to connect to databases. All drivers follow PEP 249.

## What is a cursor?
An object used to execute SQL queries and fetch results.

## What is the difference between `?` and `%s`?
SQLite uses `?` as placeholder. MySQL and PostgreSQL use `%s`.

## Why use placeholders?
To prevent SQL injection attacks.

## What is `commit()`?
Saves all changes to the database permanently.

## What is `fetchone()` vs `fetchall()`?
`fetchone()` returns one row. `fetchall()` returns all rows.

# How Spring Boot does it
```
Spring Boot:
- Configure once in application.properties
- @Autowired anywhere
- Connection pool managed automatically

Python equivalent:
- Configure once in config/database.py
- Import db anywhere
- Connection pool via SQLAlchemy
```

```bash
# .env

# Azure SQL Database Configuration

# Azure SQL Connection
AZURE_SQL_SERVER=your-server.database.windows.net
AZURE_SQL_DATABASE=your-database-name
AZURE_SQL_USERNAME=your-username
AZURE_SQL_PASSWORD=your-password
AZURE_SQL_DRIVER=ODBC Driver 18 for SQL Server

# Connection Pool Settings

DB_MAX_OVERFLOW=20
DB_POOL_TIMEOUT=30
DB_POOL_RECYCLE=1800
```

# Step 2: config/database.py
## This is the ONE TIME setup (like Spring Boot)

```python
# config/database.py
# ==========================================
# ONE TIME DATABASE SETUP
# Like application.properties in Spring Boot
# Configure once, use everywhere
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy import create_engine, text
from sqlalchemy.ext.declarative import declarative_base
from sqlalchemy.orm import sessionmaker, Session
from sqlalchemy.pool import QueuePool
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from typing import Generator
import os
import logging

# Setup logging
logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO)
logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

# Load .env file
load_dotenv()

# ==========================================
# Build Azure SQL connection string
# ==========================================
def get_connection_string() -> str:
    """
    Builds Azure SQL connection string.
    Similar to application.properties in Spring Boot.
    """
    server   = os.getenv("AZURE_SQL_SERVER")
    database = os.getenv("AZURE_SQL_DATABASE")
    username = os.getenv("AZURE_SQL_USERNAME")
    password = os.getenv("AZURE_SQL_PASSWORD")
    driver   = os.getenv(
        "AZURE_SQL_DRIVER",
        "ODBC Driver 18 for SQL Server"
    )

    # Azure SQL connection string format
    connection_string = (
        f"mssql+pyodbc://{username}:{password}"
        f"@{server}/{database}"
        f"?driver={driver.replace(' ', '+')}"
        f"&Encrypt=yes"
        f"&TrustServerCertificate=no"
        f"&Connection+Timeout=30"
    )

    logger.info(f"Connecting to: {server}/{database}")
    return connection_string


# ==========================================
# Create Engine ONCE
# This is like DataSource in Spring Boot
# Connection pool is managed here
# ==========================================
engine = create_engine(
    get_connection_string(),

    # Connection Pool Settings
    # Like HikariCP in Spring Boot
    poolclass=QueuePool,
    pool_size=int(os.getenv("DB_POOL_SIZE", 10)),
    max_overflow=int(os.getenv("DB_MAX_OVERFLOW", 20)),
    pool_timeout=int(os.getenv("DB_POOL_TIMEOUT", 30)),
    pool_recycle=int(os.getenv("DB_POOL_RECYCLE", 1800)),
    pool_pre_ping=True,    # checks connection is alive

    # Show SQL queries in debug mode
    echo=os.getenv("DEBUG", "False") == "True"
)

# ==========================================
# Session Factory
# Like @Transactional in Spring Boot
# ==========================================
SessionLocal = sessionmaker(
    autocommit=False,
    autoflush=False,
    bind=engine
)

# ==========================================
# Base class for all models
# Like @Entity in Spring Boot
# ==========================================
Base = declarative_base()


# ==========================================
# Database Session Dependency
# Like @Autowired in Spring Boot
# Use this in every class that needs DB
# ==========================================
def get_db() -> Generator[Session, None, None]:
    """
    Gives a database session.
    Automatically closes after use.

    Usage in FastAPI:
        db: Session = Depends(get_db)

    Usage anywhere else:
        with get_session() as db:
            ...
    """
    db = SessionLocal()
    try:
        yield db
    except Exception as e:
        db.rollback()
        logger.error(f"Database error: {e}")
        raise
    finally:
        db.close()


# ==========================================
# Direct session for non-FastAPI use
# Use this in services/repositories
# outside of FastAPI endpoints
# ==========================================
class DatabaseSession:
    """
    Context manager for database sessions.
    Use like:
        with DatabaseSession() as db:
            db.query(...)
    """
    def __init__(self):
        self.db = SessionLocal()

    def __enter__(self) -> Session:
        return self.db

    def __exit__(self, exc_type, exc_val, exc_tb):
        if exc_type:
            self.db.rollback()
            logger.error(f"DB Error: {exc_val}")
        else:
            self.db.commit()
        self.db.close()


# ==========================================
# Test connection on startup
# ==========================================
def test_connection() -> bool:
    """Tests database connection."""
    try:
        with engine.connect() as conn:
            conn.execute(text("SELECT 1"))
        logger.info("Database connection successful!")
        return True
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Database connection failed: {e}")
        return False


# ==========================================
# Create all tables
# ==========================================
def create_tables():
    """Creates all tables defined in models."""
    Base.metadata.create_all(bind=engine)
    logger.info("All tables created!")


# ==========================================
# Drop all tables
# ==========================================
def drop_tables():
    """Drops all tables. Use carefully!"""
    Base.metadata.drop_all(bind=engine)
    logger.warning("All tables dropped!")
```

# Step 3: models/student.py
## Like @Entity in Spring Boot

```python
# models/student.py
# ==========================================
# Student model - like @Entity in Spring Boot
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy import (
    Column, Integer, String,
    Float, Boolean, DateTime
)
from sqlalchemy.sql import func

# Import Base from ONE PLACE
from config.database import Base

class Student(Base):
    __tablename__ = "students"

    id         = Column(Integer, primary_key=True, index=True)
    name       = Column(String(100), nullable=False)
    email      = Column(String(100), unique=True)
    age        = Column(Integer)
    grade      = Column(String(10))
    is_active  = Column(Boolean, default=True)
    created_at = Column(
        DateTime(timezone=True),
        server_default=func.now()
    )

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<Student {self.name}>"

    def to_dict(self):
        return {
            "id": self.id,
            "name": self.name,
            "email": self.email,
            "age": self.age,
            "grade": self.grade,
            "is_active": self.is_active,
        }
```

```python
# models/employee.py
# ==========================================
# Employee model
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy import (
    Column, Integer, String,
    Float, Boolean, DateTime
)
from sqlalchemy.sql import func
from config.database import Base

class Employee(Base):
    __tablename__ = "employees"

    id           = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    name         = Column(String(100), nullable=False)
    email        = Column(String(100), unique=True)
    department   = Column(String(100))
    salary       = Column(Float, default=0.0)
    is_active    = Column(Boolean, default=True)
    created_at   = Column(
        DateTime(timezone=True),
        server_default=func.now()
    )

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<Employee {self.name}>"

    def to_dict(self):
        return {
            "id": self.id,
            "name": self.name,
            "email": self.email,
            "department": self.department,
            "salary": self.salary,
        }
```

# Step 5: repositories/student_repo.py
## Like @Repository in Spring Boot

```python
# repositories/student_repo.py
# ==========================================
# Student Repository
# Like @Repository in Spring Boot
# All database queries live here
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from sqlalchemy import or_
from models.student import Student
from typing import Optional, List
import logging

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

class StudentRepository:
    """
    All database operations for Student.
    Like StudentRepository extends JpaRepository
    in Spring Boot.
    """

    def __init__(self, db: Session):
        # db session injected
        # like @Autowired in Spring Boot
        self.db = db

    # ==========================================
    # CREATE
    # ==========================================
    def save(self, student: Student) -> Student:
        """Saves a student to database."""
        try:
            self.db.add(student)
            self.db.commit()
            self.db.refresh(student)
            logger.info(f"Saved student: {student.name}")
            return student
        except Exception as e:
            self.db.rollback()
            logger.error(f"Error saving student: {e}")
            raise

    # ==========================================
    # READ
    # ==========================================
    def find_by_id(
        self, student_id: int
    ) -> Optional[Student]:
        """Finds student by ID."""
        return self.db.query(Student).filter(
            Student.id == student_id
        ).first()

    def find_by_email(
        self, email: str
    ) -> Optional[Student]:
        """Finds student by email."""
        return self.db.query(Student).filter(
            Student.email == email
        ).first()

    def find_all(
        self,
        skip: int = 0,
        limit: int = 100
    ) -> List[Student]:
        """Gets all students."""
        return self.db.query(Student)\
            .offset(skip)\
            .limit(limit)\
            .all()

    def find_by_grade(
        self, grade: str
    ) -> List[Student]:
        """Finds students by grade."""
        return self.db.query(Student).filter(
            Student.grade == grade
        ).all()

    def search(self, keyword: str) -> List[Student]:
        """Searches by name or email."""
        return self.db.query(Student).filter(
            or_(
                Student.name.contains(keyword),
                Student.email.contains(keyword)
            )
        ).all()

    def count(self) -> int:
        """Counts total students."""
        return self.db.query(Student).count()

    # ==========================================
    # UPDATE
    # ==========================================
    def update(
        self,
        student_id: int,
        data: dict
    ) -> Optional[Student]:
        """Updates student data."""
        student = self.find_by_id(student_id)
        if not student:
            return None

        for key, value in data.items():
            if hasattr(student, key):
                setattr(student, key, value)

        self.db.commit()
        self.db.refresh(student)
        return student

    # ==========================================
    # DELETE
    # ==========================================
    def delete(self, student_id: int) -> bool:
        """Deletes a student."""
        student = self.find_by_id(student_id)
        if not student:
            return False

        self.db.delete(student)
        self.db.commit()
        return True

    def exists_by_email(self, email: str) -> bool:
        """Checks if email exists."""
        return self.db.query(Student).filter(
            Student.email == email
        ).first() is not None
```

---

# Step 6: services/student_service.py
## Like @Service in Spring Boot

```python
# services/student_service.py
# ==========================================
# Student Service
# Like @Service in Spring Boot
# Business logic lives here
# ==========================================

from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from models.student import Student
from repositories.student_repo import StudentRepository
from typing import Optional, List
import logging

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

class StudentService:
    """
    Business logic for students.
    Like @Service in Spring Boot.
    """

    def __init__(self, db: Session):
        # Inject repository
        # like @Autowired StudentRepository
        self.repo = StudentRepository(db)

    def create_student(
        self,
        name: str,
        email: str,
        age: int,
        grade: str
    ) -> dict:
        """Creates a new student."""

        # Business logic: check email
        if self.repo.exists_by_email(email):
            raise ValueError(
                f"Email {email} already exists"
            )

        # Business logic: validate age
        if age < 5 or age > 30:
            raise ValueError(
                "Age must be between 5 and 30"
            )

        # Create student
        student = Student(
            name=name,
            email=email,
            age=age,
            grade=grade
        )

        saved = self.repo.save(student)
        logger.info(f"Student created: {name}")
        return saved.to_dict()

    def get_student(self, student_id: int) -> dict:
        """Gets one student."""
        student = self.repo.find_by_id(student_id)
        if not student:
            raise ValueError(
                f"Student {student_id} not found"
            )
        return student.to_dict()

    def get_all_students(
        self,
        skip: int = 0,
        limit: int = 100
    ) -> List[dict]:
        """Gets all students."""
        students = self.repo.find_all(skip, limit)
        return [s.to_dict() for s in students]

    def update_student(
        self,
        student_id: int,
        data: dict
    ) -> dict:
        """Updates student."""
        student = self.repo.update(student_id, data)
        if not student:
            raise ValueError(
                f"Student {student_id} not found"
            )
        return student.to_dict()

    def delete_student(self, student_id: int) -> bool:
        """Deletes student."""
        if not self.repo.find_by_id(student_id):
            raise ValueError(
                f"Student {student_id} not found"
            )
        return self.repo.delete(student_id)

    def search_students(
        self, keyword: str
    ) -> List[dict]:
        """Searches students."""
        students = self.repo.search(keyword)
        return [s.to_dict() for s in students]
```

---

# Step 7: routers/student_router.py
## Like @RestController in Spring Boot

```python
# routers/student_router.py
# ==========================================
# Student Router
# Like @RestController in Spring Boot
# ==========================================

from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends, HTTPException
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from pydantic import BaseModel
from typing import Optional, List
from config.database import get_db
from services.student_service import StudentService

router = APIRouter(
    prefix="/students",
    tags=["Students"]
)

# Request/Response schemas
class StudentCreate(BaseModel):
    name: str
    email: str
    age: int
    grade: str

class StudentUpdate(BaseModel):
    name: Optional[str] = None
    grade: Optional[str] = None
    age: Optional[int] = None


# ==========================================
# Dependency - injects service with db
# Like @Autowired in Spring Boot
# ==========================================
def get_student_service(
    db: Session = Depends(get_db)
) -> StudentService:
    return StudentService(db)


@router.post("/", status_code=201)
def create_student(
    data: StudentCreate,
    service: StudentService = Depends(
        get_student_service
    )
):
    try:
        return service.create_student(
            data.name,
            data.email,
            data.age,
            data.grade
        )
    except ValueError as e:
        raise HTTPException(400, str(e))


@router.get("/")
def get_all_students(
    skip: int = 0,
    limit: int = 10,
    service: StudentService = Depends(
        get_student_service
    )
):
    return service.get_all_students(skip, limit)


@router.get("/{student_id}")
def get_student(
    student_id: int,
    service: StudentService = Depends(
        get_student_service
    )
):
    try:
        return service.get_student(student_id)
    except ValueError as e:
        raise HTTPException(404, str(e))


@router.put("/{student_id}")
def update_student(
    student_id: int,
    data: StudentUpdate,
    service: StudentService = Depends(
        get_student_service
    )
):
    try:
        update_data = data.dict(exclude_unset=True)
        return service.update_student(
            student_id, update_data
        )
    except ValueError as e:
        raise HTTPException(404, str(e))


@router.delete("/{student_id}")
def delete_student(
    student_id: int,
    service: StudentService = Depends(
        get_student_service
    )
):
    try:
        service.delete_student(student_id)
        return {"message": "Student deleted"}
    except ValueError as e:
        raise HTTPException(404, str(e))


@router.get("/search/{keyword}")
def search_students(
    keyword: str,
    service: StudentService = Depends(
        get_student_service
    )
):
    return service.search_students(keyword)
```

---

# Step 8: main.py

```python
# main.py
# ==========================================
# Main application entry point
# Like @SpringBootApplication
# ==========================================

from fastapi import FastAPI
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware
from contextlib import asynccontextmanager
import logging

from config.database import (
    test_connection,
    create_tables
)
from routers import student_router, employee_router

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

# ==========================================
# Startup and shutdown events
# Like @PostConstruct in Spring Boot
# ==========================================
@asynccontextmanager
async def lifespan(app: FastAPI):
    # Startup
    logger.info("Starting application...")
    test_connection()
    create_tables()
    logger.info("Application ready!")
    yield
    # Shutdown
    logger.info("Shutting down...")

# ==========================================
# Create app
# ==========================================
app = FastAPI(
    title="Python Spring Boot Style App",
    description="Azure SQL + FastAPI",
    version="1.0.0",
    lifespan=lifespan
)

# CORS
app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=["*"],
    allow_methods=["*"],
    allow_headers=["*"],
)

# ==========================================
# Register routers
# Like @ComponentScan in Spring Boot
# ==========================================
app.include_router(student_router.router)
app.include_router(employee_router.router)

@app.get("/")
def home():
    return {
        "message": "API is running",
        "database": "Azure SQL",
        "docs": "/docs"
    }

@app.get("/health")
def health():
    is_connected = test_connection()
    return {
        "status": "healthy" if is_connected else "unhealthy",
        "database": is_connected
    }
```

---

# Spring Boot vs Python comparison

```
Spring Boot                Python (FastAPI)
─────────────────────────────────────────────
application.properties  →  .env file
DataSource              →  engine (SQLAlchemy)
HikariCP pool           →  QueuePool
@Entity                 →  SQLAlchemy model
@Repository             →  Repository class
@Service                →  Service class
@RestController         →  APIRouter
@Autowired              →  Depends()
@Transactional          →  Session + commit
JpaRepository           →  SQLAlchemy Session
@SpringBootApplication  →  main.py + lifespan
@ComponentScan          →  include_router()
@PostConstruct          →  lifespan startup
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
Setup once:
  config/database.py → engine, SessionLocal, Base

Use anywhere:
  from config.database import get_db, Base

Models:
  from config.database import Base
  class MyModel(Base): ...

Repositories:
  def __init__(self, db: Session):
      self.db = db

Services:
  def __init__(self, db: Session):
      self.repo = MyRepo(db)

Routers:
  db: Session = Depends(get_db)
  service = MyService(db)
```

## Copilot

Here's a **complete, simple, easy-to-revise guide on GitHub/Git concepts**.

---

# Easy way to remember Git

```
Git = a time machine for your code

SAVE    → commit
TRAVEL  → checkout
COPY    → branch
COMBINE → merge/rebase
UPLOAD  → push
DOWNLOAD→ pull
HIDE    → stash
TAG     → release point
```

---

# 1) GIT STASH

Stash means **temporarily save changes** without committing.

---

## Simple idea
```
You are working on a feature.
Boss says: fix this urgent bug NOW.
You cannot commit unfinished work.
Solution: STASH your changes.
```

---

## All stash commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# BASIC STASH
# ==========================================

# Save current changes to stash
git stash

# Save with a message
git stash save "working on login feature"

# List all stashes
git stash list

# Apply most recent stash (keeps stash)
git stash apply

# Apply most recent stash (removes from stash)
git stash pop

# Apply specific stash
git stash apply stash@{2}

# Drop specific stash
git stash drop stash@{0}

# Clear all stashes
git stash clear

# Show what is in stash
git stash show
git stash show -p    # detailed diff

# Stash including untracked files
git stash -u
git stash --include-untracked

# Stash with a branch
git stash branch new-branch-name
```

---

## Simple example

```bash
# You are on feature branch, working on login
git status
# Shows: modified login.py

# Boss says fix urgent bug
# Stash your work
git stash save "half done login feature"

# Switch to main
git checkout main

# Fix the bug
git add bugfix.py
git commit -m "fix urgent bug"

# Go back to feature branch
git checkout feature/login

# Get your stash back
git stash pop

# Now continue your work
```

---

# 2) GIT POP

`git stash pop` = apply stash + remove from stash list

---

## stash apply vs stash pop

```bash
# apply - keeps stash in list
git stash apply
# stash is still in list

# pop - applies AND removes from list
git stash pop
# stash is gone from list
```

---

## Example

```bash
# See stash list
git stash list
# stash@{0}: working on login
# stash@{1}: working on dashboard

# Pop most recent (stash@{0})
git stash pop

# Pop specific stash
git stash pop stash@{1}

# If conflict during pop
git stash pop
# CONFLICT - fix conflicts then
git add .
git stash drop    # manually remove stash
```

---

# 3) GIT REBASE

Rebase means **move your branch on top of another branch**.

---

## Simple idea

```
BEFORE REBASE:
main:    A → B → C
feature:     ↘ D → E

AFTER REBASE:
main:    A → B → C
feature:             ↘ D' → E'

Feature branch moved on top of latest main.
```

---

## Merge vs Rebase

```
MERGE:
- keeps all history
- creates merge commit
- messier history

REBASE:
- cleaner linear history
- no merge commit
- rewrites commits
```

---

## All rebase commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# BASIC REBASE
# ==========================================

# Go to feature branch
git checkout feature/login

# Rebase on top of main
git rebase main

# ==========================================
# INTERACTIVE REBASE
# Lets you edit, squash, reorder commits
# ==========================================

# Rebase last 3 commits interactively
git rebase -i HEAD~3

# In editor you will see:
# pick abc123 commit message 1
# pick def456 commit message 2
# pick ghi789 commit message 3

# Change pick to:
# pick   = keep commit as is
# squash = combine with previous commit
# reword = change commit message
# drop   = remove commit
# edit   = pause and edit commit

# ==========================================
# ABORT REBASE
# ==========================================
git rebase --abort

# ==========================================
# CONTINUE REBASE after fixing conflict
# ==========================================
git add .
git rebase --continue

# ==========================================
# SKIP a commit during rebase
# ==========================================
git rebase --skip
```

---

## Simple rebase example

```bash
# Feature branch is behind main
git checkout feature/login

# Update main first
git checkout main
git pull origin main

# Go back to feature
git checkout feature/login

# Rebase on main
git rebase main

# If conflicts appear:
# Fix conflict in files
git add fixed_file.py
git rebase --continue

# Push (need force because history changed)
git push origin feature/login --force-with-lease
```

---

# 4) GIT MERGE

Merge means **combining two branches**.

---

## Types of merge

```
FAST-FORWARD MERGE:
main:    A → B
feature:          → C → D
result:  A → B → C → D
(no merge commit, straight line)

3-WAY MERGE:
main:    A → B → C
feature:     ↘ D → E
result:  A → B → C → M  (M = merge commit)
                   ↗
               D → E
```

---

## All merge commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# BASIC MERGE
# ==========================================

# Switch to main
git checkout main

# Merge feature into main
git merge feature/login

# ==========================================
# MERGE WITH COMMIT MESSAGE
# ==========================================
git merge feature/login -m "merge login feature"

# ==========================================
# NO FAST FORWARD
# Always creates merge commit
# ==========================================
git merge --no-ff feature/login

# ==========================================
# SQUASH MERGE
# Combines all commits into one
# ==========================================
git merge --squash feature/login
git commit -m "add login feature"

# ==========================================
# ABORT MERGE
# ==========================================
git merge --abort

# ==========================================
# CHECK MERGE CONFLICTS
# ==========================================
git status
# Shows conflicted files

# After fixing conflicts
git add .
git commit -m "resolve merge conflicts"
```

---

## Merge conflict example

```bash
# Merge feature into main
git merge feature/login

# Conflict in login.py
# Open login.py - you will see:

<<<<<<< HEAD (main)
def login():
    print("main version")
=======
def login():
    print("feature version")
>>>>>>> feature/login

# Fix it manually - keep what you want:
def login():
    print("feature version")

# Save file then:
git add login.py
git commit -m "resolve merge conflict"
```

---

# 5) PR (Pull Request)

A PR means **requesting to merge your branch into another**.

---

## Simple flow

```
1. Create branch
2. Make changes
3. Push branch
4. Create PR on GitHub
5. Team reviews code
6. Approve and merge
```

---

## Commands for PR workflow

```bash
# ==========================================
# STEP 1: Create branch
# ==========================================
git checkout main
git pull origin main
git checkout -b feature/login

# ==========================================
# STEP 2: Make changes and commit
# ==========================================
git add .
git commit -m "add login feature"

# ==========================================
# STEP 3: Push branch to GitHub
# ==========================================
git push origin feature/login

# ==========================================
# STEP 4: Create PR on GitHub
# Go to GitHub → New Pull Request
# base: main ← compare: feature/login
# ==========================================

# ==========================================
# STEP 5: After PR is merged, cleanup
# ==========================================
git checkout main
git pull origin main
git branch -d feature/login
git push origin --delete feature/login
```

---

# 6) BRANCHING

Branch means **a separate line of development**.

---

## All branch commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# CREATE BRANCH
# ==========================================

# Create branch
git branch feature/login

# Create and switch to branch
git checkout -b feature/login

# New way (git 2.23+)
git switch -c feature/login

# Create from specific commit
git checkout -b feature/login abc123

# Create from another branch
git checkout -b feature/login develop

# ==========================================
# VIEW BRANCHES
# ==========================================

# List local branches
git branch

# List all branches (local + remote)
git branch -a

# List remote branches only
git branch -r

# See last commit on each branch
git branch -v

# ==========================================
# SWITCH BRANCH
# ==========================================

git checkout main
git switch main    # new way

# ==========================================
# DELETE BRANCH
# ==========================================

# Delete local branch (safe)
git branch -d feature/login

# Force delete local branch
git branch -D feature/login

# Delete remote branch
git push origin --delete feature/login

# ==========================================
# RENAME BRANCH
# ==========================================

# Rename current branch
git branch -m new-name

# Rename specific branch
git branch -m old-name new-name

# ==========================================
# TRACK REMOTE BRANCH
# ==========================================

git checkout --track origin/feature/login
```

---

# 7) TAGGING

Tags mark **specific points in history** like releases.

---

## Types of tags

```
LIGHTWEIGHT TAG → just a pointer to commit
ANNOTATED TAG   → full object with message, date, author
```

---

## All tag commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# CREATE TAG
# ==========================================

# Lightweight tag
git tag v1.0

# Annotated tag (recommended)
git tag -a v1.0 -m "Version 1.0 release"

# Tag a specific commit
git tag -a v1.0 abc123 -m "Version 1.0"

# ==========================================
# VIEW TAGS
# ==========================================

# List all tags
git tag

# List tags with pattern
git tag -l "v1.*"

# Show tag details
git show v1.0

# ==========================================
# PUSH TAGS
# ==========================================

# Push one tag
git push origin v1.0

# Push all tags
git push origin --tags

# ==========================================
# DELETE TAG
# ==========================================

# Delete local tag
git tag -d v1.0

# Delete remote tag
git push origin --delete v1.0

# ==========================================
# CHECKOUT TAG
# ==========================================

# Go to tag (detached HEAD)
git checkout v1.0

# Create branch from tag
git checkout -b hotfix/v1.0 v1.0
```

---

# 8) PATCHES

Patches mean **exporting commits as files** to share.

---

## All patch commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# CREATE PATCH
# ==========================================

# Create patch for last commit
git format-patch -1

# Create patch for last 3 commits
git format-patch -3

# Create patch from specific commit
git format-patch abc123

# Create patch comparing two branches
git format-patch main..feature/login

# Save patch to specific directory
git format-patch -3 -o patches/

# ==========================================
# APPLY PATCH
# ==========================================

# Apply patch file
git apply patch-file.patch

# Apply patch with commit info
git am patch-file.patch

# Apply all patches in directory
git am patches/*.patch

# Check if patch applies cleanly
git apply --check patch-file.patch

# ==========================================
# CREATE DIFF PATCH
# ==========================================

# Create diff patch
git diff > my-changes.patch

# Apply diff patch
git apply my-changes.patch
```

---

# 9) IF BRANCH GOT DELETED

How to **recover a deleted branch**.

---

## Method 1: Using reflog

```bash
# ==========================================
# RECOVER DELETED BRANCH
# ==========================================

# Step 1: Find the lost commit
git reflog

# You will see:
# abc123 HEAD@{0}: checkout: moving from feature/login to main
# def456 HEAD@{1}: commit: add login feature
# ghi789 HEAD@{2}: commit: add login form

# Step 2: Create branch from that commit
git checkout -b feature/login def456

# Or using HEAD@{n}
git checkout -b feature/login HEAD@{1}
```

---

## Method 2: Using git fsck

```bash
# Find dangling commits (orphaned commits)
git fsck --lost-found

# You will see:
# dangling commit abc123

# Recover it
git checkout -b recovered-branch abc123
```

---

## Method 3: Remote branch still exists

```bash
# If remote branch still exists
git checkout --track origin/feature/login

# Or
git fetch origin
git checkout -b feature/login origin/feature/login
```

---

# 10) GIT REFLOG

Reflog records **every movement of HEAD**.

---

## Simple idea
```
Reflog = your git safety net
Even if you delete branch or reset,
reflog remembers everything for 90 days.
```

---

## All reflog commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# VIEW REFLOG
# ==========================================

# Show all HEAD movements
git reflog

# You see:
# abc123 HEAD@{0}: commit: add feature
# def456 HEAD@{1}: checkout: moved to main
# ghi789 HEAD@{2}: reset: moving to HEAD~1

# Show reflog for specific branch
git reflog show feature/login

# Show with dates
git reflog --date=iso

# ==========================================
# RECOVER USING REFLOG
# ==========================================

# Undo accidental reset
git reset --hard HEAD@{1}

# Recover deleted commit
git checkout -b recovered HEAD@{3}

# Find lost commit
git reflog | grep "commit message"
```

---

## Practical recovery example

```bash
# You accidentally did hard reset
git reset --hard HEAD~3
# Oh no! Lost 3 commits!

# Check reflog
git reflog
# abc123 HEAD@{0}: reset: moving to HEAD~3
# def456 HEAD@{1}: commit: my important work
# ghi789 HEAD@{2}: commit: more work
# jkl012 HEAD@{3}: commit: latest work

# Recover to before the reset
git reset --hard HEAD@{1}
# All commits restored!
```

---

# 11) Advanced Git Commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# CHERRY PICK
# Pick specific commit from another branch
# ==========================================
git cherry-pick abc123

# Cherry pick multiple commits
git cherry-pick abc123 def456

# Cherry pick a range
git cherry-pick abc123..def456

# ==========================================
# GIT BISECT
# Find which commit introduced a bug
# ==========================================
git bisect start
git bisect bad              # current is bad
git bisect good v1.0        # v1.0 was good
# Git will checkout middle commit
# Test it, then:
git bisect good  # or
git bisect bad
# Repeat until bug commit found
git bisect reset            # end bisect

# ==========================================
# GIT BLAME
# See who wrote each line
# ==========================================
git blame filename.py

# ==========================================
# GIT LOG
# ==========================================

# Basic log
git log

# One line per commit
git log --oneline

# With graph
git log --oneline --graph --all

# Last 5 commits
git log -5

# Search commit messages
git log --grep="login"

# Commits by author
git log --author="Aman"

# Commits between dates
git log --after="2024-01-01" --before="2024-12-31"

# Show changes in each commit
git log -p

# ==========================================
# GIT RESET
# ==========================================

# Soft reset - keeps changes staged
git reset --soft HEAD~1

# Mixed reset - keeps changes unstaged
git reset --mixed HEAD~1

# Hard reset - discards all changes
git reset --hard HEAD~1

# ==========================================
# GIT REVERT
# Creates new commit that undoes changes
# Safe for shared branches
# ==========================================
git revert abc123
git revert HEAD~2..HEAD
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
STASH       → hide changes temporarily
STASH POP   → bring back hidden changes
REBASE      → move branch on top of another
MERGE       → combine two branches
PR          → request to merge branch
BRANCHING   → separate line of development
TAGGING     → mark release points
PATCHES     → export commits as files
REFLOG      → history of HEAD movements
CHERRY PICK → pick specific commit
BISECT      → find bug commit
BLAME       → see who wrote what
RESET       → go back in time
REVERT      → undo commit safely
```

---

# Interview-ready one-line answers

## What is git stash?
Temporarily saves uncommitted changes so you can work on something else.

## Stash pop vs apply?
Pop applies and removes from stash. Apply keeps it in stash list.

## Merge vs rebase?
Merge creates a merge commit and keeps full history. Rebase creates a clean linear history.

## What is a PR?
A request to merge one branch into another with code review.

## What is git tag?
A named pointer to a specific commit, usually used for releases.

## What is reflog?
A log of all HEAD movements, useful for recovering lost commits or branches.

## How to recover deleted branch?
Use `git reflog` to find the last commit of that branch then `git checkout -b branch-name commit-hash`.

## Copilot

Here's a **complete Docker image template for Python using Alpine** (lightweight).

---

# Why Alpine?

```
Ubuntu based image  → 900MB+
Python slim image   → 120MB
Python Alpine image → 50MB

Alpine = smallest + most secure
```

---

# 1) Basic Python Alpine Dockerfile

```dockerfile
# Dockerfile
# ==========================================
# Basic Python Alpine Image
# ==========================================

# Alpine based Python image
# 3.12-alpine = Python 3.12 on Alpine Linux
FROM python:3.12-alpine

# Set working directory
WORKDIR /app

# Copy requirements first
# (Docker caches this layer)
COPY requirements.txt .

# Install dependencies
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Copy application code
COPY . .

# Run the application
CMD ["python", "main.py"]
```

---

# 2) Production Grade Template

```dockerfile
# Dockerfile
# ==========================================
# Production Python Alpine Image
# Multi-stage + Security + Optimized
# ==========================================

# ==========================================
# STAGE 1: Builder
# Install dependencies here
# ==========================================
FROM python:3.12-alpine AS builder

# Set environment variables
ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1 \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1 \
    PIP_NO_CACHE_DIR=1 \
    PIP_DISABLE_PIP_VERSION_CHECK=1

WORKDIR /app

# Install build dependencies
# These are needed to compile some Python packages
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    gcc \
    musl-dev \
    libffi-dev \
    openssl-dev \
    python3-dev \
    build-base

# Copy and install requirements
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir \
    --prefix=/install \
    -r requirements.txt

# ==========================================
# STAGE 2: Final image
# Only copy what we need
# No build tools = smaller image
# ==========================================
FROM python:3.12-alpine AS final

# Set environment variables
ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1 \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1 \
    PATH="/install/bin:$PATH" \
    PYTHONPATH="/install/lib/python3.12/site-packages"

# Create non-root user for security
RUN addgroup -S appgroup && \
    adduser -S appuser -G appgroup

WORKDIR /app

# Copy installed packages from builder
COPY --from=builder /install /install

# Copy application code
COPY --chown=appuser:appgroup . .

# Switch to non-root user
USER appuser

# Expose port
EXPOSE 8000

# Health check
HEALTHCHECK --interval=30s \
            --timeout=10s \
            --start-period=5s \
            --retries=3 \
    CMD wget -qO- http://localhost:8000/health \
    || exit 1

# Run application
CMD ["python", "main.py"]
```

---

# 3) FastAPI Alpine Template

```dockerfile
# Dockerfile
# ==========================================
# FastAPI + Python Alpine
# ==========================================

FROM python:3.12-alpine AS builder

ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1 \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1

WORKDIR /app

# Install system dependencies needed for FastAPI
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    gcc \
    musl-dev \
    libffi-dev \
    openssl-dev \
    python3-dev \
    build-base \
    curl

# Install Python dependencies
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir \
    --prefix=/install \
    -r requirements.txt

# ==========================================
# Final stage
# ==========================================
FROM python:3.12-alpine AS final

ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1 \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1 \
    PATH="/install/bin:$PATH" \
    PYTHONPATH="/install/lib/python3.12/site-packages"

# Install runtime dependencies only
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    curl \
    libffi \
    openssl

# Create non-root user
RUN addgroup -S appgroup && \
    adduser -S appuser -G appgroup

WORKDIR /app

# Copy packages from builder
COPY --from=builder /install /install

# Copy app code
COPY --chown=appuser:appgroup . .

USER appuser

EXPOSE 8000

# Health check for FastAPI
HEALTHCHECK --interval=30s \
            --timeout=10s \
            --start-period=10s \
            --retries=3 \
    CMD curl -f http://localhost:8000/health \
    || exit 1

# Run FastAPI with uvicorn
CMD ["uvicorn", "main:app", \
     "--host", "0.0.0.0", \
     "--port", "8000", \
     "--workers", "4"]
```

# 4) FastAPI + Azure SQL Alpine Template

```dockerfile
# Dockerfile
# ==========================================
# FastAPI + Azure SQL + Python Alpine
# ==========================================

FROM python:3.12-alpine AS builder

ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1 \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1

WORKDIR /app

# Install dependencies needed for:
# - pyodbc (Azure SQL)
# - SQLAlchemy
# - FastAPI
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    gcc \
    musl-dev \
    libffi-dev \
    openssl-dev \
    python3-dev \
    build-base \
    unixodbc-dev \
    curl

# Install ODBC driver for Azure SQL
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    --repository http://dl-cdn.alpinelinux.org/alpine/edge/testing \
    msodbcsql18 \
    mssql-tools18

COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir \
    --prefix=/install \
    -r requirements.txt

# ==========================================
# Final stage
# ==========================================
FROM python:3.12-alpine AS final

ENV PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1 \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1 \
    PATH="/install/bin:$PATH" \
    PYTHONPATH="/install/lib/python3.12/site-packages"

# Runtime dependencies for Azure SQL
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    curl \
    libffi \
    openssl \
    unixodbc \
    && apk add --no-cache \
    --repository http://dl-cdn.alpinelinux.org/alpine/edge/testing \
    msodbcsql18

# Non-root user
RUN addgroup -S appgroup && \
    adduser -S appuser -G appgroup

WORKDIR /app

COPY --from=builder /install /install
COPY --chown=appuser:appgroup . .

USER appuser

EXPOSE 8000

HEALTHCHECK --interval=30s \
            --timeout=10s \
            --retries=3 \
    CMD curl -f http://localhost:8000/health \
    || exit 1

CMD ["uvicorn", "main:app", \
     "--host", "0.0.0.0", \
     "--port", "8000"]
```

# 6) docker-compose.yml

```yaml
# docker-compose.yml
# ==========================================
# Full stack with Python Alpine
# ==========================================

version: '3.8'

services:

  # ==========================================
  # FastAPI Application
  # ==========================================
  app:
    build:
      context: .
      dockerfile: Dockerfile
      target: final
    container_name: fastapi_app
    restart: unless-stopped
    ports:
      - "8000:8000"
    environment:
      - APP_ENV=production
      - DEBUG=False
      - DATABASE_URL=${DATABASE_URL}
      - OPENAI_API_KEY=${OPENAI_API_KEY}
    env_file:
      - .env
    depends_on:
      db:
        condition: service_healthy
    networks:
      - app_network
    volumes:
      - ./logs:/app/logs
    healthcheck:
      test: ["CMD", "curl", "-f",
             "http://localhost:8000/health"]
      interval: 30s
      timeout: 10s
      retries: 3

  # ==========================================
  # PostgreSQL Database
  # ==========================================
  db:
    image: postgres:16-alpine
    container_name: postgres_db
    restart: unless-stopped
    environment:
      POSTGRES_USER: ${DB_USER}
      POSTGRES_PASSWORD: ${DB_PASSWORD}
      POSTGRES_DB: ${DB_NAME}
    ports:
      - "5432:5432"
    volumes:
      - postgres_data:/var/lib/postgresql/data
    networks:
      - app_network
    healthcheck:
      test: ["CMD-SHELL",
             "pg_isready -U ${DB_USER}"]
      interval: 10s
      timeout: 5s
      retries: 5

  # ==========================================
  # Redis Cache
  # ==========================================
  redis:
    image: redis:7-alpine
    container_name: redis_cache
    restart: unless-stopped
    ports:
      - "6379:6379"
    networks:
      - app_network
    healthcheck:
      test: ["CMD", "redis-cli", "ping"]
      interval: 10s
      timeout: 5s
      retries: 3

  # ==========================================
  # Nginx Reverse Proxy
  # ==========================================
  nginx:
    image: nginx:alpine
    container_name: nginx_proxy
    restart: unless-stopped
    ports:
      - "80:80"
      - "443:443"
    volumes:
      - ./nginx.conf:/etc/nginx/nginx.conf
    depends_on:
      - app
    networks:
      - app_network

# ==========================================
# Networks
# ==========================================
networks:
  app_network:
    driver: bridge

# ==========================================
# Volumes
# ==========================================
volumes:
  postgres_data:
```

# 8) All Docker commands

```bash
# ==========================================
# BUILD
# ==========================================

# Build image
docker build -t myapp:latest .

# Build with specific stage
docker build --target final -t myapp:latest .

# Build with no cache
docker build --no-cache -t myapp:latest .

# Build with build args
docker build \
  --build-arg APP_ENV=production \
  -t myapp:latest .

# ==========================================
# RUN
# ==========================================

# Run container
docker run -d \
  --name myapp \
  -p 8000:8000 \
  myapp:latest

# Run with env file
docker run -d \
  --name myapp \
  -p 8000:8000 \
  --env-file .env \
  myapp:latest

# Run interactively
docker run -it \
  --name myapp \
  myapp:latest \
  /bin/sh

# ==========================================
# DOCKER COMPOSE
# ==========================================

# Start all services
docker-compose up -d

# Start with build
docker-compose up -d --build

# Stop all services
docker-compose down

# Stop and remove volumes
docker-compose down -v

# View logs
docker-compose logs -f

# View logs for specific service
docker-compose logs -f app

# ==========================================
# MANAGE
# ==========================================

# List running containers
docker ps

# List all containers
docker ps -a

# List images
docker images

# Stop container
docker stop myapp

# Remove container
docker rm myapp

# Remove image
docker rmi myapp:latest

# View container logs
docker logs myapp -f

# Execute command in container
docker exec -it myapp /bin/sh

# ==========================================
# CLEANUP
# ==========================================

# Remove all stopped containers
docker container prune

# Remove unused images
docker image prune

# Remove everything unused
docker system prune -a
```

---

# 9) Environment file

```bash
# .env
# ==========================================
# Environment Variables
# ==========================================

# App
APP_ENV=production
DEBUG=False
APP_PORT=8000

# Database
DATABASE_URL=postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/mydb
DB_USER=myuser
DB_PASSWORD=mypassword
DB_NAME=mydb

# Azure SQL
AZURE_SQL_SERVER=server.database.windows.net
AZURE_SQL_DATABASE=mydb
AZURE_SQL_USERNAME=myuser
AZURE_SQL_PASSWORD=mypassword

# Redis
REDIS_URL=redis://redis:6379

# OpenAI
OPENAI_API_KEY=sk-your-key

# Security
SECRET_KEY=your-secret-key
```

---

# Image size comparison

```
Image                    Size
─────────────────────────────
python:3.12              1.02GB
python:3.12-slim         130MB
python:3.12-alpine       50MB
Multi-stage alpine       ~80MB
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
FROM python:3.12-alpine  → base alpine image
WORKDIR /app             → set working directory
COPY requirements.txt .  → copy deps first
RUN apk add --no-cache   → install system deps
RUN pip install          → install python deps
COPY . .                 → copy app code
USER appuser             → non-root user
EXPOSE 8000              → open port
HEALTHCHECK              → monitor container
CMD                      → run command

Multi-stage build:
  Stage 1 (builder) → compile/install
  Stage 2 (final)   → copy only needed files

apk = Alpine package manager
apk add = install package
--no-cache = don't cache package list
```

# ==========================================
# Basic Python Alpine Image
# ==========================================

# Alpine based Python image
# 3.12-alpine = Python 3.12 on Alpine Linux
FROM python:3.12-alpine

# Set working directory
WORKDIR /app

# Install system dependencies required by pyodbc on Alpine
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    gcc \
    g++ \
    musl-dev \
    unixodbc \
    unixodbc-dev

# Copy requirements first
# (Docker caches this layer)
COPY requirements.txt .

# Install dependencies

# Copy application code

# Run from app package directory so current imports resolve
WORKDIR /app/my_app

# Run the application

## Copilot

Here's a **complete line-by-line explanation** of your Dockerfile.

---

# Full Dockerfile Explained

```dockerfile
# Dockerfile
```
```
This is just a comment.
The file must be named exactly "Dockerfile"
Docker looks for this file when you run:
docker build .
```

---

```dockerfile
# ==========================================
# Basic Python Alpine Image
# ==========================================
```
```
These are just comment lines.
They do nothing but explain what this file does.
Good practice to add comments.
```

---

```dockerfile
# Alpine based Python image
# 3.12-alpine = Python 3.12 on Alpine Linux
FROM python:3.12-alpine
```
```
FROM = first instruction in every Dockerfile
       tells Docker which base image to use

python:3.12-alpine means:
  python    = official Python image
  3.12      = Python version 3.12
  alpine    = built on Alpine Linux OS

Why Alpine?
  Ubuntu image  → 900MB
  Alpine image  → 50MB
  Much smaller and more secure

This downloads image from Docker Hub
hub.docker.com/_/python
```

---

```dockerfile
# Set working directory
WORKDIR /app
```
```
WORKDIR = sets the current directory
          inside the container

Like doing: cd /app

All commands after this run inside /app
If /app does not exist, Docker creates it

Why /app?
  Common convention for application code
  Clean separation from system files
```

---

```dockerfile
# Install system dependencies required by pyodbc on Alpine
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    gcc \
    g++ \
    musl-dev \
    unixodbc \
    unixodbc-dev
```
```
RUN = executes a command during image build
      Creates a new layer in the image

apk = Alpine Package Keeper
      Alpine's package manager
      Like apt-get in Ubuntu
      Like yum in CentOS

add = install packages

--no-cache = do NOT store package index
             keeps image smaller
             without this: apk downloads
             and saves package list = bigger image

\ = line continuation
    same as writing one long line
    used for readability

gcc
  = GNU C Compiler
  = needed to compile C code
  = some Python packages have C extensions
  = pyodbc needs this to compile

g++
  = GNU C++ Compiler
  = needed for C++ code compilation
  = some packages need C++ compiler

musl-dev
  = Alpine's C standard library
  = Alpine uses musl instead of glibc
  = development headers for musl
  = needed when compiling C packages

unixodbc
  = ODBC runtime library
  = ODBC = Open Database Connectivity
  = standard way to connect to databases
  = pyodbc uses this to talk to SQL Server
  = Azure SQL needs this

unixodbc-dev
  = Development headers for unixodbc
  = needed when compiling pyodbc
  = contains .h header files
  = without this pyodbc cannot compile

Simple way to remember:
  gcc + g++        = compilers
  musl-dev         = Alpine C library
  unixodbc         = database driver runtime
  unixodbc-dev     = database driver headers
```

---

```dockerfile
# Copy requirements first
# (Docker caches this layer)
COPY requirements.txt .
```
```
COPY = copies files from your computer
       into the Docker container

Format:
  COPY <source on your machine> <destination in container>

requirements.txt = source file on your machine
.                = current directory in container
                   which is /app (set by WORKDIR)

So this copies:
  your-machine/requirements.txt
  → container/app/requirements.txt

WHY COPY REQUIREMENTS FIRST?
  Very important optimization!

  Docker builds in layers.
  Each instruction = one layer.
  Docker CACHES layers.

  If requirements.txt has not changed:
  → Docker uses cached layer
  → Skips pip install
  → Much faster build

  If you copy all files first then pip install:
  → Any code change = pip install runs again
  → Very slow!

  Best practice:
  1. COPY requirements.txt  ← copy deps file
  2. RUN pip install        ← install deps
  3. COPY . .               ← copy all code
```

---

```dockerfile
# Install dependencies
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt
```
```
RUN = executes command during build

pip install = Python package installer

--no-cache-dir
  = do not save pip cache
  = pip normally saves downloaded packages
    in cache folder for reuse
  = in Docker we do not need this cache
  = saves disk space
  = makes image smaller

-r requirements.txt
  = read packages from requirements.txt file
  = installs all listed packages
  = -r means "requirements file"

Example requirements.txt:
  fastapi==0.110.0
  uvicorn==0.29.0
  sqlalchemy==2.0.29
  pyodbc==5.1.0

This installs all of them.
```

---

```dockerfile
# Copy application code
COPY . .
```
```
COPY . .
  = copy everything from current directory
    on your machine
    into current directory in container

First  . = source  = your project folder
Second . = destination = /app in container

This copies:
  main.py
  my_app/
  config/
  models/
  etc.

WHY AFTER pip install?
  Code changes frequently.
  If we put this before pip install:
  → Every code change = pip install again
  → Very slow build

  By putting after pip install:
  → Code changes only invalidate COPY layer
  → pip install layer stays cached
  → Much faster builds

What gets copied?
  Everything EXCEPT what is in .dockerignore
  .dockerignore is like .gitignore for Docker
```

---

```dockerfile
# Run from app package directory so current imports resolve
WORKDIR /app/my_app
```
```
WORKDIR again = changes working directory

Now inside container we move from:
  /app
to:
  /app/my_app

WHY?
  Your project structure is:
  /app/
  └── my_app/
      ├── main.py
      ├── config/
      ├── models/
      └── routers/

  If you run python main.py from /app:
  → Python cannot find imports like:
    from config.database import ...
    from models.student import ...
  → ImportError!

  If you run from /app/my_app:
  → Python finds all imports correctly
  → from config.database works
  → from models.student works

This is like doing cd my_app before running.

Common mistake fixed by this line!
```

---

```dockerfile
# Run the application
CMD ["python", "main.py"]
```
```
CMD = command to run when container STARTS

Format:
  CMD ["executable", "argument1", "argument2"]
  This is called exec form - recommended

CMD ["python", "main.py"] means:
  run: python main.py

Since WORKDIR is /app/my_app:
  It runs: /app/my_app/main.py

Difference between RUN and CMD:
  RUN  = runs during IMAGE BUILD
         used for installing packages etc.
         becomes part of image

  CMD  = runs when CONTAINER STARTS
         your actual application
         can be overridden at runtime

Only ONE CMD per Dockerfile.
If you have multiple, only last one runs.

Override CMD at runtime:
  docker run myapp python other_file.py
```

---

# Full file with all explanations inline

```dockerfile
# ==========================================
# comment only - no effect
# ==========================================

# Pull Python 3.12 on Alpine Linux base image
# Alpine = tiny Linux (5MB vs Ubuntu 200MB)
FROM python:3.12-alpine

# All next commands run inside /app
# Docker creates /app if it does not exist
WORKDIR /app

# Install C compilers and ODBC libraries
# needed before pip install pyodbc
# apk = Alpine package manager
# --no-cache = smaller image
RUN apk add --no-cache \
    gcc \          # C compiler
    g++ \          # C++ compiler
    musl-dev \     # Alpine C library headers
    unixodbc \     # ODBC runtime (Azure SQL)
    unixodbc-dev   # ODBC headers for compilation

# Copy only requirements.txt first
# Docker caches this layer
# pip install only reruns if requirements.txt changes
COPY requirements.txt .

# Install all Python packages
# --no-cache-dir = smaller image
# -r = read from file
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Copy all project files into /app
# Done AFTER pip install for better caching
COPY . .

# Move into my_app subfolder
# So imports like "from config.database"
# resolve correctly
WORKDIR /app/my_app

# Start the app when container runs
# Runs: python main.py
# from /app/my_app directory
CMD ["python", "main.py"]
```

---

# Build and run flow

```bash
# Build the image
docker build -t myapp .

# What Docker does step by step:
# Step 1: FROM    → downloads python:3.12-alpine
# Step 2: WORKDIR → creates /app folder
# Step 3: RUN     → installs gcc, pyodbc libs
# Step 4: COPY    → copies requirements.txt
# Step 5: RUN     → installs Python packages
# Step 6: COPY    → copies all your code
# Step 7: WORKDIR → moves to /app/my_app
# Step 8: CMD     → saves start command

# Run the container
docker run -d \
  --name myapp \
  -p 8000:8000 \
  --env-file .env \
  myapp:latest
```

---

# Common mistakes explained

```dockerfile
# MISTAKE 1: Wrong order
COPY . .                    # copies all code
RUN pip install -r req.txt  # runs every time code changes
# BAD - slow builds

# CORRECT order
COPY requirements.txt .     # copy only deps
RUN pip install -r req.txt  # cached if deps unchanged
COPY . .                    # copy code last

# ==========================================

# MISTAKE 2: Missing WORKDIR
RUN pip install -r requirements.txt
# Files go to / root - messy!

# CORRECT
WORKDIR /app
# Now everything is in /app - clean!

# ==========================================

# MISTAKE 3: Using cache
RUN apk add gcc             # saves package index
# Bigger image!

# CORRECT
RUN apk add --no-cache gcc  # no package index saved
# Smaller image!

# ==========================================

# MISTAKE 4: Using shell form for CMD
CMD python main.py          # shell form - not recommended

# CORRECT exec form
CMD ["python", "main.py"]   # exec form - recommended
# Handles signals properly
# Container stops cleanly
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
FROM        → base image to start from
WORKDIR     → set working directory
RUN         → run command during BUILD
COPY        → copy files into container
CMD         → command to run on START
ENV         → set environment variable
EXPOSE      → document which port app uses
ARG         → build-time variable

apk         → Alpine package manager
--no-cache  → do not save cache
gcc/g++     → C/C++ compilers
musl-dev    → Alpine C standard library
unixodbc    → ODBC driver for SQL databases

pip install --no-cache-dir  → no pip cache saved
pip install -r              → install from file

COPY req.txt first → faster builds via caching
COPY . . last      → code changes dont bust cache
```

## Copilot

Here's a **complete guide on pushing Docker images** to different registries.

---

# Where can you push Docker images?

```
Docker Hub          → most popular, public
Azure Container     → best for Azure apps
Registry (ACR)
AWS ECR             → best for AWS apps
GitHub Container    → best with GitHub Actions
Registry (GHCR)
Google Artifact     → best for GCP apps
Registry
Private Registry    → self hosted
```

---

# 1) Docker Hub

## Setup

```bash
# Step 1: Create account
# Go to: https://hub.docker.com
# Sign up for free account

# Step 2: Login from terminal
docker login

# Enter:
# Username: your-dockerhub-username
# Password: your-dockerhub-password

# Or login with token (safer)
docker login -u your-username \
  -p your-access-token
```

---

## Build and Push

```bash
# ==========================================
# STEP 1: Build image
# ==========================================
docker build -t myapp .

# ==========================================
# STEP 2: Tag image
# Format: username/repository:tag
# ==========================================
docker tag myapp your-username/myapp:latest

# Tag with version number too
docker tag myapp your-username/myapp:v1.0.0

# ==========================================
# STEP 3: Push image
# ==========================================
docker push your-username/myapp:latest

# Push version tag too
docker push your-username/myapp:v1.0.0

# ==========================================
# STEP 4: Verify on Docker Hub
# Go to: https://hub.docker.com/r/your-username/myapp
# ==========================================
```

---

## Full Docker Hub flow

```bash
# Complete flow in one go
docker build -t your-username/myapp:latest .
docker push your-username/myapp:latest

# Pull from anywhere
docker pull your-username/myapp:latest
```

---

# 2) Azure Container Registry (ACR)

Best for Azure SQL + FastAPI apps.

---

## Setup ACR

```bash
# ==========================================
# STEP 1: Install Azure CLI
# ==========================================
# Mac
brew install azure-cli

# Windows
winget install Microsoft.AzureCLI

# Ubuntu/Debian
curl -sL https://aka.ms/InstallAzureCLIDeb | sudo bash

# ==========================================
# STEP 2: Login to Azure
# ==========================================
az login
# Opens browser for login

# ==========================================
# STEP 3: Create Resource Group
# ==========================================
az group create \
  --name myResourceGroup \
  --location eastus

# ==========================================
# STEP 4: Create Container Registry
# ==========================================
az acr create \
  --resource-group myResourceGroup \
  --name myregistryname \
  --sku Basic

# Registry name rules:
# - 5 to 50 characters
# - alphanumeric only
# - must be globally unique

# ==========================================
# STEP 5: Login to ACR
# ==========================================
az acr login --name myregistryname

# ==========================================
# STEP 6: Get ACR login server URL
# ==========================================
az acr show \
  --name myregistryname \
  --query loginServer \
  --output table

# Output:
# myregistryname.azurecr.io
```

---

## Build and Push to ACR

```bash
# ==========================================
# STEP 1: Build image
# ==========================================
docker build -t myapp .

# ==========================================
# STEP 2: Tag with ACR URL
# Format: registryname.azurecr.io/image:tag
# ==========================================
docker tag myapp \
  myregistryname.azurecr.io/myapp:latest

# Tag with version
docker tag myapp \
  myregistryname.azurecr.io/myapp:v1.0.0

# ==========================================
# STEP 3: Push to ACR
# ==========================================
docker push \
  myregistryname.azurecr.io/myapp:latest

docker push \
  myregistryname.azurecr.io/myapp:v1.0.0

# ==========================================
# STEP 4: Verify images in ACR
# ==========================================
az acr repository list \
  --name myregistryname \
  --output table

# See tags for specific image
az acr repository show-tags \
  --name myregistryname \
  --repository myapp \
  --output table
```

---

## Build directly in ACR (no local Docker needed)

```bash
# ACR Tasks - builds in cloud
az acr build \
  --registry myregistryname \
  --image myapp:latest .
```

---

# 3) GitHub Container Registry (GHCR)

Best when using GitHub Actions.

---

## Setup and Push

```bash
# ==========================================
# STEP 1: Create GitHub Personal Access Token
# Go to: GitHub → Settings → Developer Settings
# → Personal Access Tokens → Tokens (classic)
# → Generate new token
# Select scopes:
#   - write:packages
#   - read:packages
#   - delete:packages
# ==========================================

# ==========================================
# STEP 2: Login to GHCR
# ==========================================
echo "your-github-token" | docker login \
  ghcr.io \
  -u your-github-username \
  --password-stdin

# ==========================================
# STEP 3: Build image
# ==========================================
docker build -t myapp .

# ==========================================
# STEP 4: Tag for GHCR
# Format: ghcr.io/username/image:tag
# ==========================================
docker tag myapp \
  ghcr.io/your-github-username/myapp:latest

# ==========================================
# STEP 5: Push to GHCR
# ==========================================
docker push \
  ghcr.io/your-github-username/myapp:latest
```
