# LEVEL 2 - MEDIUM 🟡

---

## Assignment 6 - Medium

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN students with departments
-- 2. GROUP BY department name
-- 3. Use COUNT(students)

-- Q6: Count how many students
-- are in each department
-- Show department name not id

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name          AS department,
    COUNT(s.id)     AS total_students
FROM students s
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
GROUP BY d.name
ORDER BY total_students DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 7 - Medium

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN teachers with departments
-- 2. GROUP BY department
-- 3. Use AVG(salary)
-- 4. ROUND to 2 decimal places

-- Q7: Find average salary of teachers
-- in each department
-- Sort by average salary highest first

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name                  AS department,
    ROUND(AVG(t.salary), 2) AS avg_salary
FROM teachers t
JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
GROUP BY d.name
ORDER BY avg_salary DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 8 - Medium

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use GROUP BY on city
-- 2. Count students per city
-- 3. Use HAVING COUNT(*) > 1
--    to show cities with multiple students

-- Q8: Find cities that have
-- more than 1 student
-- Show city name and student count

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    city,
    COUNT(*) AS student_count
FROM students
GROUP BY city
HAVING COUNT(*) > 1
ORDER BY student_count DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 9 - Medium

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN enrollments with courses
-- 2. GROUP BY course
-- 3. COUNT enrollments per course

-- Q9: Count how many students
-- enrolled in each course
-- Show course title and count
-- Sort by most enrolled first

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    c.title           AS course,
    COUNT(e.id)       AS enrolled_students
FROM courses c
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
GROUP BY c.title
ORDER BY enrolled_students DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 10 - Medium

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. Filter WHERE status = 'paid'
-- 2. GROUP BY payment_method
-- 3. SUM the amounts

-- Q10: Find total fees collected
-- per payment method
-- Only include paid fees

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    payment_method,
    COUNT(*)       AS transactions,
    SUM(amount)    AS total_collected
FROM fees
WHERE status = 'paid'
GROUP BY payment_method
ORDER BY total_collected DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 11 - Medium

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN results with exams
-- 2. GROUP BY exam_type
-- 3. Use AVG, MAX, MIN, COUNT

-- Q11: Show exam statistics
-- for each exam type
-- (midterm vs final)
-- Show avg, max, min marks

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    e.exam_type,
    COUNT(r.id)           AS total_results,
    ROUND(AVG(r.marks),2) AS avg_marks,
    MAX(r.marks)          AS highest_marks,
    MIN(r.marks)          AS lowest_marks
FROM results r
JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
GROUP BY e.exam_type;
```

# LEVEL 3 - HARD 🔴

---

## Assignment 12 - Hard

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN teachers + departments
-- 2. GROUP BY department
-- 3. Use HAVING AVG(salary) > 65000
-- 4. Also use COUNT > 1

-- Q12: Find departments where
-- average teacher salary is above 65000
-- AND has more than 1 teacher
-- Show department, avg salary, teacher count

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name                  AS department,
    COUNT(t.id)             AS teacher_count,
    ROUND(AVG(t.salary),2)  AS avg_salary,
    SUM(t.salary)           AS total_salary
FROM teachers t
JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
WHERE t.is_active = TRUE
GROUP BY d.name
HAVING AVG(t.salary) > 65000
AND COUNT(t.id) > 1
ORDER BY avg_salary DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 13 - Hard

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN results + students + exams
-- 2. GROUP BY student
-- 3. Only final exams (WHERE exam_type='final')
-- 4. SUM marks per student
-- 5. HAVING SUM > 70

-- Q13: Find students who scored
-- more than 70 total marks
-- in final exams only
-- Show student name and total marks

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name,
    COUNT(r.id)          AS exams_taken,
    SUM(r.marks)         AS total_marks,
    ROUND(AVG(r.marks),2) AS avg_marks
FROM results r
JOIN students s
    ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
WHERE e.exam_type = 'final'
GROUP BY s.name
HAVING SUM(r.marks) > 70
ORDER BY total_marks DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 14 - Hard

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN fees + students + departments
-- 2. GROUP BY department
-- 3. Only where status = 'paid'
-- 4. SUM amounts per department

-- Q14: Find total fees collected
-- per department
-- (fees paid by students of each dept)
-- Sort by highest collection first

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name          AS department,
    COUNT(f.id)     AS total_payments,
    SUM(f.amount)   AS total_fees_collected,
    COUNT(DISTINCT f.student_id) AS students_paid
FROM fees f
JOIN students s
    ON f.student_id = s.id
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE f.status = 'paid'
GROUP BY d.name
ORDER BY total_fees_collected DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 15 - Hard

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. GROUP BY admission_year AND gender
-- 2. COUNT students per year per gender
-- 3. This is called pivot-style query

-- Q15: Count students per admission year
-- broken down by gender
-- Show year, male count, female count

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    admission_year,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN gender = 'Male'
               THEN 1 END)   AS male_students,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN gender = 'Female'
               THEN 1 END)   AS female_students,
    COUNT(*)                 AS total_students
FROM students
GROUP BY admission_year
ORDER BY admission_year;
```

---

## Assignment 16 - Hard

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use CASE inside aggregate
-- 2. COUNT paid, pending, overdue separately
-- 3. GROUP BY nothing - whole table

-- Q16: Show fee status summary
-- How many paid, pending, overdue
-- and total amount for each status

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    status,
    COUNT(*)      AS total_records,
    SUM(amount)   AS total_amount,
    ROUND(AVG(amount),2) AS avg_amount
FROM fees
GROUP BY status
ORDER BY total_amount DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 17 - Very Hard 🔥

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. Multiple JOINs needed
-- 2. JOIN students, departments,
--    results, exams
-- 3. GROUP BY department
-- 4. Calculate avg marks per dept
-- 5. Only show depts with avg > 70

-- Q17: Find departments where
-- average student marks in
-- final exams is above 70
-- Show dept name, avg marks,
-- total students who gave exam

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name                  AS department,
    COUNT(DISTINCT s.id)    AS students_appeared,
    ROUND(AVG(r.marks),2)   AS avg_final_marks,
    MAX(r.marks)            AS highest_marks,
    MIN(r.marks)            AS lowest_marks
FROM results r
JOIN students s
    ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
WHERE e.exam_type = 'final'
GROUP BY d.name
HAVING AVG(r.marks) > 70
ORDER BY avg_final_marks DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 18 - Very Hard 🔥

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. This needs GROUP BY on multiple columns
-- 2. GROUP BY course AND grade
-- 3. COUNT students per grade per course

-- Q18: For each course show
-- how many students got each grade
-- (A+, A, B+, B, C etc)

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    c.title    AS course,
    r.grade,
    COUNT(*)   AS student_count
FROM results r
JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id
GROUP BY c.title, r.grade
ORDER BY c.title, r.grade;
```

---

## Assignment 19 - Very Hard 🔥

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use SUM with CASE
-- 2. GROUP BY student
-- 3. Calculate percentage attendance

-- Q19: Calculate attendance percentage
-- for each student in each course
-- Show only students below 80% attendance

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name      AS student,
    c.title     AS course,
    COUNT(*)    AS total_classes,
    SUM(CASE WHEN a.status = 'present'
             THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS present,
    SUM(CASE WHEN a.status = 'absent'
             THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS absent,
    ROUND(
        SUM(CASE WHEN a.status = 'present'
                 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) * 100.0
        / COUNT(*), 2
    ) AS attendance_percentage
FROM attendance a
JOIN students s ON a.student_id = s.id
JOIN courses c  ON a.course_id = c.id
GROUP BY s.name, c.title
HAVING ROUND(
    SUM(CASE WHEN a.status = 'present'
             THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) * 100.0
    / COUNT(*), 2
) < 80
ORDER BY attendance_percentage ASC;
```

---

## Assignment 20 - Expert Level 🏆

```sql
-- HINT:
-- 1. Need library + students + departments
-- 2. GROUP BY department
-- 3. SUM fines per department
-- 4. COUNT overdue books
-- 5. Only depts with total fine > 0

-- Q20: Library fine report per department
-- Show department name,
-- total students with books,
-- total fines collected,
-- number of overdue books

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name                  AS department,
    COUNT(DISTINCT l.student_id) AS students_with_books,
    COUNT(l.id)             AS total_books_issued,
    SUM(l.fine)             AS total_fines,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN l.status = 'overdue'
               THEN 1 END)  AS overdue_books,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN l.status = 'issued'
               THEN 1 END)  AS currently_issued
FROM library l
JOIN students s
    ON l.student_id = s.id
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
GROUP BY d.name
HAVING SUM(l.fine) > 0
   OR COUNT(CASE WHEN l.status
            IN ('overdue','issued')
            THEN 1 END) > 0
ORDER BY total_fines DESC;
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
AGGREGATE FUNCTIONS:
COUNT(*)     → count all rows
COUNT(col)   → count non-null
SUM(col)     → add up
AVG(col)     → average
MAX(col)     → highest
MIN(col)     → lowest

GROUP BY     → group rows
HAVING       → filter groups
WHERE        → filter rows (before group)

ORDER:
SELECT → FROM → WHERE
→ GROUP BY → HAVING
→ ORDER BY → LIMIT

KEY RULES:
SELECT col must be in GROUP BY
OR inside aggregate function
Cannot use aggregate in WHERE
Use HAVING for aggregate filters
```

```
------------|-----------|---------------------------

Medium 🟡   | 6 - 11   | GROUP BY + JOIN + HAVING
Hard   🔴   | 12 - 16  | Multiple conditions
Very Hard 🔥| 17 - 19  | Multiple JOINs + CASE
Expert 🏆   | 20       | Full complex query
```

## @brehman_uhg

TOPIC 4: JOINS
Explanation
Code
INNER JOIN  → matching rows only
LEFT JOIN   → all left + matched right
RIGHT JOIN  → all right + matched left
FULL JOIN   → all rows both sides
SELF JOIN   → table joins itself now teach this

## Copilot

Here's a **complete JOINS guide** from basics to advanced.

---

# First understand the basics

---

## What is a JOIN?

```
JOIN = combine rows from TWO or more tables
       based on a related column

Without JOIN:
  Table 1: students (has department_id)
  Table 2: departments (has id, name)
  You cannot see department NAME in students

With JOIN:
  Combine both tables
  Now you can see department NAME
  next to student data
```

---

## Simple real life example

```
STUDENTS TABLE          DEPARTMENTS TABLE
id | name  | dept_id    id | dept_name
---|-------|--------    ---|----------
1  | Aman  | 1          1  | Computer Science
2  | Sara  | 2          2  | Mathematics
3  | Raj   | 1          3  | Physics
4  | Priya | NULL       4  | Chemistry

JOIN on students.dept_id = departments.id
```

---

## Visual diagram of all JOINs

```
INNER JOIN          LEFT JOIN
   A ∩ B               A
  ┌─────┐           ┌──────┐
  │ ✓✓✓ │           │ ✓✓✓✓ │
  └─────┘           └──────┘
  only matching     all A + matched B


RIGHT JOIN          FULL JOIN
      B               A ∪ B
  ┌──────┐         ┌────────┐
  │  ✓✓✓✓│         │ ✓✓✓✓✓✓ │
  └──────┘         └────────┘
  all B + matched A  everything
```

---

# INNER JOIN

---

## What is INNER JOIN?

```
INNER JOIN = only rows that MATCH in BOTH tables
             Non-matching rows are EXCLUDED

Like a STRICT FILTER
Both sides must have matching data
```

---

## Visual example

```
STUDENTS              DEPARTMENTS
id | name  | dept_id  id | name
1  | Aman  | 1        1  | CS
2  | Sara  | 2        2  | Math
3  | Raj   | 1        3  | Physics
4  | Priya | NULL     (no match for NULL)

INNER JOIN result:
id | name | dept_name
1  | Aman | CS          ✓ dept_id=1 exists
2  | Sara | Math        ✓ dept_id=2 exists
3  | Raj  | CS          ✓ dept_id=1 exists
4  | Priya excluded     ✗ dept_id=NULL no match
   Physics excluded     ✗ no student has dept 3
```

---

## INNER JOIN syntax

```sql
SELECT columns
FROM table1
INNER JOIN table2
    ON table1.column = table2.column;

-- INNER keyword is optional
-- These are same:
SELECT * FROM students
INNER JOIN departments ON students.department_id = departments.id;

SELECT * FROM students
JOIN departments ON students.department_id = departments.id;
```

---

## INNER JOIN examples on our database

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 1: Students with department names
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.id,
    s.name          AS student_name,
    s.roll_number,
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location
FROM students s
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

/*
OUTPUT:
student_name | roll_number | department       | location
-------------|-------------|------------------|----------
Aman Singh   | CS2020001   | Computer Science | Block A
Sara Khan    | MA2019002   | Mathematics      | Block B
Raj Patel    | CS2021003   | Computer Science | Block A
...
Note: Student 20 (Deepa Mishra - inactive)
      still shows IF she has department_id
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 2: Teachers with departments
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    t.experience,
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location
FROM teachers t
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, t.salary DESC;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 3: Courses with teacher names
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    c.code,
    c.title         AS course,
    c.fee,
    c.credits,
    t.name          AS teacher,
    d.name          AS department
FROM courses c
INNER JOIN teachers t
    ON c.teacher_id = t.id
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON c.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 4: Student results with details
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    s.roll_number,
    c.title         AS course,
    e.exam_name,
    e.exam_type,
    r.marks,
    r.grade,
    r.remarks
FROM results r
INNER JOIN students s
    ON r.student_id = s.id
INNER JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
INNER JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id
ORDER BY s.name, e.exam_date;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 5: Enrollment details
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    c.title         AS course,
    c.fee,
    e.enrolled_date,
    e.status        AS enrollment_status,
    t.name          AS teacher
FROM enrollments e
INNER JOIN students s   ON e.student_id = s.id
INNER JOIN courses c    ON e.course_id = c.id
INNER JOIN teachers t   ON c.teacher_id = t.id
ORDER BY s.name;
```

---

# LEFT JOIN

---

## What is LEFT JOIN?

```
LEFT JOIN = ALL rows from LEFT table
            + matching rows from RIGHT table
            + NULL where no match on right

Left table = table written BEFORE JOIN
Right table = table written AFTER JOIN

Think of it as:
"Give me everything from left
 and whatever matches from right
 if no match - put NULL"
```

---

## Visual example

```
STUDENTS (LEFT)       DEPARTMENTS (RIGHT)
id | name  | dept_id  id | name
1  | Aman  | 1        1  | CS
2  | Sara  | 2        2  | Math
3  | Raj   | 1        3  | Physics
4  | Priya | NULL     (no student)

LEFT JOIN result:
name  | dept_name
Aman  | CS          ✓ matched
Sara  | Math        ✓ matched
Raj   | CS          ✓ matched
Priya | NULL        ✓ included but no dept
      Physics NOT   ✗ not in left table
```

---

## LEFT JOIN examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 1: ALL students with their dept
-- Even students with no department
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    s.roll_number,
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

/*
OUTPUT includes:
- All students WITH department name
- Students with NULL department_id
  show NULL for department columns
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 2: ALL students + their fees
-- Even students who have NOT paid
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    s.roll_number,
    f.amount,
    f.status,
    f.paid_date
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN fees f
    ON s.id = f.student_id
ORDER BY s.name;

/*
OUTPUT:
- Students WITH fees show fee data
- Students WITHOUT fees show NULL
  for fee columns
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 3: ALL students + library books
-- Even students with no books
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    s.roll_number,
    l.book_name,
    l.status        AS book_status,
    l.fine
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN library l
    ON s.id = l.student_id
ORDER BY s.name;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 4: Find students with NO fees
-- Using LEFT JOIN + WHERE IS NULL
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    s.roll_number,
    s.admission_year
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN fees f
    ON s.id = f.student_id
WHERE f.id IS NULL;

/*
This finds students who have
NO record in fees table at all
The trick: LEFT JOIN keeps all students
WHERE f.id IS NULL = no match found
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 5: ALL courses + enrollment count
-- Even courses with 0 enrollments
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    c.title         AS course,
    c.fee,
    COUNT(e.id)     AS enrolled_students
FROM courses c
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
GROUP BY c.title, c.fee
ORDER BY enrolled_students DESC;

/*
Courses with 0 enrollments show 0
not excluded like INNER JOIN would
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 6: All teachers + their courses
-- Teachers teaching no course show NULL
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    c.title         AS course,
    c.code
FROM teachers t
LEFT JOIN courses c
    ON t.id = c.teacher_id
ORDER BY t.name;
```

---

# RIGHT JOIN

---

## What is RIGHT JOIN?

```
RIGHT JOIN = ALL rows from RIGHT table
             + matching rows from LEFT table
             + NULL where no match on left

Opposite of LEFT JOIN

Think of it as:
"Give me everything from right
 and whatever matches from left"

NOTE: RIGHT JOIN is rare in practice
Most developers convert RIGHT JOIN
to LEFT JOIN by swapping table order
```

---

## Visual example

```
STUDENTS (LEFT)       DEPARTMENTS (RIGHT)
id | name  | dept_id  id | name
1  | Aman  | 1        1  | CS
2  | Sara  | 2        2  | Math
3  | Raj   | 1        3  | Physics
4  | Priya | NULL     4  | Chemistry

RIGHT JOIN result:
name  | dept_name
Aman  | CS          ✓ matched
Raj   | CS          ✓ matched
Sara  | Math        ✓ matched
NULL  | Physics     ✓ included no student
NULL  | Chemistry   ✓ included no student
Priya NOT included  ✗ not in right match
```

---

## RIGHT JOIN examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 1: All departments + students
-- Even departments with no students
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name;

/*
OUTPUT:
- All departments show
- Departments with no students
  show NULL for student name
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 2: All courses + teachers
-- Even if course has no teacher assigned
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    c.title         AS course,
    c.code,
    c.fee
FROM teachers t
RIGHT JOIN courses c
    ON t.id = c.teacher_id
ORDER BY c.title;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 3: Find departments with NO students
-- RIGHT JOIN + WHERE IS NULL trick
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location,
    d.established_year
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE s.id IS NULL;

/*
Shows departments that have
ZERO students enrolled
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 4: Convert RIGHT to LEFT JOIN
-- These give SAME result
-- ==========================================

-- Using RIGHT JOIN
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

-- Same using LEFT JOIN (preferred)
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM departments d
LEFT JOIN students s
    ON d.id = s.department_id;

-- Both give same output
-- LEFT JOIN version is preferred
```

---

# FULL JOIN (FULL OUTER JOIN)

---

## What is FULL JOIN?

```
FULL JOIN = ALL rows from BOTH tables
            Matching rows combined
            Non-matching rows show NULL
            on the missing side

Think of it as:
LEFT JOIN + RIGHT JOIN combined
Everything from both sides
```

---

## Visual example

```
STUDENTS (LEFT)       DEPARTMENTS (RIGHT)
id | name  | dept_id  id | name
1  | Aman  | 1        1  | CS
2  | Sara  | 2        2  | Math
3  | Raj   | 1        3  | Physics
4  | Priya | NULL     4  | Chemistry

FULL JOIN result:
name  | dept_name
Aman  | CS          ✓ matched
Raj   | CS          ✓ matched
Sara  | Math        ✓ matched
Priya | NULL        ✓ student no dept
NULL  | Physics     ✓ dept no student
NULL  | Chemistry   ✓ dept no student
```

---

## FULL JOIN examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- NOTE: MySQL does NOT support FULL OUTER JOIN
-- Use UNION of LEFT + RIGHT instead
-- PostgreSQL and SQL Server support it
-- ==========================================

-- ==========================================
-- PostgreSQL / SQL Server syntax
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    d.name          AS department
FROM students s
FULL OUTER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name;

-- ==========================================
-- MySQL workaround using UNION
-- ==========================================
-- LEFT JOIN
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    d.name          AS department
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id

UNION

-- RIGHT JOIN
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    d.name          AS department
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id

ORDER BY department;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 2: Find unmatched on BOTH sides
-- Students with no dept AND
-- Depts with no students
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    d.name          AS department,
    CASE
        WHEN d.id IS NULL THEN 'No Department'
        WHEN s.id IS NULL THEN 'No Students'
        ELSE 'Matched'
    END             AS status
FROM students s
FULL OUTER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE s.id IS NULL
   OR d.id IS NULL;
```

---

# SELF JOIN

---

## What is SELF JOIN?

```
SELF JOIN = table joins WITH ITSELF

Use when:
- a table has a reference to itself
- employee has manager_id
  (manager is also an employee)
- student has mentor_id
  (mentor is also a student)

Trick: use TWO aliases for same table
```

---

## Visual example

```
EMPLOYEES TABLE
id | name    | manager_id
1  | Boss    | NULL
2  | Aman    | 1          (reports to Boss)
3  | Sara    | 1          (reports to Boss)
4  | Raj     | 2          (reports to Aman)

SELF JOIN result:
employee | manager
Aman     | Boss
Sara     | Boss
Raj      | Aman
```

---

## Self JOIN setup and examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Add manager_id to teachers table
-- for self join example
-- ==========================================
ALTER TABLE teachers ADD COLUMN manager_id INT;

UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = NULL  WHERE id = 1;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 1     WHERE id = 2;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 1     WHERE id = 3;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 2     WHERE id = 4;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 2     WHERE id = 5;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 3     WHERE id = 6;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 3     WHERE id = 7;
UPDATE teachers SET manager_id = 1     WHERE id = 8;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 1: Teacher and their manager
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    m.name          AS manager
FROM teachers t
LEFT JOIN teachers m
    ON t.manager_id = m.id
ORDER BY m.name;

/*
OUTPUT:
teacher      | salary | manager
-------------|--------|--------
Priya Patel  | 65000  | Amit Sharma
Raj Kumar    | 70000  | Amit Sharma
Sunita Singh | 68000  | Priya Patel
Vikram Verma | 60000  | Priya Patel
Amit Sharma  | 75000  | NULL (top level)
*/

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 2: Find all subordinates
-- of a specific manager
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t.name          AS subordinate,
    t.salary,
    m.name          AS manager
FROM teachers t
INNER JOIN teachers m
    ON t.manager_id = m.id
WHERE m.name = 'Amit Sharma';

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 3: Compare student marks
-- Students scoring more than another student
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s1.name         AS student,
    r1.marks        AS marks,
    s2.name         AS scored_more_than,
    r2.marks        AS their_marks
FROM results r1
JOIN students s1 ON r1.student_id = s1.id
JOIN results r2  ON r1.exam_id = r2.exam_id
JOIN students s2 ON r2.student_id = s2.id
WHERE r1.marks > r2.marks
AND r1.student_id != r2.student_id
ORDER BY r1.marks DESC;

-- ==========================================
-- EXAMPLE 4: Find teachers in same dept
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t1.name         AS teacher1,
    t2.name         AS teacher2,
    t1.department_id
FROM teachers t1
JOIN teachers t2
    ON t1.department_id = t2.department_id
    AND t1.id < t2.id
ORDER BY t1.department_id;

/*
t1.id < t2.id prevents duplicates
Without it: (Aman,Sara) AND (Sara,Aman)
With it: only (Aman,Sara)
*/
```

---

# All JOINs side by side

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- SAME QUERY - different JOIN types
-- Students and Departments
-- ==========================================

-- INNER JOIN - only matched
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;
-- Excludes: students with no dept
-- Excludes: depts with no students

-- LEFT JOIN - all students
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;
-- Includes: ALL students
-- Excludes: depts with no students

-- RIGHT JOIN - all departments
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;
-- Excludes: students with no dept
-- Includes: ALL departments

-- FULL JOIN - everything
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
FULL OUTER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;
-- Includes: ALL students
-- Includes: ALL departments
```

---

# ASSIGNMENTS - Easy to Hard

---

# LEVEL 1 - EASY 🟢

---

## Assignment 1 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: INNER JOIN
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use students table
-- 2. INNER JOIN with departments
-- 3. Show student name + dept name

-- Q1: Show all students with
-- their department name
-- Only students who have a department

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name        AS student_name,
    s.roll_number,
    d.name        AS department
FROM students s
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, s.name;
```

---

## Assignment 2 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: INNER JOIN
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use teachers table
-- 2. INNER JOIN with departments
-- 3. Show teacher + salary + dept name

-- Q2: Show all teachers with
-- their department name and location
-- Sort by salary highest first

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    t.name        AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    t.experience,
    d.name        AS department,
    d.location
FROM teachers t
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY t.salary DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 3 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: LEFT JOIN
-- HINT:
-- 1. LEFT table = students
-- 2. RIGHT table = fees
-- 3. LEFT JOIN keeps ALL students
-- 4. Students with no fees show NULL

-- Q3: Show all students and
-- their fee payment status
-- Include students with no fee records

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name,
    s.roll_number,
    f.amount,
    f.status,
    f.payment_method
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN fees f
    ON s.id = f.student_id
ORDER BY s.name;
```

---

## Assignment 4 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: LEFT JOIN + IS NULL
-- HINT:
-- 1. LEFT JOIN students with library
-- 2. WHERE library.id IS NULL
--    means no book record found

-- Q4: Find students who have
-- NEVER borrowed a library book

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name,
    s.roll_number,
    s.department_id
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN library l
    ON s.id = l.student_id
WHERE l.id IS NULL
ORDER BY s.name;
```

---

## Assignment 5 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: INNER JOIN 3 tables
-- HINT:
-- 1. enrollments is the middle table
-- 2. JOIN students to enrollments
-- 3. JOIN courses to enrollments

-- Q5: Show student name and
-- the courses they enrolled in
-- With enrollment status

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    c.title         AS course,
    c.fee,
    e.enrolled_date,
    e.status
FROM enrollments e
INNER JOIN students s
    ON e.student_id = s.id
INNER JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id
ORDER BY s.name;
```

---

# LEVEL 2 - MEDIUM 🟡

---

## Assignment 6 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: LEFT JOIN + GROUP BY
-- HINT:
-- 1. LEFT JOIN courses with enrollments
-- 2. GROUP BY course
-- 3. COUNT enrollments per course
-- 4. LEFT JOIN so 0 enrollment courses show

-- Q6: Show each course with
-- total number of enrolled students
-- Include courses with 0 enrollments

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    c.title         AS course,
    c.code,
    c.fee,
    COUNT(e.id)     AS total_enrolled
FROM courses c
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
GROUP BY c.title, c.code, c.fee
ORDER BY total_enrolled DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 7 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: RIGHT JOIN
-- HINT:
-- 1. RIGHT table = departments
-- 2. LEFT table = teachers
-- 3. RIGHT JOIN keeps ALL departments
-- 4. Use IS NULL to find empty depts

-- Q7: Find departments that have
-- NO teachers assigned

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location,
    d.established_year
FROM teachers t
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
WHERE t.id IS NULL
ORDER BY d.name;
```

---

## Assignment 8 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: INNER JOIN 4 tables
-- HINT:
-- 1. results → exams → courses → departments
-- 2. Chain JOINs one by one
-- 3. Show student result details

-- Q8: Show student name, course name,
-- exam type, marks and grade
-- for all results

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    c.title         AS course,
    e.exam_type,
    e.exam_name,
    r.marks,
    r.grade,
    r.remarks
FROM results r
INNER JOIN students s
    ON r.student_id = s.id
INNER JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
INNER JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id
ORDER BY s.name, r.marks DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 9 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: SELF JOIN
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use teachers table TWICE
-- 2. Alias as t (teacher) and m (manager)
-- 3. JOIN ON t.manager_id = m.id

-- Q9: Show each teacher and
-- their manager name
-- Include teachers with no manager (CEO)

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    t.experience,
    COALESCE(m.name, 'Top Level')
                    AS manager
FROM teachers t
LEFT JOIN teachers m
    ON t.manager_id = m.id
ORDER BY m.name, t.name;
```

---

## Assignment 10 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: LEFT JOIN + NULL filter
-- HINT:
-- 1. LEFT JOIN courses with enrollments
-- 2. WHERE enrollment IS NULL
--    finds courses with no students

-- Q10: Find courses that have
-- NO students enrolled yet

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    c.title         AS course,
    c.code,
    c.fee,
    t.name          AS teacher
FROM courses c
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
LEFT JOIN teachers t
    ON c.teacher_id = t.id
WHERE e.id IS NULL
ORDER BY c.title;
```

---

# LEVEL 3 - HARD 🔴

---

## Assignment 11 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: Multiple JOINs + GROUP BY
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN departments → teachers
-- 2. GROUP BY department
-- 3. COUNT teachers, AVG salary
-- 4. Also JOIN to get student count

-- Q11: Show department summary:
-- dept name, teacher count,
-- avg teacher salary, student count

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name              AS department,
    COUNT(DISTINCT t.id) AS teacher_count,
    ROUND(AVG(t.salary),2) AS avg_salary,
    COUNT(DISTINCT s.id) AS student_count
FROM departments d
LEFT JOIN teachers t
    ON d.id = t.department_id
LEFT JOIN students s
    ON d.id = s.department_id
GROUP BY d.name
ORDER BY student_count DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 12 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: FULL JOIN simulation + UNION
-- HINT:
-- 1. LEFT JOIN students with enrollments
-- 2. UNION
-- 3. RIGHT JOIN to get all courses
-- 4. Shows students not enrolled
--    AND courses with no students

-- Q12: Show ALL students and ALL courses
-- even if no enrollment exists
-- Mark which ones have no match

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    c.title         AS course,
    e.status,
    'enrolled'      AS record_type
FROM students s
INNER JOIN enrollments e
    ON s.id = e.student_id
INNER JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id

UNION ALL

SELECT
    s.name,
    NULL            AS course,
    NULL            AS status,
    'not enrolled'
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON s.id = e.student_id
WHERE e.id IS NULL

UNION ALL

SELECT
    NULL            AS student,
    c.title,
    NULL,
    'no students'
FROM courses c
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
WHERE e.id IS NULL

ORDER BY record_type, student;
```

---

## Assignment 13 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: SELF JOIN comparison
-- HINT:
-- 1. Use results table twice
-- 2. r1 and r2 both alias results
-- 3. JOIN on same exam_id
-- 4. Compare marks between students

-- Q13: For each exam find pairs of
-- students where one scored higher
-- than the other
-- Show both student names and marks

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s1.name         AS higher_scorer,
    r1.marks        AS higher_marks,
    s2.name         AS lower_scorer,
    r2.marks        AS lower_marks,
    c.title         AS course,
    e.exam_name
FROM results r1
JOIN results r2
    ON r1.exam_id = r2.exam_id
    AND r1.marks > r2.marks
JOIN students s1 ON r1.student_id = s1.id
JOIN students s2 ON r2.student_id = s2.id
JOIN exams e     ON r1.exam_id = e.id
JOIN courses c   ON e.course_id = c.id
ORDER BY r1.marks DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 14 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: Complex LEFT JOIN + conditions
-- HINT:
-- 1. JOIN students, fees, library
-- 2. Find students with pending fees
--    OR overdue books
-- 3. Use LEFT JOIN to keep all students

-- Q14: Find students who have
-- either pending fees OR overdue books
-- Show their name and what issue they have

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    s.roll_number,
    f.status        AS fee_status,
    f.amount        AS fee_amount,
    l.book_name,
    l.status        AS book_status,
    l.fine
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN fees f
    ON s.id = f.student_id
    AND f.status IN ('pending','overdue')
LEFT JOIN library l
    ON s.id = l.student_id
    AND l.status = 'overdue'
WHERE f.id IS NOT NULL
   OR l.id IS NOT NULL
ORDER BY s.name;
```

---

# LEVEL 4 - VERY HARD 🔥

---

## Assignment 15 - Very Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: All JOIN types combined
-- HINT:
-- 1. Start with departments
-- 2. LEFT JOIN teachers (some depts no teacher)
-- 3. LEFT JOIN courses (some teachers no course)
-- 4. LEFT JOIN enrollments + students
-- 5. GROUP BY department
-- 6. Show complete department report

-- Q15: Complete department report showing:
-- dept name, teacher count, course count,
-- enrolled student count, total fees

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    d.name              AS department,
    d.location,
    d.budget,
    COUNT(DISTINCT t.id) AS teachers,
    COUNT(DISTINCT c.id) AS courses,
    COUNT(DISTINCT e.student_id)
                        AS enrolled_students,
    COALESCE(SUM(DISTINCT f.amount),0)
                        AS total_fees_collected
FROM departments d
LEFT JOIN teachers t
    ON d.id = t.department_id
    AND t.is_active = TRUE
LEFT JOIN courses c
    ON d.id = c.department_id
    AND c.is_active = TRUE
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
LEFT JOIN fees f
    ON e.student_id = f.student_id
    AND f.status = 'paid'
GROUP BY d.name, d.location, d.budget
ORDER BY enrolled_students DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 16 - Expert 🏆

```sql
-- TOPIC: SELF JOIN hierarchy
-- HINT:
-- 1. Find top teacher per department
-- 2. Self join to compare salaries
-- 3. Show who earns more than
--    average of their peers

-- Q16: For each teacher show:
-- their name, salary, department
-- how many colleagues earn LESS than them
-- how many colleagues earn MORE than them

-- YOUR ANSWER:
SELECT
    t1.name             AS teacher,
    t1.salary,
    d.name              AS department,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN t2.salary < t1.salary
               THEN 1 END) AS earn_less_than_me,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN t2.salary > t1.salary
               THEN 1 END) AS earn_more_than_me
FROM teachers t1
JOIN departments d
    ON t1.department_id = d.id
LEFT JOIN teachers t2
    ON t1.department_id = t2.department_id
    AND t1.id != t2.id
GROUP BY t1.name, t1.salary, d.name
ORDER BY t1.salary DESC;
```

---

# Quick revision sheet

```
JOIN TYPE    | LEFT TABLE | RIGHT TABLE | NULL SIDE
-------------|------------|-------------|----------
INNER JOIN   | matched    | matched     | none
LEFT JOIN    | ALL rows   | matched     | right
RIGHT JOIN   | matched    | ALL rows    | left
FULL JOIN    | ALL rows   | ALL rows    | both sides
SELF JOIN    | same table | same table  | depends

FIND UNMATCHED:
  LEFT JOIN + WHERE right.id IS NULL
  = rows in LEFT with no match in RIGHT

  RIGHT JOIN + WHERE left.id IS NULL
  = rows in RIGHT with no match in LEFT

ALIASES:
  Always use short aliases
  t = teachers
  s = students
  d = departments
  c = courses
  e = enrollments or exams
  r = results
  f = fees
  l = library
```

---

# Summary of all assignments

```
Level        | Q   | Topic
-------------|-----|--------------------------------
Easy    🟢   | 1   | INNER JOIN 2 tables
Easy    🟢   | 2   | INNER JOIN with sort
Easy    🟢   | 3   | LEFT JOIN all rows
Easy    🟢   | 4   | LEFT JOIN + IS NULL
Easy    🟢   | 5   | INNER JOIN 3 tables
Medium  🟡   | 6   | LEFT JOIN + GROUP BY
Medium  🟡   | 7   | RIGHT JOIN + IS NULL
Medium  🟡   | 8   | INNER JOIN 4 tables
Medium  🟡   | 9   | SELF JOIN
Medium  🟡   | 10  | LEFT JOIN + NULL filter
Hard    🔴   | 11  | Multiple JOINs + GROUP BY
Hard    🔴   | 12  | FULL JOIN simulation
Hard    🔴   | 13  | SELF JOIN comparison
Hard    🔴   | 14  | Complex LEFT JOIN
V.Hard  🔥   | 15  | All JOIN types combined
Expert  🏆   | 16  | SELF JOIN hierarchy
```

# INNER JOIN - 2 Assignments

---

## Assignment 1 - Easy 🟢

```sql
-- TOPIC: INNER JOIN
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show all students with their
-- department name and location
-- Only show students who HAVE a department
-- Sort by department name
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Table 1 = students
-- Table 2 = departments
-- Link = students.department_id = departments.id
-- Use s and d as aliases

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student_name,
    s.roll_number,
    s.city,
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location
FROM students s
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, s.name;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
student_name  | roll_number | department       | location
--------------|-------------|------------------|----------
Aman Singh    | CS2020001   | Computer Science | Block A
Raj Patel     | CS2021003   | Computer Science | Block A
Arjun Tiwari  | CS2021015   | Computer Science | Block A
Sara Khan     | MA2019002   | Mathematics      | Block B
...
*/
```

---

## Assignment 2 - Medium 🟡

```sql
-- TOPIC: INNER JOIN 4 tables
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show complete result card:
-- student name, course name,
-- exam name, exam type,
-- marks and grade
-- Only for FINAL exams
-- Sort by marks highest first
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- results → JOIN students (student_id)
-- results → JOIN exams    (exam_id)
-- exams   → JOIN courses  (course_id)
-- Filter WHERE exam_type = 'final'

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    s.roll_number,
    c.title         AS course,
    e.exam_name,
    e.exam_type,
    r.marks,
    r.grade,
    r.remarks
FROM results r
INNER JOIN students s
    ON r.student_id = s.id
INNER JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
INNER JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id
WHERE e.exam_type = 'final'
ORDER BY r.marks DESC;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
student      | course          | exam_type | marks | grade
-------------|-----------------|-----------|-------|------
Divya Nair   | Cell Biology    | final     | 94.00 | A+
Aman Singh   | Calculus        | final     | 92.00 | A+
Priya Sharma | Mechanics       | final     | 90.00 | A+
...
*/
```

---

---

# LEFT JOIN - 2 Assignments

---

## Assignment 3 - Easy 🟢

```sql
-- TOPIC: LEFT JOIN
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show ALL students and their
-- library book details
-- Include students who have
-- NEVER borrowed any book
-- Those students should show NULL
-- for book columns
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- LEFT table  = students (keep ALL)
-- RIGHT table = library
-- Link = students.id = library.student_id
-- Students with no books → NULL on right side

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    s.roll_number,
    l.book_name,
    l.author,
    l.status        AS book_status,
    l.fine,
    CASE
        WHEN l.id IS NULL
        THEN 'Never Borrowed'
        ELSE 'Has Book Record'
    END             AS library_status
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN library l
    ON s.id = l.student_id
ORDER BY s.name;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
student       | roll_number | book_name                    | status
--------------|-------------|------------------------------|--------
Ahmed Ali     | CH2019005   | Organic Chemistry            | returned
Aman Singh    | CS2020001   | Introduction to Algorithms   | returned
Anjali Reddy  | EC2020010   | NULL                         | Never Borrowed
Arjun Tiwari  | CS2021015   | NULL                         | Never Borrowed
...
*/
```

---

## Assignment 4 - Hard 🔴

```sql
-- TOPIC: LEFT JOIN + IS NULL + GROUP BY
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Find all courses with their
-- enrollment count
-- Show courses with ZERO enrollments too
-- Also show teacher name for each course
-- Sort by enrollment count DESC
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- LEFT table  = courses (keep ALL)
-- RIGHT table = enrollments
-- Also JOIN teachers for teacher name
-- COUNT(e.id) gives 0 for no enrollments
-- because COUNT(NULL) = 0

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    c.title             AS course,
    c.code,
    c.fee,
    t.name              AS teacher,
    COUNT(e.id)         AS total_enrolled,
    CASE
        WHEN COUNT(e.id) = 0
        THEN 'No Students Yet'
        ELSE 'Has Students'
    END                 AS status
FROM courses c
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON c.id = e.course_id
LEFT JOIN teachers t
    ON c.teacher_id = t.id
GROUP BY
    c.title,
    c.code,
    c.fee,
    t.name
ORDER BY total_enrolled DESC;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
course                 | teacher       | total_enrolled | status
-----------------------|---------------|----------------|--------
Intro to Programming   | Amit Sharma   | 6              | Has Students
Calculus               | Priya Patel   | 4              | Has Students
...
Fine Arts              | Deepa Nair    | 0              | No Students Yet
*/
```

---

---

# RIGHT JOIN - 2 Assignments

---

## Assignment 5 - Easy 🟢

```sql
-- TOPIC: RIGHT JOIN
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show ALL departments and
-- teachers working in them
-- Include departments that have
-- NO teachers assigned
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- LEFT table  = teachers
-- RIGHT table = departments (keep ALL)
-- Departments with no teachers → NULL
-- for teacher columns

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    t.qualification,
    d.name          AS department,
    d.location,
    CASE
        WHEN t.id IS NULL
        THEN 'No Teacher Assigned'
        ELSE 'Has Teacher'
    END             AS status
FROM teachers t
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, t.salary DESC;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
teacher        | salary  | department       | location
---------------|---------|------------------|----------
Amit Sharma    | 75000   | Computer Science | Block A
Arjun Reddy    | 80000   | Computer Science | Block A
Priya Patel    | 65000   | Mathematics      | Block B
...
NULL           | NULL    | Geography        | Block I
*/
```

---

## Assignment 6 - Hard 🔴

```sql
-- TOPIC: RIGHT JOIN + IS NULL
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Find departments that have
-- NO students enrolled
-- Show department name, location,
-- established year and budget
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- LEFT table  = students
-- RIGHT table = departments (keep ALL)
-- WHERE students.id IS NULL
-- means that department has no students
-- This is RIGHT JOIN + NULL trick

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    d.name              AS department,
    d.location,
    d.established_year,
    d.budget,
    d.head_name
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE s.id IS NULL
ORDER BY d.name;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
department | location | established_year | budget
-----------|----------|-----------------|--------
Arts       | Block J  | 1987            | 180000
(departments that have zero students)
*/
```

---

---

# FULL JOIN - 2 Assignments

---

## Assignment 7 - Medium 🟡

```sql
-- TOPIC: FULL JOIN using UNION
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show ALL students and ALL courses
-- Even if student has no enrollment
-- Even if course has no students
-- Label each row with its type
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- MySQL has no FULL OUTER JOIN
-- Use LEFT JOIN UNION RIGHT JOIN
-- Part 1: All students + their courses
-- Part 2: All courses + their students
-- UNION removes duplicates

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:

-- Part 1: All students + matched courses
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    c.title         AS course,
    'Student Side'  AS source
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON s.id = e.student_id
LEFT JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id

UNION

-- Part 2: All courses + matched students
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    c.title         AS course,
    'Course Side'   AS source
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN enrollments e
    ON s.id = e.student_id
RIGHT JOIN courses c
    ON e.course_id = c.id

ORDER BY course, student;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
student       | course                  | source
--------------|-------------------------|------------
Aman Singh    | Intro to Programming    | Student Side
NULL          | Fine Arts               | Course Side
Anjali Reddy  | NULL                    | Student Side
...
*/
```

---

## Assignment 8 - Hard 🔴

```sql
-- TOPIC: FULL JOIN - find ALL unmatched
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Find students with no fees record
-- AND fees records with no student
-- Show both in one result
-- Label which problem each row has
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Part 1: LEFT JOIN students+fees
--         WHERE fees IS NULL
--         = students with no fee record
-- Part 2: RIGHT JOIN students+fees
--         WHERE students IS NULL
--         = fee records with no student
-- UNION both parts

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:

-- Students with NO fee record
SELECT
    s.name          AS student,
    s.roll_number,
    NULL            AS fee_amount,
    'No Fee Record' AS issue
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN fees f
    ON s.id = f.student_id
WHERE f.id IS NULL

UNION ALL

-- Fee records with NO matching student
SELECT
    NULL            AS student,
    NULL            AS roll_number,
    f.amount        AS fee_amount,
    'Orphan Fee Record' AS issue
FROM fees f
LEFT JOIN students s
    ON f.student_id = s.id
WHERE s.id IS NULL

ORDER BY issue, student;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
student      | roll_number | fee_amount | issue
-------------|-------------|------------|------------------
Kavita Bhatt | GE2020016   | NULL       | No Fee Record
...
NULL         | NULL        | 50000      | Orphan Fee Record
*/
```

---

---

# SELF JOIN - 2 Assignments

---

## Assignment 9 - Medium 🟡

```sql
-- TOPIC: SELF JOIN
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show each teacher and their
-- manager name
-- Teachers with no manager should
-- show 'Head of School'
-- Sort by manager name
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Use teachers table TWICE
-- t = the teacher
-- m = the manager (also a teacher)
-- JOIN ON t.manager_id = m.id
-- LEFT JOIN so NULL managers included
-- COALESCE(m.name, 'Head of School')

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    t.name              AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    t.qualification,
    COALESCE(
        m.name,
        'Head of School'
    )                   AS reports_to,
    COALESCE(
        m.salary,
        0
    )                   AS manager_salary
FROM teachers t
LEFT JOIN teachers m
    ON t.manager_id = m.id
ORDER BY
    reports_to,
    t.salary DESC;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
teacher       | salary | reports_to      | manager_salary
--------------|--------|-----------------|---------------
Amit Sharma   | 75000  | Head of School  | 0
Priya Patel   | 65000  | Amit Sharma     | 75000
Raj Kumar     | 70000  | Amit Sharma     | 75000
Sunita Singh  | 68000  | Priya Patel     | 65000
*/
```

---

## Assignment 10 - Hard 🔴

```sql
-- TOPIC: SELF JOIN - compare rows
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Find pairs of students who are
-- from the same city
-- Show both student names and city
-- Avoid duplicate pairs
-- (dont show Aman-Raj AND Raj-Aman)
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Use students table TWICE
-- s1 and s2 as aliases
-- JOIN ON s1.city = s2.city
-- AND s1.id < s2.id
-- s1.id < s2.id avoids duplicates
-- and self pairing

-- YOUR ANSWER HERE:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s1.name         AS student_1,
    s2.name         AS student_2,
    s1.city,
    s1.department_id AS s1_dept,
    s2.department_id AS s2_dept
FROM students s1
INNER JOIN students s2
    ON s1.city = s2.city
    AND s1.id < s2.id
ORDER BY
    s1.city,
    s1.name;

/*
EXPECTED OUTPUT:
student_1   | student_2    | city
------------|--------------|----------
Aman Singh  | Raj Patel    | Mumbai
Aman Singh  | Arjun Tiwari | Mumbai  (if same city)
...

NOTE:
s1.id < s2.id prevents:
- Same student paired with themselves
- Duplicate pairs like (Aman,Raj) & (Raj,Aman)
*/
```

```
No. | Topic      | Level  | Key concept
----|------------|--------|---------------------------
1   | INNER JOIN | 🟢 Easy | 2 tables basic join
2   | INNER JOIN | 🟡 Med  | 4 tables + filter

4   | LEFT JOIN  | 🔴 Hard | NULL check + GROUP BY
5   | RIGHT JOIN | 🟢 Easy | keep all right rows
6   | RIGHT JOIN | 🔴 Hard | IS NULL trick
7   | FULL JOIN  | 🟡 Med  | UNION simulation

10  | SELF JOIN  | 🔴 Hard | compare same table rows
```

## Copilot

Here's a **complete SQL interview questions guide** - all important questions.

---

# SQL Interview Questions - Complete Guide

---

# CATEGORY 1: BASICS

---

## Q1) What is SQL? What are its types?

```
SQL = Structured Query Language
Used to manage relational databases

Types:
DDL → Data Definition Language
      CREATE, ALTER, DROP, TRUNCATE

DML → Data Manipulation Language
      SELECT, INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE

DCL → Data Control Language
      GRANT, REVOKE

TCL → Transaction Control Language
      COMMIT, ROLLBACK, SAVEPOINT
```

---

## Q2) Difference between DELETE, TRUNCATE, DROP?

```sql
-- DELETE
-- Removes specific rows
-- Can use WHERE
-- Can ROLLBACK
-- Slower - logs each row
DELETE FROM students WHERE id = 1;

-- TRUNCATE
-- Removes ALL rows
-- Cannot use WHERE
-- Cannot ROLLBACK
-- Faster - no row logging
-- Keeps table structure
TRUNCATE TABLE students;

-- DROP
-- Removes entire table
-- Table structure also gone
-- Cannot ROLLBACK
DROP TABLE students;
```

```
Feature    | DELETE  | TRUNCATE | DROP
-----------|---------|----------|------
WHERE      | YES     | NO       | NO
ROLLBACK   | YES     | NO       | NO
Structure  | Kept    | Kept     | Gone
Speed      | Slow    | Fast     | Fast
Logs       | Each row| Minimal  | None
```

---

## Q3) Difference between WHERE and HAVING?

```sql
-- WHERE filters ROWS before grouping
-- HAVING filters GROUPS after grouping

-- WHERE - cannot use aggregate
SELECT department_id, AVG(salary)
FROM teachers
WHERE is_active = TRUE        -- ✓ filters rows
GROUP BY department_id
HAVING AVG(salary) > 65000;   -- ✓ filters groups

-- WRONG - cannot use aggregate in WHERE
SELECT department_id
FROM teachers
WHERE AVG(salary) > 65000;    -- ✗ ERROR
```

```
Feature        | WHERE      | HAVING
---------------|------------|----------
When           | Before GROUP BY | After GROUP BY
Aggregate      | NO         | YES
Filters        | Rows       | Groups
```

---

## Q4) What is DISTINCT?

```sql
-- DISTINCT removes duplicate values

-- Without DISTINCT - shows duplicates
SELECT city FROM students;
-- Mumbai, Delhi, Mumbai, Pune, Delhi

-- With DISTINCT - unique only
SELECT DISTINCT city FROM students;
-- Mumbai, Delhi, Pune

-- Count unique cities
SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT city)
FROM students;

-- Multiple columns
SELECT DISTINCT city, gender
FROM students;
```

---

## Q5) What is NULL? How to handle it?

```sql
-- NULL = missing or unknown value
-- NULL is NOT 0 or empty string

-- Check for NULL
SELECT * FROM students
WHERE email IS NULL;

-- Check for NOT NULL
SELECT * FROM students
WHERE email IS NOT NULL;

-- WRONG - cannot use = for NULL
SELECT * FROM students
WHERE email = NULL;  -- ✗ always returns nothing

-- COALESCE - return first non-null value
SELECT
    name,
    COALESCE(phone, 'No Phone') AS phone
FROM students;

-- IFNULL (MySQL)
SELECT IFNULL(phone, 'No Phone')
FROM students;

-- NULLIF - returns NULL if both equal
SELECT NULLIF(salary, 0) FROM teachers;
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 2: JOINS

---

## Q6) What are different types of JOINs?

```sql
-- INNER JOIN - only matching rows
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
INNER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

-- LEFT JOIN - all left + matched right
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

-- RIGHT JOIN - all right + matched left
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
RIGHT JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

-- FULL OUTER JOIN - all rows both sides
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
FULL OUTER JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id;

-- SELF JOIN - table with itself
SELECT
    t.name AS teacher,
    m.name AS manager
FROM teachers t
LEFT JOIN teachers m
    ON t.manager_id = m.id;

-- CROSS JOIN - every combination
SELECT s.name, c.title
FROM students s
CROSS JOIN courses c;
```

---

## Q7) Difference between INNER and OUTER JOIN?

```
INNER JOIN:
  Only rows that MATCH in BOTH tables
  Non-matching rows EXCLUDED

OUTER JOIN (LEFT/RIGHT/FULL):
  Includes non-matching rows too
  Shows NULL for missing side

Example:
  Students table: 25 students
  Departments table: 10 departments
  2 students have no department

  INNER JOIN  = 23 rows (2 excluded)
  LEFT JOIN   = 25 rows (all students)
  RIGHT JOIN  = varies (all departments)
```

---

## Q8) What is SELF JOIN? When to use?

```sql
-- SELF JOIN = table joins with itself
-- Use when table has reference to itself

-- Example: Employee-Manager relationship
SELECT
    e.name      AS employee,
    m.name      AS manager
FROM teachers e
LEFT JOIN teachers m
    ON e.manager_id = m.id;

-- Use cases:
-- 1. Employee - Manager hierarchy
-- 2. Find duplicate records
-- 3. Compare rows in same table
-- 4. Find students in same city

SELECT
    s1.name,
    s2.name,
    s1.city
FROM students s1
JOIN students s2
    ON s1.city = s2.city
    AND s1.id < s2.id;
```

---

## Q9) How to find records in one table but not another?

```sql
-- Method 1: LEFT JOIN + IS NULL
SELECT s.name
FROM students s
LEFT JOIN enrollments e
    ON s.id = e.student_id
WHERE e.id IS NULL;
-- Students with NO enrollments

-- Method 2: NOT IN
SELECT name
FROM students
WHERE id NOT IN (
    SELECT student_id
    FROM enrollments
);

-- Method 3: NOT EXISTS
SELECT name
FROM students s
WHERE NOT EXISTS (
    SELECT 1
    FROM enrollments e
    WHERE e.student_id = s.id
);

-- Best practice: LEFT JOIN + IS NULL
-- Fastest performance
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 3: AGGREGATES AND GROUP BY

---

## Q10) What are aggregate functions?

```sql
-- COUNT - count rows
SELECT COUNT(*)    FROM students;
SELECT COUNT(email) FROM students; -- non-null only

-- SUM - total
SELECT SUM(salary) FROM teachers;

-- AVG - average
SELECT ROUND(AVG(salary),2) FROM teachers;

-- MAX - highest
SELECT MAX(marks)  FROM results;

-- MIN - lowest
SELECT MIN(marks)  FROM results;

-- GROUP BY - per group
SELECT
    department_id,
    COUNT(*)        AS total,
    AVG(salary)     AS avg_salary,
    MAX(salary)     AS max_salary
FROM teachers
GROUP BY department_id;
```

---

## Q11) Find Nth highest salary?

```sql
-- 2nd highest salary

-- Method 1: LIMIT OFFSET
SELECT DISTINCT salary
FROM teachers
ORDER BY salary DESC
LIMIT 1 OFFSET 1;

-- Method 2: Subquery
SELECT MAX(salary)
FROM teachers
WHERE salary < (
    SELECT MAX(salary)
    FROM teachers
);

-- Method 3: DENSE_RANK (best way)
SELECT salary
FROM (
    SELECT
        salary,
        DENSE_RANK() OVER (
            ORDER BY salary DESC
        ) AS rnk
    FROM teachers
) ranked
WHERE rnk = 2;

-- For Nth highest - just change the number
-- rnk = 3 for 3rd highest
-- rnk = 4 for 4th highest
```

---

## Q12) Find duplicate records?

```sql
-- Find duplicate emails in students
SELECT
    email,
    COUNT(*) AS count
FROM students
GROUP BY email
HAVING COUNT(*) > 1;

-- Find duplicate names
SELECT
    name,
    COUNT(*) AS count
FROM students
GROUP BY name
HAVING COUNT(*) > 1;

-- Show all details of duplicates
SELECT *
FROM students
WHERE email IN (
    SELECT email
    FROM students
    GROUP BY email
    HAVING COUNT(*) > 1
);

-- Delete duplicates keep one
DELETE FROM students
WHERE id NOT IN (
    SELECT MIN(id)
    FROM students
    GROUP BY email
);
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 4: SUBQUERIES

---

## Q13) What is a subquery? Types?

```sql
-- Subquery = query inside query

-- Type 1: Subquery in WHERE
SELECT name, salary
FROM teachers
WHERE salary > (
    SELECT AVG(salary)
    FROM teachers
);

-- Type 2: Subquery in FROM
SELECT dept, avg_sal
FROM (
    SELECT
        department_id AS dept,
        AVG(salary) AS avg_sal
    FROM teachers
    GROUP BY department_id
) AS dept_avg
WHERE avg_sal > 65000;

-- Type 3: Subquery in SELECT
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    (SELECT AVG(salary) FROM teachers)
        AS company_avg
FROM teachers;

-- Type 4: Correlated subquery
-- Runs for EACH row of outer query
SELECT name, salary
FROM teachers t1
WHERE salary > (
    SELECT AVG(salary)
    FROM teachers t2
    WHERE t2.department_id = t1.department_id
);
```

---

## Q14) Difference between subquery and JOIN?

```
SUBQUERY:
  Query inside query
  Easier to read
  Slower for large data
  Good for single value comparison

JOIN:
  Combine tables
  Usually faster
  Better for multiple columns
  Better for large datasets

-- Same result different approach:

-- Using Subquery
SELECT name FROM students
WHERE department_id = (
    SELECT id FROM departments
    WHERE name = 'Computer Science'
);

-- Using JOIN
SELECT s.name
FROM students s
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE d.name = 'Computer Science';
```

---

## Q15) What is EXISTS vs IN?

```sql
-- IN - checks if value in a list
SELECT name
FROM students
WHERE department_id IN (1, 2, 3);

-- IN with subquery
SELECT name
FROM students
WHERE department_id IN (
    SELECT id FROM departments
    WHERE location = 'Block A'
);

-- EXISTS - checks if rows exist
SELECT name
FROM departments d
WHERE EXISTS (
    SELECT 1
    FROM students s
    WHERE s.department_id = d.id
);

-- Difference:
-- IN    = compares values
--         slow with large subquery
--         handles NULL badly

-- EXISTS = checks existence only
--          faster for large data
--          stops at first match
--          better performance

-- NOT IN vs NOT EXISTS
-- NOT IN  - fails if subquery has NULL
-- NOT EXISTS - handles NULL correctly

-- Safe way with NOT EXISTS
SELECT name
FROM students s
WHERE NOT EXISTS (
    SELECT 1 FROM fees f
    WHERE f.student_id = s.id
);
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 5: WINDOW FUNCTIONS

---

## Q16) What are window functions?

```sql
-- Window functions calculate across
-- related rows WITHOUT collapsing them
-- Unlike GROUP BY which collapses rows

-- Syntax:
-- function() OVER (
--     PARTITION BY col  -- like GROUP BY
--     ORDER BY col      -- sort within window
-- )

-- ROW_NUMBER - unique number
SELECT
    name, salary,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS row_num
FROM teachers;

-- RANK - same value same rank, gaps
SELECT
    name, salary,
    RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS rnk
FROM teachers;

-- DENSE_RANK - same value same rank, no gaps
SELECT
    name, salary,
    DENSE_RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS dense_rnk
FROM teachers;

-- PARTITION BY - rank within group
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    RANK() OVER (
        PARTITION BY department_id
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS dept_rank
FROM teachers;
```

---

## Q17) Difference between RANK, DENSE_RANK, ROW_NUMBER?

```sql
-- Example data:
-- Aman  → 90
-- Sara  → 85
-- Raj   → 85
-- Priya → 80

SELECT
    name,
    marks,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC),
    RANK()       OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC),
    DENSE_RANK() OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC)
FROM results;

/*
name  | marks | ROW_NUMBER | RANK | DENSE_RANK
------|-------|------------|------|----------
Aman  | 90    | 1          | 1    | 1
Sara  | 85    | 2          | 2    | 2
Raj   | 85    | 3          | 2    | 2     ← same
Priya | 80    | 4          | 4    | 3     ← no gap

ROW_NUMBER  = always unique 1,2,3,4
RANK        = same value same rank, SKIPS next 1,2,2,4
DENSE_RANK  = same value same rank, NO SKIP  1,2,2,3
*/
```

---

## Q18) What is LAG and LEAD?

```sql
-- LAG  = get value from PREVIOUS row
-- LEAD = get value from NEXT row

-- Compare salary with previous employee
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    LAG(salary) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS prev_salary,
    salary - LAG(salary) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS difference
FROM teachers;

-- Compare with next employee
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    LEAD(salary) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS next_salary
FROM teachers;

-- Month over month comparison
SELECT
    paid_date,
    amount,
    LAG(amount) OVER (
        ORDER BY paid_date
    ) AS prev_amount,
    amount - LAG(amount) OVER (
        ORDER BY paid_date
    ) AS growth
FROM fees
WHERE status = 'paid';
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 6: INDEXES

---

## Q19) What is an Index?

```sql
-- Index = makes queries FASTER
-- Like index in a book
-- No need to scan every row

-- Types:
-- 1. Single column index
CREATE INDEX idx_student_email
ON students(email);

-- 2. Unique index
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX idx_roll_number
ON students(roll_number);

-- 3. Composite index
CREATE INDEX idx_dept_salary
ON teachers(department_id, salary);

-- When to USE index:
-- Columns in WHERE clause
-- Columns in JOIN conditions
-- Columns in ORDER BY
-- High cardinality columns (many unique values)

-- When NOT to use:
-- Small tables
-- Columns updated very frequently
-- Low cardinality (few unique values like gender)
-- Too many indexes slow INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE
```

---

## Q20) Clustered vs Non-Clustered Index?

```
CLUSTERED INDEX:
  Sorts actual table data
  Only ONE per table
  Primary Key is clustered by default
  Faster for range queries
  Data physically reordered

NON-CLUSTERED INDEX:
  Separate structure from table data
  Multiple allowed per table
  Stores pointer to actual data
  Slightly slower than clustered
  Does not reorder table data

Think of it as:
  Clustered    = dictionary (data sorted alphabetically)
  Non-Clustered = book index (separate page with pointers)
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 7: CONSTRAINTS

---

## Q21) What are SQL constraints?

```sql
-- PRIMARY KEY - unique + not null
CREATE TABLE students (
    id INT PRIMARY KEY
);

-- FOREIGN KEY - link to another table
CREATE TABLE enrollments (
    student_id INT,
    FOREIGN KEY (student_id)
        REFERENCES students(id)
);

-- UNIQUE - no duplicate values
CREATE TABLE students (
    email VARCHAR(100) UNIQUE
);

-- NOT NULL - cannot be empty
CREATE TABLE students (
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL
);

-- CHECK - custom validation
CREATE TABLE teachers (
    salary DECIMAL CHECK (salary > 0),
    age    INT     CHECK (age BETWEEN 21 AND 65)
);

-- DEFAULT - default value
CREATE TABLE students (
    is_active BOOLEAN DEFAULT TRUE
);
```

---

## Q22) Primary Key vs Unique Key?

```
Feature        | PRIMARY KEY  | UNIQUE KEY
---------------|--------------|------------
NULL allowed   | NO           | YES (one NULL)
Per table      | Only ONE     | Multiple allowed
Index created  | YES          | YES
Duplicate      | NO           | NO
Purpose        | Row identity | Uniqueness only

Example:
  students.id    = PRIMARY KEY
  students.email = UNIQUE KEY
  students.roll  = UNIQUE KEY
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 8: TRANSACTIONS

---

## Q23) What is a transaction? ACID properties?

```sql
-- Transaction = group of operations
-- Either ALL succeed or ALL fail

BEGIN TRANSACTION;

UPDATE fees SET status = 'paid'
WHERE student_id = 1;

INSERT INTO payments VALUES (1, 50000, NOW());

COMMIT;    -- save all changes
-- or
ROLLBACK;  -- undo all changes

-- SAVEPOINT
BEGIN TRANSACTION;
UPDATE fees SET status = 'paid' WHERE id = 1;
SAVEPOINT sp1;
UPDATE fees SET status = 'paid' WHERE id = 2;
ROLLBACK TO sp1;  -- undo only after sp1
COMMIT;
```

```
ACID Properties:

A = Atomicity
    All operations succeed or all fail
    No partial updates

C = Consistency
    Database stays in valid state
    Before and after transaction

I = Isolation
    Transactions don't interfere
    Each transaction is independent

D = Durability
    Committed data persists
    Even after system failure
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 9: STORED PROCEDURES AND VIEWS

---

## Q24) What is a View?

```sql
-- VIEW = saved SELECT query
-- Acts like a virtual table
-- Does not store data
-- Always shows fresh data

-- Create view
CREATE VIEW active_students AS
SELECT
    s.name,
    s.roll_number,
    d.name AS department
FROM students s
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE s.is_active = TRUE;

-- Use view like a table
SELECT * FROM active_students;
SELECT * FROM active_students
WHERE department = 'Computer Science';

-- Update view
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW active_students AS
SELECT name, roll_number FROM students
WHERE is_active = TRUE;

-- Drop view
DROP VIEW active_students;

-- Benefits:
-- Simplify complex queries
-- Security (hide sensitive columns)
-- Reusability
```

---

## Q25) View vs Materialized View?

```
VIEW:
  Virtual table
  No data stored
  Always fresh data
  Slower (runs query each time)
  Supported by all databases

MATERIALIZED VIEW:
  Physical copy of data
  Data stored on disk
  Needs refresh for new data
  Faster (pre-computed)
  PostgreSQL, Oracle support it

-- Materialized View (PostgreSQL)
CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW dept_summary AS
SELECT
    department_id,
    COUNT(*) AS total,
    AVG(salary) AS avg_salary
FROM teachers
GROUP BY department_id;

-- Refresh materialized view
REFRESH MATERIALIZED VIEW dept_summary;
```

---

## Q26) What is a Stored Procedure?

```sql
-- Stored Procedure = saved SQL code
-- Like a function in programming
-- Execute with EXEC or CALL

-- Create procedure
CREATE PROCEDURE GetStudentsByDept(
    IN dept_name VARCHAR(100)
)
BEGIN
    SELECT s.name, s.roll_number
    FROM students s
    JOIN departments d
        ON s.department_id = d.id
    WHERE d.name = dept_name;
END;

-- Call procedure
CALL GetStudentsByDept('Computer Science');

-- Procedure vs Function:
-- Procedure: can have multiple outputs
--            cannot use in SELECT
--            use CALL to execute

-- Function:  returns single value
--            can use in SELECT
--            use SELECT to call
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 10: PERFORMANCE

---

## Q27) How to optimize slow SQL queries?

```sql
-- 1. Use specific columns not *
-- BAD
SELECT * FROM students;
-- GOOD
SELECT id, name, email FROM students;

-- 2. Add indexes on WHERE columns
CREATE INDEX idx_dept
ON students(department_id);

-- 3. Avoid functions on indexed columns
-- BAD - index not used
SELECT * FROM students
WHERE YEAR(admission_year) = 2020;
-- GOOD - index used
SELECT * FROM students
WHERE admission_year = 2020;

-- 4. Use EXISTS instead of IN
-- for large subqueries
-- BAD for large data
SELECT * FROM students
WHERE id IN (SELECT student_id FROM fees);
-- GOOD
SELECT * FROM students s
WHERE EXISTS (
    SELECT 1 FROM fees f
    WHERE f.student_id = s.id
);

-- 5. Avoid SELECT DISTINCT unnecessarily
-- 6. Use LIMIT for large result sets
-- 7. Use EXPLAIN to check query plan
EXPLAIN SELECT * FROM students
WHERE department_id = 1;
```

---

## Q28) What is EXPLAIN?

```sql
-- EXPLAIN shows how database
-- executes your query
-- Helps identify performance issues

EXPLAIN SELECT * FROM students
WHERE department_id = 1;

/*
Output shows:
id | select_type | table    | type | key          | rows
---|-------------|----------|------|--------------|-----
1  | SIMPLE      | students | ref  | idx_dept     | 5

type = ref    → uses index (GOOD)
type = ALL    → full table scan (BAD)
key  = index name used
rows = estimated rows scanned
*/

-- EXPLAIN ANALYZE (more detail)
EXPLAIN ANALYZE
SELECT s.name, d.name
FROM students s
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
WHERE d.name = 'Computer Science';
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 11: ADVANCED

---

## Q29) What is CTE?

```sql
-- CTE = Common Table Expression
-- Named temporary result set
-- Used in same query only

-- Basic CTE
WITH high_earners AS (
    SELECT name, salary
    FROM teachers
    WHERE salary > 70000
)
SELECT * FROM high_earners;

-- Multiple CTEs
WITH
dept_avg AS (
    SELECT department_id,
           AVG(salary) AS avg_sal
    FROM teachers
    GROUP BY department_id
),
above_avg AS (
    SELECT t.name, t.salary
    FROM teachers t
    JOIN dept_avg d
        ON t.department_id = d.department_id
    WHERE t.salary > d.avg_sal
)
SELECT * FROM above_avg;

-- CTE vs Subquery:
-- CTE is more readable
-- CTE can be referenced multiple times
-- Subquery is inline
```

---

## Q30) What is normalization?

```
Normalization = organizing data
to reduce redundancy

1NF (First Normal Form):
  - Each column has atomic values
  - No repeating groups
  - Each row is unique

2NF (Second Normal Form):
  - Must be in 1NF
  - No partial dependencies
  - Every non-key column depends
    on WHOLE primary key

3NF (Third Normal Form):
  - Must be in 2NF
  - No transitive dependencies
  - Non-key columns depend only
    on primary key

BCNF (Boyce-Codd Normal Form):
  - Stricter version of 3NF

Denormalization:
  - Opposite of normalization
  - Add redundancy for performance
  - Used in data warehouses
```

---

## Q31) What is a Trigger?

```sql
-- Trigger = automatic action
-- Fires BEFORE or AFTER
-- INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE

-- Example: Log every delete
CREATE TRIGGER log_deleted_student
AFTER DELETE ON students
FOR EACH ROW
BEGIN
    INSERT INTO deleted_log (
        student_id,
        name,
        deleted_at
    )
    VALUES (
        OLD.id,
        OLD.name,
        NOW()
    );
END;

-- Types:
-- BEFORE INSERT  → validate before saving
-- AFTER INSERT   → audit log
-- BEFORE UPDATE  → validate changes
-- AFTER UPDATE   → track changes
-- BEFORE DELETE  → prevent deletion
-- AFTER DELETE   → audit log
```

---

## Q32) What are different types of keys?

```
PRIMARY KEY:
  Uniquely identifies each row
  NOT NULL + UNIQUE
  Only one per table
  students.id

FOREIGN KEY:
  Links to primary key of another table
  Maintains referential integrity
  enrollments.student_id → students.id

UNIQUE KEY:
  All values unique
  NULL allowed (once)
  Multiple per table
  students.email

CANDIDATE KEY:
  Could be primary key
  Minimal set of columns
  Uniquely identifies rows

COMPOSITE KEY:
  Multiple columns as key
  PRIMARY KEY (student_id, course_id)

SUPER KEY:
  Any combination that uniquely
  identifies rows
  Superset of candidate key
```

---

---

# CATEGORY 12: TRICKY QUESTIONS

---

## Q33) Find employees who earn more than their manager?

```sql
SELECT
    e.name      AS employee,
    e.salary    AS emp_salary,
    m.name      AS manager,
    m.salary    AS mgr_salary
FROM teachers e
JOIN teachers m
    ON e.manager_id = m.id
WHERE e.salary > m.salary;
```

---

## Q34) Find students who enrolled in ALL courses?

```sql
SELECT s.name
FROM students s
WHERE (
    SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT course_id)
    FROM enrollments
    WHERE student_id = s.id
) = (
    SELECT COUNT(*)
    FROM courses
    WHERE is_active = TRUE
);
```

---

## Q35) Running total?

```sql
SELECT
    student_id,
    paid_date,
    amount,
    SUM(amount) OVER (
        PARTITION BY student_id
        ORDER BY paid_date
        ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
        AND CURRENT ROW
    ) AS running_total
FROM fees
WHERE status = 'paid';
```

---

## Q36) Find gaps in sequence?

```sql
-- Find missing IDs in students table
SELECT t1.id + 1 AS missing_id
FROM students t1
LEFT JOIN students t2
    ON t1.id + 1 = t2.id
WHERE t2.id IS NULL
AND t1.id < (SELECT MAX(id) FROM students);
```

---

## Q37) Pivot table using CASE?

```sql
-- Count students per dept per gender
SELECT
    d.name AS department,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN s.gender = 'Male'
               THEN 1 END) AS male,
    COUNT(CASE WHEN s.gender = 'Female'
               THEN 1 END) AS female,
    COUNT(*) AS total
FROM students s
JOIN departments d
    ON s.department_id = d.id
GROUP BY d.name;
```

---

## Q38) Find top N records per group?

```sql
-- Top 2 students per department by marks
SELECT *
FROM (
    SELECT
        s.name,
        d.name AS department,
        r.marks,
        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
            PARTITION BY s.department_id
            ORDER BY r.marks DESC
        ) AS rn
    FROM results r
    JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
    JOIN departments d ON s.department_id = d.id
) ranked
WHERE rn <= 2;
```
