what are windows fucntion how to use it explain so that i can revise wuickly and example and assigmentn

## Copilot

Here's a **complete Window Functions guide** - easy to revise quickly.

---

# What are Window Functions?

```
Normal Aggregate (GROUP BY):
  Groups rows together
  Returns ONE row per group
  Original rows are GONE

Window Function:
  Works on a SET of related rows
  Returns ONE value PER ROW
  Original rows are KEPT

Think of it like:
  GROUP BY = collapse rows into one
  WINDOW   = add extra column to each row
```

---

## Simple comparison

```sql
-- GROUP BY - collapses rows
SELECT
    department_id,
    AVG(salary) AS avg_salary
FROM teachers
GROUP BY department_id;
/*
dept_id | avg_salary
--------|----------
1       | 77500      ← only 1 row per dept
2       | 66000
3       | 68000
*/

-- WINDOW - keeps all rows
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    AVG(salary) OVER (
        PARTITION BY department_id
    ) AS avg_salary
FROM teachers;
/*
name         | salary | dept | avg_salary
-------------|--------|------|----------
Amit Sharma  | 75000  | 1    | 77500   ← row kept
Arjun Reddy  | 80000  | 1    | 77500   ← row kept
Priya Patel  | 65000  | 2    | 66000   ← row kept
*/
```

---

## Syntax

```sql
function_name() OVER (
    PARTITION BY column  -- like GROUP BY
    ORDER BY column      -- sort within window
    ROWS/RANGE BETWEEN   -- window frame
)

-- PARTITION BY = divide into groups
-- ORDER BY     = sort within each group
-- ROWS BETWEEN = how many rows to include
```

---

# All Window Functions

```
RANKING:
  ROW_NUMBER()  → unique number 1,2,3,4
  RANK()        → same value same rank, gaps
  DENSE_RANK()  → same value same rank, no gaps
  NTILE(n)      → divide into n buckets
  PERCENT_RANK()→ percentage rank

VALUE:
  LAG()         → value from previous row
  LEAD()        → value from next row
  FIRST_VALUE() → first value in window
  LAST_VALUE()  → last value in window
  NTH_VALUE()   → nth value in window

AGGREGATE:
  SUM() OVER    → running total
  AVG() OVER    → running average
  COUNT() OVER  → running count
  MAX() OVER    → running max
  MIN() OVER    → running min
```

---

# 1) ROW_NUMBER()

---

## What is it?

```
Assigns a UNIQUE number to each row
No ties - always unique
1, 2, 3, 4, 5...

Use for:
- Pagination
- Remove duplicates
- Find top N records
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Basic ROW_NUMBER
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS row_num
FROM teachers;

/*
name          | salary | row_num
--------------|--------|--------
Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 1
Amit Sharma   | 75000  | 2
Raj Kumar     | 70000  | 3
Sunita Singh  | 68000  | 4
Priya Patel   | 65000  | 5
...always unique
*/

-- ==========================================
-- ROW_NUMBER with PARTITION BY
-- Restarts numbering for each department
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        PARTITION BY department_id
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS row_num
FROM teachers;

/*
name         | salary | dept | row_num
-------------|--------|------|--------
Arjun Reddy  | 80000  | 1    | 1   ← dept 1 starts at 1
Amit Sharma  | 75000  | 1    | 2
Priya Patel  | 65000  | 2    | 1   ← dept 2 restarts at 1
Pooja Iyer   | 67000  | 2    | 2
*/

-- ==========================================
-- TOP 1 student per department
-- Using ROW_NUMBER
-- ==========================================
SELECT *
FROM (
    SELECT
        s.name          AS student,
        d.name          AS department,
        r.marks,
        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
            PARTITION BY s.department_id
            ORDER BY r.marks DESC
        ) AS rn
    FROM results r
    JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
    JOIN departments d
        ON s.department_id = d.id
) ranked
WHERE rn = 1;

-- ==========================================
-- PAGINATION using ROW_NUMBER
-- Page 2: rows 11 to 20
-- ==========================================
SELECT *
FROM (
    SELECT
        name,
        salary,
        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
            ORDER BY id
        ) AS rn
    FROM teachers
) paged
WHERE rn BETWEEN 11 AND 20;
```

---

# 2) RANK()

---

## What is it?

```
Assigns rank to each row
SAME value = SAME rank
SKIPS next rank after tie

Example:
  90 → rank 1
  85 → rank 2
  85 → rank 2  (tie)
  80 → rank 4  (skips 3)
  75 → rank 5
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Basic RANK
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    marks,
    RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY marks DESC
    ) AS rank_position
FROM results
JOIN students ON results.student_id = students.id;

/*
name         | marks | rank
-------------|-------|-----
Divya Nair   | 94    | 1
Aman Singh   | 92    | 2
Priya Sharma | 90    | 3
Aman Singh   | 88    | 4
Vikram Joshi | 86    | 5
Aman Singh   | 85    | 6
Sara Khan    | 85    | 6   ← tie
Priya Sharma | 75    | 8   ← skips 7
*/

-- ==========================================
-- RANK within each department
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    t.name,
    t.salary,
    d.name          AS department,
    RANK() OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) AS dept_rank
FROM teachers t
JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id;

-- ==========================================
-- Find teachers ranked 1st in their dept
-- ==========================================
SELECT *
FROM (
    SELECT
        t.name,
        t.salary,
        d.name AS dept,
        RANK() OVER (
            PARTITION BY t.department_id
            ORDER BY t.salary DESC
        ) AS rnk
    FROM teachers t
    JOIN departments d
        ON t.department_id = d.id
) ranked
WHERE rnk = 1;
```

---

# 3) DENSE_RANK()

---

## What is it?

```
Same as RANK but NO GAPS

Example:
  90 → rank 1
  85 → rank 2
  85 → rank 2  (tie)
  80 → rank 3  (NO skip, next is 3)
  75 → rank 4

Use when:
  You need consecutive rankings
  No gaps allowed
  Medal rankings
```

---

## RANK vs DENSE_RANK vs ROW_NUMBER

```sql
SELECT
    name,
    marks,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC)
        AS row_num,
    RANK()       OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC)
        AS rnk,
    DENSE_RANK() OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC)
        AS dense_rnk
FROM results
JOIN students ON results.student_id = students.id;

/*
name   | marks | ROW_NUM | RANK | DENSE_RANK
-------|-------|---------|------|----------
Divya  | 94    | 1       | 1    | 1
Aman   | 92    | 2       | 2    | 2
Priya  | 90    | 3       | 3    | 3
Vikram | 88    | 4       | 4    | 4
Sara   | 85    | 5       | 5    | 5
Raj    | 85    | 6       | 5    | 5   ← tie
Rohit  | 80    | 7       | 7    | 6   ← RANK skips 6
                                        DENSE_RANK goes 6
*/
```

---

## Nth highest using DENSE_RANK

```sql
-- Find 2nd highest salary
SELECT name, salary
FROM (
    SELECT
        name,
        salary,
        DENSE_RANK() OVER (
            ORDER BY salary DESC
        ) AS rnk
    FROM teachers
) ranked
WHERE rnk = 2;

-- Find 3rd highest marks
SELECT name, marks
FROM (
    SELECT
        s.name,
        r.marks,
        DENSE_RANK() OVER (
            ORDER BY r.marks DESC
        ) AS rnk
    FROM results r
    JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
) ranked
WHERE rnk = 3;
```

---

# 4) NTILE()

---

## What is it?

```
Divides rows into N equal buckets
Each row gets a bucket number

NTILE(4) = 4 buckets (quartiles)
NTILE(3) = 3 buckets (terciles)
NTILE(2) = 2 buckets (halves)

Use for:
  Performance bands
  Salary bands
  Grade distribution
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Divide teachers into 4 salary bands
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    NTILE(4) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS salary_band,
    CASE NTILE(4) OVER (ORDER BY salary)
        WHEN 1 THEN 'Low'
        WHEN 2 THEN 'Medium'
        WHEN 3 THEN 'High'
        WHEN 4 THEN 'Very High'
    END AS band_name
FROM teachers
ORDER BY salary;

/*
name          | salary | band | band_name
--------------|--------|------|----------
Deepa Nair    | 55000  | 1    | Low
Ravi Rao      | 57000  | 1    | Low
Vikram Verma  | 60000  | 1    | Low
Meena Gupta   | 58000  | 2    | Medium
Kavita Joshi  | 63000  | 2    | Medium
Priya Patel   | 65000  | 3    | High
Neha Bhatt    | 59000  | 3    | High
Raj Kumar     | 70000  | 4    | Very High
Amit Sharma   | 75000  | 4    | Very High
Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 4    | Very High
*/

-- ==========================================
-- Divide students into 3 performance groups
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    r.marks,
    NTILE(3) OVER (
        ORDER BY r.marks DESC
    ) AS performance_group,
    CASE NTILE(3) OVER (ORDER BY r.marks DESC)
        WHEN 1 THEN 'Top Performer'
        WHEN 2 THEN 'Average'
        WHEN 3 THEN 'Needs Improvement'
    END AS performance
FROM results r
JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
WHERE exam_id IN (
    SELECT id FROM exams
    WHERE exam_type = 'final'
);
```

---

# 5) LAG()

---

## What is it?

```
Gets value from PREVIOUS row
LAG(column, offset, default)
  column  = which column
  offset  = how many rows back (default 1)
  default = value if no previous row

Use for:
  Month over month comparison
  Day over day comparison
  Calculate difference from previous
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Compare each result with previous
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    e.exam_date,
    r.marks,
    LAG(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS prev_marks,
    r.marks - LAG(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS improvement
FROM results r
JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e    ON r.exam_id = e.id
ORDER BY s.name, e.exam_date;

/*
name       | exam_date  | marks | prev | improvement
-----------|------------|-------|------|------------
Aman Singh | 2020-10-15 | 42    | NULL | NULL
Aman Singh | 2020-12-20 | 88    | 42   | +46
Aman Singh | 2021-04-10 | 38    | 88   | -50
Aman Singh | 2021-06-25 | 75    | 38   | +37
*/

-- ==========================================
-- Fee payment comparison month by month
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    paid_date,
    amount,
    LAG(amount, 1, 0) OVER (
        ORDER BY paid_date
    ) AS prev_amount,
    amount - LAG(amount, 1, 0) OVER (
        ORDER BY paid_date
    ) AS change_amount
FROM fees
WHERE status = 'paid'
ORDER BY paid_date;

-- ==========================================
-- LAG with offset 2 (2 rows back)
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    LAG(salary, 2) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS salary_2_rows_back
FROM teachers;
```

---

# 6) LEAD()

---

## What is it?

```
Gets value from NEXT row
LEAD(column, offset, default)

Opposite of LAG
Looks FORWARD instead of backward

Use for:
  Predict next value
  Find next event date
  Compare with upcoming record
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Show next exam marks for each student
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    e.exam_name,
    r.marks         AS current_marks,
    LEAD(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS next_exam_marks
FROM results r
JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e    ON r.exam_id = e.id
ORDER BY s.name, e.exam_date;

/*
name       | exam        | marks | next_marks
-----------|-------------|-------|----------
Aman Singh | Mid Term    | 42    | 88
Aman Singh | Final Exam  | 88    | 38
Aman Singh | Mid Term 2  | 38    | 75
Aman Singh | Final Exam2 | 75    | NULL  ← no next
*/

-- ==========================================
-- LAG and LEAD together
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    e.exam_date,
    r.marks,
    LAG(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS prev_marks,
    LEAD(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS next_marks
FROM results r
JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e    ON r.exam_id = e.id
ORDER BY s.name, e.exam_date;
```

---

# 7) FIRST_VALUE() and LAST_VALUE()

---

## What is it?

```
FIRST_VALUE() = first value in window
LAST_VALUE()  = last value in window

Use for:
  Show top performer name in every row
  Show department highest salary next to each employee
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Show highest paid teacher name
-- next to every teacher
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    FIRST_VALUE(name) OVER (
        PARTITION BY department_id
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS top_earner_in_dept
FROM teachers;

/*
name          | salary | dept | top_earner_in_dept
--------------|--------|------|------------------
Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 1    | Arjun Reddy
Amit Sharma   | 75000  | 1    | Arjun Reddy
Pooja Iyer    | 67000  | 2    | Pooja Iyer
Priya Patel   | 65000  | 2    | Pooja Iyer
*/

-- ==========================================
-- Show best student marks per course
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    c.title         AS course,
    r.marks,
    FIRST_VALUE(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY e.course_id
        ORDER BY r.marks DESC
    ) AS highest_in_course,
    FIRST_VALUE(s.name) OVER (
        PARTITION BY e.course_id
        ORDER BY r.marks DESC
    ) AS top_student
FROM results r
JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e    ON r.exam_id = e.id
JOIN courses c  ON e.course_id = c.id;
```

---

# 8) SUM OVER (Running Total)

---

## What is it?

```
Running total = cumulative sum
Each row shows total SO FAR

Like your bank balance:
  Day 1: deposit 1000 → balance 1000
  Day 2: deposit 500  → balance 1500
  Day 3: deposit 200  → balance 1700
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Running total of fees collected
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    student_id,
    paid_date,
    amount,
    SUM(amount) OVER (
        ORDER BY paid_date
        ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
        AND CURRENT ROW
    ) AS running_total
FROM fees
WHERE status = 'paid'
ORDER BY paid_date;

/*
student | paid_date  | amount | running_total
--------|------------|--------|-------------
1       | 2019-07-01 | 50000  | 50000
2       | 2019-07-02 | 50000  | 100000
4       | 2019-07-07 | 50000  | 150000
...
*/

-- ==========================================
-- Running total PER STUDENT
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    s.name,
    f.paid_date,
    f.amount,
    SUM(f.amount) OVER (
        PARTITION BY f.student_id
        ORDER BY f.paid_date
        ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
        AND CURRENT ROW
    ) AS student_running_total
FROM fees f
JOIN students s ON f.student_id = s.id
WHERE f.status = 'paid'
ORDER BY s.name, f.paid_date;

-- ==========================================
-- Running AVG, COUNT, MAX also works
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    AVG(salary) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
        ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
        AND CURRENT ROW
    ) AS running_avg,
    COUNT(*) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
        ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
        AND CURRENT ROW
    ) AS running_count
FROM teachers;
```

---

# 9) PERCENT_RANK()

---

## What is it?

```
Returns relative rank as percentage
Value between 0 and 1

Formula: (rank - 1) / (total rows - 1)

Use for:
  Percentile calculations
  Where does someone stand compared to others
```

---

## Examples

```sql
-- ==========================================
-- Percentile rank of each teacher salary
-- ==========================================
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    ROUND(
        PERCENT_RANK() OVER (
            ORDER BY salary
        ) * 100, 2
    ) AS percentile
FROM teachers;

/*
name          | salary | percentile
--------------|--------|----------
Deepa Nair    | 55000  | 0.00
Ravi Rao      | 57000  | 7.14
Meena Gupta   | 58000  | 14.29
Neha Bhatt    | 59000  | 21.43
Vikram Verma  | 60000  | 28.57
...
Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 100.00
*/

-- ==========================================
-- Find teachers in top 25%
-- ==========================================
SELECT name, salary, percentile
FROM (
    SELECT
        name,
        salary,
        PERCENT_RANK() OVER (
            ORDER BY salary
        ) AS percentile
    FROM teachers
) ranked
WHERE percentile >= 0.75;
```

---

# WINDOW FRAMES explained

```sql
-- ROWS BETWEEN defines the window size

-- UNBOUNDED PRECEDING = from very first row
-- CURRENT ROW         = current row
-- UNBOUNDED FOLLOWING = to very last row
-- N PRECEDING         = N rows before current
-- N FOLLOWING         = N rows after current

-- Running total (from start to current)
SUM(salary) OVER (
    ORDER BY salary
    ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
    AND CURRENT ROW
)

-- Moving average (3 rows)
AVG(salary) OVER (
    ORDER BY salary
    ROWS BETWEEN 1 PRECEDING
    AND 1 FOLLOWING
)

-- Entire partition (same as no frame)
SUM(salary) OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
    AND UNBOUNDED FOLLOWING
)
```

---

# ASSIGNMENTS - Easy to Hard

---

# LEVEL 1 - EASY 🟢

---

## Assignment 1 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: ROW_NUMBER
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Assign a row number to each teacher
-- ordered by salary highest first
-- Show: name, salary, row number
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- ROW_NUMBER() OVER (ORDER BY salary DESC)
-- No PARTITION BY needed
-- Just order by salary descending

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS row_num
FROM teachers;
```

---

## Assignment 2 - Easy

```sql
-- TOPIC: RANK and DENSE_RANK
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show each teacher with
-- RANK, DENSE_RANK and ROW_NUMBER
-- ordered by salary
-- See the difference when ties exist
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Use all 3 in same SELECT
-- ORDER BY salary DESC for all 3

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS row_num,
    RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS rnk,
    DENSE_RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS dense_rnk
FROM teachers
ORDER BY salary DESC;
```

---

# LEVEL 2 - MEDIUM 🟡

---

## Assignment 3 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: ROW_NUMBER with PARTITION BY
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Rank teachers within each department
-- by salary (highest = rank 1)
-- Show: teacher name, dept, salary, rank
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- PARTITION BY department_id
-- ORDER BY salary DESC
-- Rank restarts for each department

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    t.name          AS teacher,
    d.name          AS department,
    t.salary,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) AS dept_rank
FROM teachers t
JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, dept_rank;
```

---

## Assignment 4 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: LAG
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- For each student show their
-- current marks and previous exam marks
-- Also show improvement
-- (current - previous)
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- LAG(marks) OVER (
--     PARTITION BY student_id
--     ORDER BY exam_date
-- )
-- Subtract LAG from current for improvement

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s.name,
    e.exam_name,
    e.exam_date,
    r.marks         AS current_marks,
    LAG(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS prev_marks,
    r.marks - LAG(r.marks) OVER (
        PARTITION BY r.student_id
        ORDER BY e.exam_date
    ) AS improvement
FROM results r
JOIN students s ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e    ON r.exam_id = e.id
ORDER BY s.name, e.exam_date;
```

---

## Assignment 5 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: SUM OVER (Running Total)
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Show running total of fees collected
-- Each row shows total collected SO FAR
-- Only include paid fees
-- Sort by paid_date
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- SUM(amount) OVER (
--     ORDER BY paid_date
--     ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
--     AND CURRENT ROW
-- )

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s.name,
    f.paid_date,
    f.amount,
    SUM(f.amount) OVER (
        ORDER BY f.paid_date
        ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
        AND CURRENT ROW
    ) AS running_total
FROM fees f
JOIN students s
    ON f.student_id = s.id
WHERE f.status = 'paid'
ORDER BY f.paid_date;
```

---

## Assignment 6 - Medium

```sql
-- TOPIC: NTILE
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Divide all students into 3 groups
-- based on their marks
-- Group 1 = top performers
-- Group 2 = average
-- Group 3 = needs improvement
-- Show name, marks, group, label
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- NTILE(3) OVER (ORDER BY marks DESC)
-- Use CASE to label each group

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    s.name,
    r.marks,
    NTILE(3) OVER (
        ORDER BY r.marks DESC
    ) AS performance_group,
    CASE NTILE(3) OVER (ORDER BY r.marks DESC)
        WHEN 1 THEN 'Top Performer'
        WHEN 2 THEN 'Average'
        WHEN 3 THEN 'Needs Improvement'
    END AS performance_label
FROM results r
JOIN students s
    ON r.student_id = s.id
JOIN exams e
    ON r.exam_id = e.id
WHERE e.exam_type = 'final'
ORDER BY r.marks DESC;
```

---

# LEVEL 3 - HARD 🔴

---

## Assignment 7 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: ROW_NUMBER + TOP N per group
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Find TOP 2 highest scoring students
-- in EACH department
-- Show: student name, dept, marks
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Step 1: Use ROW_NUMBER with
--         PARTITION BY department_id
--         ORDER BY marks DESC
-- Step 2: Wrap in subquery
-- Step 3: WHERE rn <= 2

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    student,
    department,
    marks,
    rn AS rank_in_dept
FROM (
    SELECT
        s.name          AS student,
        d.name          AS department,
        r.marks,
        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
            PARTITION BY s.department_id
            ORDER BY r.marks DESC
        ) AS rn
    FROM results r
    JOIN students s
        ON r.student_id = s.id
    JOIN departments d
        ON s.department_id = d.id
    JOIN exams e
        ON r.exam_id = e.id
    WHERE e.exam_type = 'final'
) ranked
WHERE rn <= 2
ORDER BY department, rn;
```

---

## Assignment 8 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: FIRST_VALUE
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- For each teacher show:
-- their name, salary, department
-- AND the name of highest paid teacher
-- in their department
-- AND difference from highest salary
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- FIRST_VALUE(name) OVER (
--     PARTITION BY dept
--     ORDER BY salary DESC
-- )
-- FIRST_VALUE(salary) OVER (...)
-- Subtract to get difference

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    t.name              AS teacher,
    t.salary,
    d.name              AS department,
    FIRST_VALUE(t.name) OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) AS highest_paid_teacher,
    FIRST_VALUE(t.salary) OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) AS highest_salary,
    FIRST_VALUE(t.salary) OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) - t.salary AS gap_from_top
FROM teachers t
JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, t.salary DESC;
```

---

## Assignment 9 - Hard

```sql
-- TOPIC: LAG + LEAD together
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- For each teacher ordered by salary
-- show previous teacher salary,
-- current salary,
-- next teacher salary
-- Also show if their salary is
-- higher or lower than previous
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Use both LAG and LEAD
-- in same SELECT statement
-- CASE to show higher/lower/same

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    LAG(salary) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS prev_salary,
    LEAD(salary) OVER (
        ORDER BY salary
    ) AS next_salary,
    CASE
        WHEN salary > LAG(salary) OVER (
            ORDER BY salary
        ) THEN 'Higher than previous'
        WHEN salary < LAG(salary) OVER (
            ORDER BY salary
        ) THEN 'Lower than previous'
        WHEN LAG(salary) OVER (
            ORDER BY salary
        ) IS NULL THEN 'First Record'
        ELSE 'Same as previous'
    END AS comparison
FROM teachers
ORDER BY salary;
```

---

## Assignment 10 - Expert 🏆

```sql
-- TOPIC: Multiple window functions
-- ==========================================
-- QUESTION:
-- Complete teacher performance report:
-- Show for each teacher:
-- 1. Name, dept, salary
-- 2. Rank in their department
-- 3. Rank overall in company
-- 4. Salary percentile (PERCENT_RANK)
-- 5. Which salary band (NTILE 4)
-- 6. Difference from dept average
-- 7. Highest salary in their dept
-- ==========================================

-- HINT:
-- Use multiple window functions
-- each with different OVER clause
-- Some PARTITION BY dept
-- Some without PARTITION BY

-- YOUR ANSWER:




-- SOLUTION:
SELECT
    t.name                  AS teacher,
    d.name                  AS department,
    t.salary,

    -- Rank within department
    DENSE_RANK() OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) AS dept_rank,

    -- Overall company rank
    DENSE_RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY t.salary DESC
    ) AS company_rank,

    -- Salary percentile
    ROUND(PERCENT_RANK() OVER (
        ORDER BY t.salary
    ) * 100, 1) AS percentile,

    -- Salary band 1=low 4=high
    NTILE(4) OVER (
        ORDER BY t.salary
    ) AS salary_band,

    -- Dept average salary
    ROUND(AVG(t.salary) OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
    ), 2) AS dept_avg_salary,

    -- Difference from dept avg
    ROUND(t.salary - AVG(t.salary) OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
    ), 2) AS diff_from_dept_avg,

    -- Highest in department
    MAX(t.salary) OVER (
        PARTITION BY t.department_id
    ) AS dept_max_salary

FROM teachers t
JOIN departments d
    ON t.department_id = d.id
ORDER BY d.name, t.salary DESC;
```

---

# Quick Revision Sheet

```
FUNCTION      | USE FOR                | KEY SYNTAX
--------------|------------------------|------------------
ROW_NUMBER()  | Unique row numbers     | OVER(ORDER BY)
RANK()        | Rank with gaps         | OVER(ORDER BY)
DENSE_RANK()  | Rank without gaps      | OVER(ORDER BY)
NTILE(n)      | Divide into n buckets  | OVER(ORDER BY)
PERCENT_RANK()| Percentage rank 0-1    | OVER(ORDER BY)
LAG()         | Previous row value     | OVER(PARTITION BY ORDER BY)
LEAD()        | Next row value         | OVER(PARTITION BY ORDER BY)
FIRST_VALUE() | First in window        | OVER(PARTITION BY ORDER BY)
LAST_VALUE()  | Last in window         | OVER(PARTITION BY ORDER BY)
SUM OVER      | Running total          | OVER(ORDER BY ROWS BETWEEN)
AVG OVER      | Running average        | OVER(ORDER BY ROWS BETWEEN)

PARTITION BY = like GROUP BY (restart for each group)
ORDER BY     = sort within window
ROWS BETWEEN = define window size

ROW_NUMBER vs RANK vs DENSE_RANK:
  Marks: 90, 85, 85, 80
  ROW_NUMBER  → 1, 2, 3, 4  always unique
  RANK        → 1, 2, 2, 4  skips 3
  DENSE_RANK  → 1, 2, 2, 3  no skip
```

---

# Summary of assignments

```
No. | Level  | Topic                | Key Concept
----|--------|----------------------|------------------
1   | 🟢 Easy | ROW_NUMBER           | Basic numbering
2   | 🟢 Easy | RANK vs DENSE_RANK   | See difference
3   | 🟡 Med  | ROW_NUMBER PARTITION | Per group rank
4   | 🟡 Med  | LAG                  | Previous value
5   | 🟡 Med  | SUM OVER             | Running total
6   | 🟡 Med  | NTILE                | Group into bands
7   | 🔴 Hard | TOP N per group      | ROW_NUMBER filter
8   | 🔴 Hard | FIRST_VALUE          | Best in group
9   | 🔴 Hard | LAG + LEAD together  | Compare prev/next
10  | 🏆 Expert| All combined        | Full report
```

## Copilot

Here's a **complete line by line explanation**.

---

# Full Query

```sql
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
        PARTITION BY department_id
        ORDER BY salary DESC
    ) AS row_num
FROM teachers;
```

---

# Line by Line

---

## Line 1: SELECT

```sql
SELECT
```
```
SELECT = I want to READ data
         and choose WHICH columns to show

This is the start of our query
Everything after SELECT until FROM
tells database what columns to return

Think of it like:
  "Hey database, give me these columns..."
```

---

## Line 2: name,

```sql
    name,
```
```
name = column from teachers table

This shows the teacher's name
Example values:
  Amit Sharma
  Priya Patel
  Raj Kumar

The comma (,) after name means
"more columns are coming"
```

---

## Line 3: salary,

```sql
    salary,
```
```
salary = column from teachers table

This shows how much teacher earns
Example values:
  75000.00
  65000.00
  70000.00

Comma (,) means more columns coming
```

---

## Line 4: department_id,

```sql
    department_id,
```
```
department_id = column from teachers table

This shows which department
the teacher belongs to
Example values:
  1 = Computer Science
  2 = Mathematics
  3 = Physics

Comma (,) means more columns coming
```

---

## Line 5: ROW_NUMBER() OVER (

```sql
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
```
```
ROW_NUMBER() = window function
               Assigns a unique NUMBER
               to each row
               1, 2, 3, 4, 5...
               Never repeats
               Never skips

OVER = this is what makes it a
       WINDOW function
       Without OVER it would not work

OVER ( = opening bracket
        Everything inside () tells
        ROW_NUMBER HOW to assign numbers
        Which groups?
        Which order?

Think of it like:
ROW_NUMBER() = "assign numbers"
OVER(...)    = "but do it THIS way"
```

---

## Line 6: PARTITION BY department_id

```sql
        PARTITION BY department_id
```
```
PARTITION BY = divide data into groups
               Like GROUP BY but
               rows are NOT collapsed

department_id = divide by this column

This means:
  Group all dept 1 teachers together
  Group all dept 2 teachers together
  Group all dept 3 teachers together

ROW_NUMBER restarts from 1
for EACH department

WITHOUT PARTITION BY:
  All teachers → 1, 2, 3, 4, 5...
  Numbers never restart

WITH PARTITION BY department_id:
  Dept 1 teachers → 1, 2, 3
  Dept 2 teachers → 1, 2    ← restarts!
  Dept 3 teachers → 1, 2    ← restarts!

Think of it like:
  "Number the teachers BUT
   start fresh for each department"
```

---

## Line 7: ORDER BY salary DESC

```sql
        ORDER BY salary DESC
```
```
ORDER BY = sort the rows
           WITHIN each partition/group
           BEFORE assigning numbers

salary = sort by this column

DESC = descending order
       highest salary gets number 1
       second highest gets number 2
       and so on...

ASC  = ascending (lowest first)
DESC = descending (highest first)

This means:
  Within dept 1:
    80000 → row_num 1 (highest)
    75000 → row_num 2
    70000 → row_num 3

  Within dept 2:
    67000 → row_num 1 (highest in dept 2)
    65000 → row_num 2

So row_num = 1 always means
"highest paid in that department"
```

---

## Line 8: ) AS row_num

```sql
    ) AS row_num
```
```
) = closing bracket of OVER()

AS = alias
     Give this column a name

row_num = the name we give to
          the ROW_NUMBER() result

Without AS:
  Column header shows: ROW_NUMBER() OVER(...)
  Ugly and hard to read

With AS row_num:
  Column header shows: row_num
  Clean and readable

You can use any name:
  AS rank_number
  AS position
  AS serial_no
  AS row_num     ← we used this
```

---

## Line 9: FROM teachers;

```sql
FROM teachers;
```
```
FROM = which table to get data from

teachers = our teachers table
           contains all teacher records

; = semicolon
    marks END of SQL statement
    Always put at the end

This table has columns:
  id, name, email, phone,
  department_id, salary,
  joining_date, qualification,
  experience, is_active
```

---

# Complete explanation together

```sql
SELECT              -- read data, choose columns
    name,           -- show teacher name
    salary,         -- show teacher salary
    department_id,  -- show which department

    ROW_NUMBER()    -- assign unique numbers
    OVER (          -- define how to number
        PARTITION BY department_id  -- group by dept
        ORDER BY salary DESC        -- highest salary = 1
    ) AS row_num    -- call result "row_num"

FROM teachers;      -- get data from teachers table
```

---

# What output looks like

```
Before window function runs:
teachers table has:

id | name          | salary | dept_id
---|---------------|--------|--------
1  | Amit Sharma   | 75000  | 1
2  | Priya Patel   | 65000  | 2
3  | Raj Kumar     | 70000  | 3
4  | Sunita Singh  | 68000  | 4
7  | Suresh Mehta  | 72000  | 7
11 | Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 1
12 | Pooja Iyer    | 67000  | 2
13 | Kiran Shah    | 66000  | 3
15 | Manoj Tiwari  | 64000  | 4
```

---

```
Step 1: PARTITION BY department_id
        Database groups teachers by dept:

DEPT 1:           DEPT 2:           DEPT 3:
Amit  → 75000     Priya → 65000     Raj   → 70000
Arjun → 80000     Pooja → 67000     Kiran → 66000

DEPT 4:
Sunita → 68000
Manoj  → 64000
```

---

```
Step 2: ORDER BY salary DESC within each group

DEPT 1 sorted:    DEPT 2 sorted:    DEPT 3 sorted:
Arjun → 80000     Pooja → 67000     Raj   → 70000
Amit  → 75000     Priya → 65000     Kiran → 66000

DEPT 4 sorted:
Sunita → 68000
Manoj  → 64000
```

---

```
Step 3: ROW_NUMBER assigns numbers
        Restarts at 1 for each dept

DEPT 1:               DEPT 2:
Arjun → 80000 → 1     Pooja → 67000 → 1
Amit  → 75000 → 2     Priya → 65000 → 2

DEPT 3:               DEPT 4:
Raj   → 70000 → 1     Sunita → 68000 → 1
Kiran → 66000 → 2     Manoj  → 64000 → 2
```

---

```
FINAL OUTPUT:

name          | salary | dept_id | row_num
--------------|--------|---------|--------
Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 1       | 1  ← highest in dept 1
Amit Sharma   | 75000  | 1       | 2  ← 2nd in dept 1
Pooja Iyer    | 67000  | 2       | 1  ← highest in dept 2
Priya Patel   | 65000  | 2       | 2  ← 2nd in dept 2
Raj Kumar     | 70000  | 3       | 1  ← highest in dept 3
Kiran Shah    | 66000  | 3       | 2  ← 2nd in dept 3
Sunita Singh  | 68000  | 4       | 1  ← highest in dept 4
Manoj Tiwari  | 64000  | 4       | 2  ← 2nd in dept 4
```

---

# Most common use case

```sql
-- Find TOP 1 teacher per department
-- Using ROW_NUMBER result

SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,
    row_num
FROM (
    -- Our original query becomes subquery
    SELECT
        name,
        salary,
        department_id,
        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
            PARTITION BY department_id
            ORDER BY salary DESC
        ) AS row_num
    FROM teachers
) ranked
WHERE row_num = 1;  -- only keep rank 1 per dept

/*
OUTPUT: Only highest paid per department

name          | salary | dept_id | row_num
--------------|--------|---------|--------
Arjun Reddy   | 80000  | 1       | 1
Pooja Iyer    | 67000  | 2       | 1
Raj Kumar     | 70000  | 3       | 1
Sunita Singh  | 68000  | 4       | 1
*/
```

---

# What changes if you modify each part

```sql
-- Change 1: Remove PARTITION BY
-- Numbers run across ALL teachers
ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
-- Output: 1,2,3,4,5,6... never restarts

-- ==========================================

-- Change 2: Change ORDER BY to ASC
-- Lowest salary gets number 1
ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary ASC  -- lowest first
)

-- ==========================================

-- Change 3: PARTITION BY different column
-- Restart for each city instead
ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
    PARTITION BY city
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)

-- ==========================================

-- Change 4: Use RANK instead
-- Ties get same number
RANK() OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)

-- ==========================================

-- Change 5: Use DENSE_RANK instead
-- Ties same number, no gaps
DENSE_RANK() OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
```

---

# Quick revision

```
SELECT         → read data
name           → teacher name column
salary         → teacher salary column
department_id  → which dept column
ROW_NUMBER()   → assign unique numbers
OVER           → define the window
PARTITION BY   → divide into groups
               → restart count per group
ORDER BY DESC  → highest value = number 1
AS row_num     → name the result column
FROM teachers  → get from teachers table

Key rule:
  PARTITION BY = groups (like GROUP BY)
  ORDER BY     = who gets number 1
  row_num = 1  = always the TOP record
```

## Copilot

# ROW_NUMBER() OVER - Simple Explanation

---

```
Imagine you have a class of students.
Teacher says:
"Line up department-wise,
 tallest person stands first in each line"

PARTITION BY department_id = make separate lines per department
ORDER BY salary DESC        = tallest (highest salary) stands first
ROW_NUMBER()                = give each person a number 1,2,3...

Each department line starts from 1 again.
So number 1 in every line = highest paid in that department.

That's it.
```

---

## See it visually

```
DEPT 1 LINE:          DEPT 2 LINE:
Arjun 80000 → 1       Pooja 67000 → 1
Amit  75000 → 2       Priya 65000 → 2

Row number 1 = TOP person in each department.
```

---

## One line summary

```
ROW_NUMBER = give serial number
PARTITION  = start fresh for each group
ORDER BY   = who gets number 1
```

Want me to explain **RANK, DENSE_RANK, LAG** same way?

## @brehman_uhg

syntax for all

## Copilot

# All Window Functions Syntax - Quick Reference

---

## 1) ROW_NUMBER
```sql
-- Unique number to each row
-- 1,2,3,4 never repeats

ROW_NUMBER() OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id   -- group by dept
    ORDER BY salary DESC         -- highest = 1
)
```

---

## 2) RANK
```sql
-- Same value = same rank
-- Skips next number after tie
-- 1,2,2,4 (skips 3)

RANK() OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
```

---

## 3) DENSE_RANK
```sql
-- Same value = same rank
-- NO skip after tie
-- 1,2,2,3 (no skip)

DENSE_RANK() OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
```

---

## 4) NTILE
```sql
-- Divide rows into N buckets
-- NTILE(4) = 4 groups

NTILE(4) OVER (
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
```

---

## 5) LAG
```sql
-- Get value from PREVIOUS row

LAG(salary)        OVER (ORDER BY salary)  -- 1 row back
LAG(salary, 2)     OVER (ORDER BY salary)  -- 2 rows back
LAG(salary, 1, 0)  OVER (ORDER BY salary)  -- default 0 if no prev row
```

---

## 6) LEAD
```sql
-- Get value from NEXT row

LEAD(salary)        OVER (ORDER BY salary)  -- 1 row forward
LEAD(salary, 2)     OVER (ORDER BY salary)  -- 2 rows forward
LEAD(salary, 1, 0)  OVER (ORDER BY salary)  -- default 0 if no next row
```

---

## 7) FIRST_VALUE
```sql
-- Get FIRST value in the window

FIRST_VALUE(salary) OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
```

---

## 8) LAST_VALUE
```sql
-- Get LAST value in the window

LAST_VALUE(salary) OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id
    ORDER BY salary DESC
    ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
    AND UNBOUNDED FOLLOWING     -- important for LAST_VALUE
)
```

---

## 9) SUM OVER (Running Total)
```sql
-- Cumulative sum row by row

SUM(salary) OVER (
    ORDER BY id
    ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING
    AND CURRENT ROW
)
```

---

## 10) AVG OVER
```sql
-- Running average OR group average

AVG(salary) OVER (
    PARTITION BY department_id  -- avg per dept
)
```

---

## 11) PERCENT_RANK
```sql
-- Rank as percentage 0 to 1

PERCENT_RANK() OVER (
    ORDER BY salary DESC
)
```

---

# All in ONE query

```sql
SELECT
    name,
    salary,
    department_id,

    ROW_NUMBER()    OVER (PARTITION BY department_id ORDER BY salary DESC) AS row_num,
    RANK()          OVER (PARTITION BY department_id ORDER BY salary DESC) AS rnk,
    DENSE_RANK()    OVER (PARTITION BY department_id ORDER BY salary DESC) AS dense_rnk,
    NTILE(4)        OVER (ORDER BY salary DESC)                            AS bucket,
    LAG(salary)     OVER (ORDER BY salary)                                 AS prev_sal,
    LEAD(salary)    OVER (ORDER BY salary)                                 AS next_sal,
    FIRST_VALUE(salary) OVER (PARTITION BY department_id ORDER BY salary DESC) AS top_sal,
    SUM(salary)     OVER (ORDER BY id ROWS BETWEEN UNBOUNDED PRECEDING AND CURRENT ROW) AS running_total,
    AVG(salary)     OVER (PARTITION BY department_id)                      AS dept_avg,
    PERCENT_RANK()  OVER (ORDER BY salary)                                 AS pct_rank

FROM teachers;
```

---

# Super Quick Cheat Sheet

```
FUNCTION          RETURNS
----------------- --------------------------------
ROW_NUMBER()      1,2,3,4       always unique
RANK()            1,2,2,4       gaps after tie
DENSE_RANK()      1,2,2,3       no gaps
NTILE(n)          1 to n        bucket number
LAG(col)          previous row value
LEAD(col)         next row value
FIRST_VALUE(col)  first in group
LAST_VALUE(col)   last in group
SUM() OVER        running total
AVG() OVER        running or group average
PERCENT_RANK()    0.0 to 1.0

OVER()            required for all above
PARTITION BY      restart per group
ORDER BY          sort within group
```

olap and oltp def

## Copilot

# OLAP vs OLTP - Simple Definition

---

## OLTP
```
OLTP = Online Transaction Processing

Used for DAY TO DAY operations
Insert, Update, Delete frequently
Small queries, fast response
Current data only

Examples:
  Bank ATM transaction
  Online shopping order
  Student fee payment
  Hospital patient registration

Who uses it:
  Cashiers, clerks, customers
```

---

## OLAP
```
OLAP = Online Analytical Processing

Used for ANALYSIS and REPORTING
Read heavy, complex queries
Large data, slow response ok
Historical data

Examples:
  Sales report of last 5 years
  Which product sold most this year
  Student performance analysis
  Hospital monthly report

Who uses it:
  Managers, analysts, data scientists
```

---

## Simple one line difference

```
OLTP = daily work    → INSERT UPDATE DELETE
OLAP = analysis work → SELECT heavy reporting
```

---

## Comparison table

```
Feature        OLTP              OLAP
-------------- ----------------- -----------------
Full Name      Online Transaction Online Analytical
               Processing        Processing

Purpose        Daily operations  Analysis/Reporting

Operations     INSERT/UPDATE/     SELECT (complex)
               DELETE

Data Size      Small per query   Millions of rows

Speed          Very fast         Can be slow

Data           Current data      Historical data

Users          Employees         Analysts/Managers

Example DB     MySQL, PostgreSQL  Snowflake, Redshift

Normalization  Highly normalized Denormalized

Tables         Many small tables Few large tables

Example        Bank transaction  Sales yearly report
```

---

## Real life example

```
SCHOOL SYSTEM:

OLTP:
  Student pays fee      → INSERT into fees
  Teacher marks attend  → INSERT into attendance
  Student enrolls       → INSERT into enrollments
  Update student grade  → UPDATE results

OLAP:
  Which dept has best results last 3 years?
  How has fee collection grown year by year?
  Which teacher has highest pass rate?
  Compare student performance across batches
```

---

## Simple memory trick

```
OLTP = Online TRANSACTION  = T = Today's work
OLAP = Online ANALYTICAL   = A = Analysis work

T = Transaction = small fast daily
A = Analysis    = big slow reporting
```

## @brehman_uhg

what is datawarehouse

## Copilot

# Data Warehouse - Simple Explanation

---

## What is it?

```
Normal Database:
  Stores current data
  For daily operations
  Like a CASH REGISTER

Data Warehouse:
  Stores historical data
  For analysis and reporting
  Like a LIBRARY of all past records

Simple definition:
  Data Warehouse = big storage system
  that collects data from
  MULTIPLE sources
  and stores it for ANALYSIS
```

---

## Real life example

```
A SCHOOL has many systems:

System 1 → Student database
System 2 → Fee management system
System 3 → Attendance system
System 4 → Library system
System 5 → Exam system

Each system has its OWN database.
Principal wants ONE report showing:
  - Student performance
  - Fee collection
  - Attendance percentage
  - Library usage
  ALL TOGETHER for last 5 years

SOLUTION = Data Warehouse
  Collect data from ALL systems
  Store in ONE place
  Analyze together
```

---

## Simple diagram

```
SOURCE SYSTEMS          DATA WAREHOUSE        REPORTS
--------------          --------------        -------
Student DB    ──┐
Fee DB        ──┤                            Dashboard
Attendance DB ──┼──► ETL Process ──► DWH ──► Reports
Library DB    ──┤                            Analysis
Exam DB       ──┘

ETL = Extract Transform Load
      Extract  = pull data from sources
      Transform = clean and format
      Load      = put into warehouse
```

---

## Database vs Data Warehouse

```
Feature          Database           Data Warehouse
---------------- ------------------ ------------------
Purpose          Daily operations   Analysis/Reporting
Data Type        Current data       Historical data
Data Source      Single system      Multiple systems
Query Type       Simple CRUD        Complex analytics
Size             GBs                TBs or PBs
Speed            Fast transactions  Slow complex queries
Users            Employees          Analysts/Managers
Update           Frequent           Periodic (batch)
Example          MySQL, PostgreSQL   Snowflake, Redshift
Design           Normalized         Denormalized
```

---

## Data Warehouse Architecture

```
LAYER 1: Source Layer
  All operational databases
  Student DB, Fee DB, HR DB etc

      ↓ ETL Process ↓

LAYER 2: Staging Layer
  Temporary storage
  Data cleaning happens here
  Remove duplicates
  Fix formats
  Handle nulls

      ↓ Load ↓

LAYER 3: Data Warehouse Layer
  Clean historical data
  Fact tables
  Dimension tables
  Star schema design

      ↓ Query ↓

LAYER 4: Presentation Layer
  Reports
  Dashboards
  Analytics tools
  Power BI, Tableau
```

---

## Key concepts in Data Warehouse

---

### 1) Fact Table
```
Stores NUMBERS and MEASUREMENTS
The main data you want to analyze

Example:
FACT_SALES table:
  sale_id
  amount        ← number
  quantity      ← number
  date_id       ← foreign key
  student_id    ← foreign key
  course_id     ← foreign key
```

---

### 2) Dimension Table
```
Stores DESCRIPTIVE information
Gives context to fact table

Example:
DIM_STUDENT table:
  student_id
  name
  city
  gender
  department

DIM_DATE table:
  date_id
  date
  month
  quarter
  year
```

---

### 3) Star Schema
```
One FACT table in center
DIMENSION tables around it
Like a star shape

         DIM_DATE
             |
DIM_STUDENT──FACT_RESULTS──DIM_COURSE
             |
         DIM_EXAM

Simple and fast for queries
Most common design
```

---

### 4) Snowflake Schema
```
Like Star Schema but
dimension tables are normalized
More tables, more complex

DIM_STUDENT → DIM_CITY → DIM_STATE
     |
FACT_RESULTS
     |
DIM_COURSE → DIM_DEPARTMENT

More storage efficient
Slower queries than star schema
```

---

## ETL Process explained

```
E = EXTRACT
    Pull data from source systems
    Student DB → extract student records
    Fee DB     → extract payment records

T = TRANSFORM
    Clean and prepare data
    - Remove duplicates
    - Fix null values
    - Convert formats
    - 01/01/2024 → 2024-01-01
    - "male" → "M"
    - Calculate new columns

L = LOAD
    Put clean data into warehouse
    - Full load   = load everything
    - Incremental = load only new data

Runs on schedule:
    Daily at midnight
    Weekly on Sunday
    Monthly on 1st
```

---

## Popular Data Warehouse tools

```
Cloud:
  Snowflake         → most popular
  Amazon Redshift   → AWS
  Google BigQuery   → GCP
  Azure Synapse     → Microsoft

On-premise:
  Oracle DW
  Teradata
  IBM Db2

ETL Tools:
  Azure Data Factory  ← you mentioned this
  Apache Airflow
  Informatica
  Talend
  AWS Glue
```

---

## Azure Data Warehouse setup

```
SOURCE DATA
    ↓
Azure Data Factory (ETL)
    ↓
Azure Data Lake (raw storage)
    ↓
Azure Synapse Analytics (warehouse)
    ↓
Power BI (reports)
```

---

## Simple SQL in Data Warehouse

```sql
-- Fact table
CREATE TABLE fact_results (
    result_id    INT,
    marks        DECIMAL,
    date_id      INT,
    student_id   INT,
    course_id    INT,
    exam_id      INT
);

-- Dimension table
CREATE TABLE dim_student (
    student_id   INT,
    name         VARCHAR(100),
    city         VARCHAR(50),
    gender       VARCHAR(10),
    department   VARCHAR(100)
);

-- Dimension date
CREATE TABLE dim_date (
    date_id      INT,
    full_date    DATE,
    day          INT,
    month        INT,
    quarter      INT,
    year         INT
);

-- Analytical query
-- Average marks per department per year
SELECT
    ds.department,
    dd.year,
    ROUND(AVG(fr.marks), 2) AS avg_marks,
    COUNT(*)                AS total_exams
FROM fact_results fr
JOIN dim_student ds ON fr.student_id = ds.student_id
JOIN dim_date dd    ON fr.date_id    = dd.date_id
GROUP BY ds.department, dd.year
ORDER BY dd.year, avg_marks DESC;
```

---

## Quick revision

```
Data Warehouse:
  = central storage for historical data
  = data from multiple sources
  = used for analysis and reporting

Key parts:
  ETL    = Extract Transform Load
  Fact   = numbers/measurements
  Dim    = descriptions/context
  Star   = simple schema design
  OLAP   = analytical processing

Flow:
  Source DB → ETL → Staging → DWH → Reports

Popular tools:
  Snowflake, Redshift, BigQuery,
  Azure Synapse, Azure Data Factory
```

3. **Azure Data Factory explained**
4. **Data Warehouse interview questions**

## @brehman_uhg

what is normalisation in simpel lanug explain with example

## Copilot

# Normalization - Simple Explanation

---

## What is it?

```
Normalization = organizing your table
to remove repeated data
and keep data clean

Simple example:
  Instead of writing
  "Computer Science" 100 times
  in 100 rows

  Write it ONCE in one table
  and just use its ID number
  in other tables

Goal:
  No duplicate data
  No data inconsistency
  Clean organized tables
```

---

## Problem without Normalization

```
BAD TABLE - everything in one table:

student_id | student_name | course    | teacher  | teacher_phone | dept
-----------|--------------|-----------|----------|---------------|-----
1          | Aman         | Python    | Amit     | 9876543210    | CS
2          | Sara         | Python    | Amit     | 9876543210    | CS
3          | Raj          | Python    | Amit     | 9876543210    | CS
4          | Priya        | Maths     | Priya    | 9876543211    | Maths
5          | Ahmed        | Maths     | Priya    | 9876543211    | Maths

PROBLEMS:
  Amit's phone repeated 3 times
  If Amit changes phone →
  update 3 rows → miss one → WRONG DATA
  This is called data anomaly
```

---

## Solution with Normalization

```
Split into clean tables:

STUDENTS:            COURSES:          TEACHERS:
id | name            id | course_name  id | name  | phone
---|-----            ---|----------    ---|-------|------
1  | Aman            1  | Python       1  | Amit  | 98765
2  | Sara            2  | Maths        2  | Priya | 98766
3  | Raj
4  | Priya

Now Amit's phone stored ONCE
Change once → updated everywhere
```

---

# Normal Forms

---

## 1NF - First Normal Form

```
RULE:
Each column should have
ONE single value
No repeating groups

BAD - multiple values in one cell:
student | courses
--------|------------------
Aman    | Python, Maths, English
Sara    | Python, English

GOOD - one value per cell:
student | course
--------|-------
Aman    | Python
Aman    | Maths
Aman    | English
Sara    | Python
Sara    | English
```

---

## 2NF - Second Normal Form

```
RULE:
Must be in 1NF first
Every column must depend on
WHOLE primary key
not just part of it

BAD TABLE:
primary key = (student_id + course_id)

student_id | course_id | marks | student_name | course_name
-----------|-----------|-------|--------------|------------
1          | 1         | 85    | Aman         | Python
1          | 2         | 90    | Aman         | Maths

PROBLEM:
  student_name depends only on student_id
  course_name depends only on course_id
  NOT on the combination of both

SOLUTION - split into 3 tables:

STUDENTS:        COURSES:         RESULTS:
id | name        id | name        student_id | course_id | marks
---|----         ---|------       -----------|-----------|------
1  | Aman        1  | Python      1          | 1         | 85
2  | Sara        2  | Maths       1          | 2         | 90
```

---

## 3NF - Third Normal Form

```
RULE:
Must be in 2NF first
No column should depend
on another NON-KEY column

BAD TABLE:
student_id | name | dept_id | dept_name | dept_location
-----------|------|---------|-----------|---------------
1          | Aman | 1       | CS        | Block A
2          | Sara | 2       | Maths     | Block B

PROBLEM:
  dept_name depends on dept_id
  dept_location depends on dept_id
  NOT on student_id directly
  This is called transitive dependency

SOLUTION - split into 2 tables:

STUDENTS:                    DEPARTMENTS:
id | name | dept_id          id | name  | location
---|------|--------          ---|-------|----------
1  | Aman | 1                1  | CS    | Block A
2  | Sara | 2                2  | Maths | Block B
```

---

## All 3 together - Real example

```
START: One messy table

id | student | course  | teacher | t_phone    | dept  | marks
---|---------|---------|---------|------------|-------|------
1  | Aman    | Python  | Amit    | 9876543210 | CS    | 85
2  | Aman    | Maths   | Priya   | 9876543211 | Maths | 90
3  | Sara    | Python  | Amit    | 9876543210 | CS    | 78
4  | Raj     | Physics | Raj K   | 9876543212 | Phys  | 88


AFTER 1NF:
  Each cell has one value ✓
  Already done above ✓

AFTER 2NF:
  Split student info and course info

  STUDENTS:          COURSES:
  id | name          id | name    | teacher | t_phone
  ---|-----          ---|---------|---------|----------
  1  | Aman          1  | Python  | Amit    | 9876543210
  2  | Sara          2  | Maths   | Priya   | 9876543211
  3  | Raj           3  | Physics | Raj K   | 9876543212

  RESULTS:
  student_id | course_id | marks
  -----------|-----------|------
  1          | 1         | 85
  1          | 2         | 90
  2          | 1         | 78
  3          | 3         | 88

AFTER 3NF:
  Teacher phone depends on teacher
  not on course
  Split again

  TEACHERS:               COURSES:
  id | name  | phone      id | name    | teacher_id
  ---|-------|--------    ---|---------|----------
  1  | Amit  | 987654     1  | Python  | 1
  2  | Priya | 987655     2  | Maths   | 2
  3  | Raj K | 987656     3  | Physics | 3
```

---

## Final clean normalized database

```
4 clean tables:

STUDENTS          TEACHERS
id | name         id | name  | phone
1  | Aman         1  | Amit  | 9876543210
2  | Sara         2  | Priya | 9876543211
3  | Raj          3  | Raj K | 9876543212

COURSES                    RESULTS
id | name    | teacher_id  s_id | c_id | marks
1  | Python  | 1           1    | 1    | 85
2  | Maths   | 2           1    | 2    | 90
3  | Physics | 3           2    | 1    | 78
                           3    | 3    | 88
```

---

## Quick revision

```
1NF = one value per cell
      no repeating groups

2NF = 1NF +
      every column depends on
      FULL primary key

3NF = 2NF +
      no column depends on
      another non-key column

Simple rule:
  Each fact stored ONCE
  Each table has ONE topic
  Use IDs to link tables

Benefits:
  No duplicate data
  Easy to update
  No data inconsistency
  Saves storage space

Disadvantage:
  Need JOINs to get data
  More tables to manage
```

what is partail dependcny and what is transitve dependency

## Copilot

# Partial and Transitive Dependency - Simple Explanation

---

## First understand - what is dependency?

```
Dependency = one column's value
             depends on another column

Example:
  student_name depends on student_id
  If you know student_id = 1
  you know name = Aman

  We write it as:
  student_id → student_name
  (student_id DETERMINES student_name)
```

---

# Partial Dependency

---

## What is it?

```
Partial Dependency =
  a column depends on only
  PART of the primary key
  not the WHOLE primary key

This happens when:
  Primary key has TWO or more columns
  (composite primary key)
  and some column depends on
  only ONE of those columns
```

---

## Simple example

```
TABLE: student_courses

PRIMARY KEY = (student_id + course_id)
Both together identify each row

student_id | course_id | marks | student_name | course_name
-----------|-----------|-------|--------------|------------
1          | 1         | 85    | Aman         | Python
1          | 2         | 90    | Aman         | Maths
2          | 1         | 78    | Sara         | Python
3          | 3         | 88    | Raj          | Physics
```

---

## Find the dependencies

```
marks depends on student_id + course_id
  → need BOTH to know marks
  → Aman in Python = 85
  → Aman in Maths  = 90
  → FULL dependency ✓ (this is OK)

student_name depends on ONLY student_id
  → just need student_id to know name
  → student_id = 1 → always Aman
  → course_id does not matter
  → PARTIAL dependency ✗ (problem!)

course_name depends on ONLY course_id
  → just need course_id to know name
  → course_id = 1 → always Python
  → student_id does not matter
  → PARTIAL dependency ✗ (problem!)
```

---

## Diagram

```
PRIMARY KEY = (student_id + course_id)

student_id ──────────────────► student_name
                                (PARTIAL - only half key)

course_id  ──────────────────► course_name
                                (PARTIAL - only half key)

student_id + course_id ──────► marks
                                (FULL - whole key, OK)
```

---

## Fix partial dependency (2NF)

```
Split into 3 tables:

STUDENTS:              COURSES:
id | name              id | name
---|-----              ---|-------
1  | Aman              1  | Python
2  | Sara              2  | Maths
3  | Raj               3  | Physics

RESULTS:
student_id | course_id | marks
-----------|-----------|------
1          | 1         | 85
1          | 2         | 90
2          | 1         | 78

Now:
  student_name lives in students table
  course_name lives in courses table
  marks depends on BOTH ids
  Partial dependency REMOVED ✓
```

---

---

# Transitive Dependency

---

## What is it?

```
Transitive Dependency =
  column A depends on column B
  column B depends on column C
  so column A indirectly depends on C

Simple words:
  Non-key column depends on
  ANOTHER non-key column
  instead of depending on primary key

A → B → C
C depends on A through B
This is transitive dependency
```

---

## Simple example

```
TABLE: students

PRIMARY KEY = student_id

student_id | name | dept_id | dept_name | dept_location
-----------|------|---------|-----------|---------------
1          | Aman | 1       | CS        | Block A
2          | Sara | 2       | Maths     | Block B
3          | Raj  | 1       | CS        | Block A
4          | Priya| 3       | Physics   | Block C
```

---

## Find the dependencies

```
student_id → name
  student_id determines name
  DIRECT dependency ✓ (OK)

student_id → dept_id
  student_id determines dept_id
  DIRECT dependency ✓ (OK)

dept_id → dept_name
  dept_id determines dept_name
  dept 1 = always CS
  dept 2 = always Maths
  NON-KEY depends on NON-KEY ✗ (problem!)

dept_id → dept_location
  dept_id determines dept_location
  dept 1 = always Block A
  NON-KEY depends on NON-KEY ✗ (problem!)

So:
  student_id → dept_id → dept_name
  student_id → dept_id → dept_location

  dept_name and dept_location
  depend on student_id
  THROUGH dept_id
  This is TRANSITIVE dependency
```

---

## Diagram

```
student_id ──► dept_id ──► dept_name
                      └──► dept_location

dept_name reaches student_id
THROUGH dept_id
= Transitive dependency
```

---

## Fix transitive dependency (3NF)

```
Split into 2 tables:

STUDENTS:                    DEPARTMENTS:
id | name | dept_id          id | name    | location
---|------|--------          ---|---------|----------
1  | Aman | 1                1  | CS      | Block A
2  | Sara | 2                2  | Maths   | Block B
3  | Raj  | 1                3  | Physics | Block C
4  | Priya| 3

Now:
  dept_name lives in departments table
  dept_location lives in departments table
  They depend on dept_id directly
  Transitive dependency REMOVED ✓
```

---

# Side by side comparison

```
PARTIAL DEPENDENCY:
  Needs composite primary key
  Column depends on PART of key
  Fix by splitting table (2NF)

  (student_id + course_id) → marks    OK
  student_id alone → student_name     PARTIAL

TRANSITIVE DEPENDENCY:
  Primary key can be single column
  Non-key depends on another non-key
  Fix by splitting table (3NF)

  student_id → dept_id → dept_name    TRANSITIVE
  dept_name should depend on
  dept_id directly not through student
```

---

## One line summary

```
PARTIAL    = column depends on HALF the key
             (composite key problem)

TRANSITIVE = column depends on another
             NON-KEY column
             (A → B → C problem)
```

---

## Memory trick

```
PARTIAL     = HALF key
              like getting partial marks
              in an exam
              not full marks

TRANSITIVE  = MIDDLE MAN
              like A tells B tells C
              instead of A telling C directly
              remove the middle man
```

---

## Copilot

# Partial vs Transitive Dependency - 3 Lines Each

---

## Partial Dependency

```
When primary key has TWO columns (composite key)
and some column depends on only ONE of them
instead of BOTH together.

Example:
(student_id + course_id) is primary key
student_name depends only on student_id = PARTIAL
```

---

## Transitive Dependency

```
When a non-key column depends on
another non-key column
instead of directly depending on primary key.

Example:
student_id → dept_id → dept_name
dept_name depends on dept_id not student_id = TRANSITIVE
```

---

## One line each

```
PARTIAL    = column needs only HALF the key
TRANSITIVE = non-key column depends on another NON-KEY column
```

# Python Concepts + RAG + LLM - Complete Guide

---

# 1) GENERATOR

---

## What is it?
```
Generator = function that returns
            values ONE AT A TIME
            instead of all at once

Normal function = returns all values at once
Generator       = returns one value, PAUSES,
                  returns next, PAUSES...

Uses YIELD instead of RETURN
Saves memory - does not store all values
```

---

## Syntax
```python
# Normal function
def normal():
    return [1, 2, 3]     # returns all at once

# Generator function
def generator():
    yield 1              # returns 1, pauses
    yield 2              # returns 2, pauses
    yield 3              # returns 3, pauses
```

---

## Example
```python
# ==========================================
# BASIC GENERATOR
# ==========================================
def count_up(n):
    i = 1
    while i <= n:
        yield i          # pause and return i
        i += 1

# Use generator
gen = count_up(5)

print(next(gen))   # 1
print(next(gen))   # 2
print(next(gen))   # 3

# Loop through generator
for num in count_up(5):
    print(num)
# 1, 2, 3, 4, 5

# ==========================================
# REAL EXAMPLE
# Read large file line by line
# ==========================================
def read_large_file(filename):
    with open(filename, 'r') as f:
        for line in f:
            yield line   # one line at a time
                         # not whole file in memory

# ==========================================
# GENERATOR EXPRESSION
# Like list comprehension but lazy
# ==========================================
# List comprehension - stores all in memory
my_list = [x * 2 for x in range(10)]

# Generator expression - one at a time
my_gen  = (x * 2 for x in range(10))

print(next(my_gen))   # 0
print(next(my_gen))   # 2
```

---

## Simple trick to remember
```
RETURN  = give everything and STOP
YIELD   = give one, PAUSE, continue later

Like a vending machine:
  return = gives all snacks at once
  yield  = gives one snack at a time
```

---

---

# 2) DECORATOR

---

## What is it?
```
Decorator = function that WRAPS
            another function
            adds extra behaviour
            without changing original code

Like a gift wrapper:
  Gift    = original function
  Wrapper = decorator
  You add wrapper around gift
  Gift inside stays same
```

---

## Syntax
```python
# Define decorator
def my_decorator(func):
    def wrapper():
        # code BEFORE function runs
        print("before")
        func()           # call original function
        # code AFTER function runs
        print("after")
    return wrapper

# Apply decorator using @
@my_decorator
def say_hello():
    print("Hello!")

# Call function
say_hello()
# Output:
# before
# Hello!
# after
```

---

## Examples
```python
# ==========================================
# EXAMPLE 1: Timer decorator
# ==========================================
import time

def timer(func):
    def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):
        start = time.time()
        result = func(*args, **kwargs)
        end = time.time()
        print(f"Time taken: {end - start} seconds")
        return result
    return wrapper

@timer
def slow_function():
    time.sleep(2)
    print("Done!")

slow_function()
# Done!
# Time taken: 2.0 seconds

# ==========================================
# EXAMPLE 2: Login check decorator
# ==========================================
def login_required(func):
    def wrapper(user, *args, **kwargs):
        if user.get('is_logged_in'):
            return func(user, *args, **kwargs)
        else:
            print("Please login first!")
    return wrapper

@login_required
def view_dashboard(user):
    print(f"Welcome {user['name']}!")

# Test
user1 = {'name': 'Aman', 'is_logged_in': True}
user2 = {'name': 'Sara', 'is_logged_in': False}

view_dashboard(user1)   # Welcome Aman!
view_dashboard(user2)   # Please login first!

# ==========================================
# EXAMPLE 3: Logger decorator
# ==========================================
def logger(func):
    def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):
        print(f"Calling: {func.__name__}")
        print(f"Arguments: {args}")
        result = func(*args, **kwargs)
        print(f"Result: {result}")
        return result
    return wrapper

@logger
def add(a, b):
    return a + b

add(3, 5)
# Calling: add
# Arguments: (3, 5)
# Result: 8
```

---

## Simple trick to remember
```
Decorator = add extra features
            to existing function
            without touching it

Like CCTV camera on a door:
  Door     = original function
  Camera   = decorator
  Camera watches who enters/exits
  Door still works same way
```

---

---

# 3) ITERATOR

---

## What is it?
```
Iterator = object that lets you
           go through items
           ONE BY ONE
           using next()

Every generator is an iterator
But not every iterator is a generator

Two methods needed:
  __iter__() = returns iterator object
  __next__() = returns next value
```

---

## Syntax
```python
# Make a class an iterator
class MyIterator:
    def __iter__(self):    # required
        return self

    def __next__(self):    # required
        # return next value
        # raise StopIteration when done
```

---

## Examples
```python
# ==========================================
# EXAMPLE 1: Basic iterator class
# ==========================================
class CountUp:
    def __init__(self, start, end):
        self.current = start
        self.end = end

    def __iter__(self):
        return self

    def __next__(self):
        if self.current <= self.end:
            value = self.current
            self.current += 1
            return value
        else:
            raise StopIteration  # tells loop to stop

# Use iterator
counter = CountUp(1, 5)
for num in counter:
    print(num)
# 1, 2, 3, 4, 5

# Using next() manually
counter2 = CountUp(1, 3)
print(next(counter2))   # 1
print(next(counter2))   # 2
print(next(counter2))   # 3
# print(next(counter2)) # StopIteration error

# ==========================================
# EXAMPLE 2: Built-in iterators
# ==========================================
# Lists, strings, dicts are ITERABLE
# iter() makes them ITERATOR

my_list = [1, 2, 3]
it = iter(my_list)
print(next(it))    # 1
print(next(it))    # 2
print(next(it))    # 3

# String iterator
my_str = "Aman"
it = iter(my_str)
print(next(it))    # A
print(next(it))    # m

# ==========================================
# EXAMPLE 3: Iterator vs Iterable
# ==========================================
my_list = [1, 2, 3]   # ITERABLE (can loop over)
it = iter(my_list)     # ITERATOR (has next())

# For loop internally does this:
it = iter(my_list)
while True:
    try:
        item = next(it)
        print(item)
    except StopIteration:
        break
```

---

## Generator vs Iterator vs Iterable

```python
# ITERABLE  = can be looped over
#             has __iter__()
#             list, string, dict, tuple

# ITERATOR  = has __iter__() AND __next__()
#             remembers position
#             goes forward only

# GENERATOR = special iterator
#             uses yield
#             simpler to write

# Check if something is iterable
my_list = [1, 2, 3]
it = iter(my_list)      # works = iterable

my_gen = (x for x in range(5))
print(next(my_gen))     # works = iterator
```

---

## Simple trick to remember
```
ITERABLE  = can be looped   (list, string)
ITERATOR  = has next()      (iter(list))
GENERATOR = auto iterator   (uses yield)

Like a book:
  ITERABLE  = book (you can read it)
  ITERATOR  = bookmark (remembers page)
  GENERATOR = someone reading page by page to you
```

---

---

# 4) RAG

---

## Full form
```
RAG = Retrieval Augmented Generation
```

---

## What does it do?
```
Problem with normal LLM:
  LLM knows only what it was trained on
  Training data has a cutoff date
  Does not know YOUR private documents
  Cannot answer company specific questions

RAG Solution:
  RETRIEVAL   = search relevant documents
  AUGMENTED   = add that info to prompt
  GENERATION  = LLM generates answer
                using retrieved info

Simple words:
  Instead of asking LLM from memory
  First FIND relevant documents
  Then GIVE those docs to LLM
  Then LLM answers using those docs
```

---

## How RAG works - step by step
```
STEP 1: INDEXING (done once)
  Take your documents
  Split into chunks
  Convert to vectors (embeddings)
  Store in vector database

STEP 2: RETRIEVAL (each query)
  User asks question
  Convert question to vector
  Search similar vectors in DB
  Get top matching chunks

STEP 3: GENERATION
  Take retrieved chunks
  Add to prompt:
  "Using this context: {chunks}
   Answer this: {question}"
  LLM generates final answer

FLOW:
User Question
    ↓
Convert to Embedding
    ↓
Search Vector DB
    ↓
Get Relevant Chunks
    ↓
Send to LLM with context
    ↓
LLM generates Answer
```

---

## Simple example
```
Company has 1000 HR policy documents
Employee asks: "How many leaves do I get?"

WITHOUT RAG:
  LLM does not know your HR policy
  Gives generic answer
  WRONG for your company

WITH RAG:
  Search HR documents for "leaves"
  Find relevant policy document
  Give that to LLM as context
  LLM answers correctly from YOUR policy
```

---

## RAG code example
```python
# Simple RAG flow
from openai import OpenAI

# Step 1: Your documents (already stored)
documents = [
    "Employees get 20 paid leaves per year",
    "Sick leave is 10 days per year",
    "Casual leave is 5 days per year"
]

# Step 2: Search relevant docs
def retrieve_docs(question, documents):
    # In real RAG use vector search
    # Simple example: keyword search
    relevant = []
    for doc in documents:
        if any(word in doc.lower()
               for word in question.lower().split()):
            relevant.append(doc)
    return relevant

# Step 3: Generate answer
def rag_answer(question):
    # Retrieve relevant documents
    context = retrieve_docs(question, documents)
    context_text = "\n".join(context)

    # Build prompt with context
    prompt = f"""
    Context information:
    {context_text}

    Based on above context answer:
    {question}
    """

    # Send to LLM
    client = OpenAI()
    response = client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=[
            {"role": "user", "content": prompt}
        ]
    )
    return response.choices[0].message.content

# Use RAG
answer = rag_answer("How many leaves do I get?")
print(answer)
# "You get 20 paid leaves, 10 sick leaves
#  and 5 casual leaves per year"
```

---

---

# 5) LLM

---

## Full form
```
LLM = Large Language Model
```

---

## What is it?
```
LLM = AI model trained on
      massive amounts of text data
      to understand and generate
      human language

Large    = billions of parameters
Language = understands human text
Model    = mathematical model

Examples:
  GPT-4      → OpenAI
  GPT-3.5    → OpenAI
  Claude     → Anthropic
  Gemini     → Google
  Llama      → Meta
  Mistral    → Mistral AI
```

---

## How LLM works - simple
```
TRAINING:
  Fed billions of text documents
  Books, websites, articles, code
  Learns patterns in language
  Learns facts, reasoning, grammar

PREDICTION:
  Given input text (prompt)
  Predicts most likely next words
  Generates human-like response

Think of it like:
  Autocomplete on your phone
  But extremely powerful
  Trained on ALL of internet
```

---

## LLM in code
```python
# ==========================================
# Using OpenAI GPT
# ==========================================
from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI(api_key="your-api-key")

# Simple chat
response = client.chat.completions.create(
    model="gpt-4",
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "system",
            "content": "You are a helpful assistant"
        },
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": "What is Python?"
        }
    ],
    temperature=0.7,    # creativity 0=strict 1=creative
    max_tokens=500      # max words in response
)

print(response.choices[0].message.content)

# ==========================================
# Chat with history
# ==========================================
messages = [
    {"role": "system",
     "content": "You are a SQL expert"}
]

def chat(user_input):
    messages.append({
        "role": "user",
        "content": user_input
    })

    response = client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4",
        messages=messages
    )

    reply = response.choices[0].message.content
    messages.append({
        "role": "assistant",
        "content": reply
    })
    return reply

# Use it
print(chat("What is a JOIN?"))
print(chat("Give me an example"))  # remembers context
```

---

## LLM Key terms
```
PROMPT      = input text you give to LLM
TOKEN       = piece of word (roughly 4 chars)
TEMPERATURE = creativity level
              0   = very strict, same answer
              1   = very creative, random
CONTEXT     = conversation history LLM remembers
EMBEDDING   = convert text to numbers (vectors)
FINE TUNING = train LLM more on specific data
RAG         = give LLM external docs to use
HALLUCINATION = LLM making up wrong facts
```

---

# Quick Revision

```
GENERATOR:
  Uses yield
  Returns one value at a time
  Saves memory
  Good for large data

DECORATOR:
  Wraps a function
  Adds extra behaviour
  Uses @decorator_name
  Does not change original function

ITERATOR:
  Goes through items one by one
  Has __iter__() and __next__()
  Raises StopIteration when done
  For loop uses iterator internally

RAG:
  Retrieval Augmented Generation
  Finds relevant docs first
  Gives docs to LLM as context
  LLM answers using those docs
  Solves knowledge cutoff problem

LLM:
  Large Language Model
  Trained on massive text data
  Understands and generates text
  Examples: GPT-4, Claude, Gemini
  Key input = PROMPT
```

3. **FastAPI with LLM integration**
